Section 1: Excellence 
 
5G-SOLUTIONS is a flagship 5G-PPP project supporting EC’s 5G policy by implementing the last phase of the 
5G cPPP roadmap. It aims to prove and validate that the 5G capabilities provide prominent industry verticals with 
ubiquitous access to a wide range of forward-looking services with orders of magnitude of improvement over 4G, 
thus bringing the 5G vision closer to realisation. This will be achieved through conducting advanced field trials 
of innovative use cases, directly involving end-users across five significant industry vertical domains: 
▪ Factories of the Future 
▪ Smart Energy 
▪ Smart Cities 
▪ Smart Ports 
▪ Media & Entertainment 
The field trials will be used to validate both the technological as well as the business aspects of 5G for increased 
resilience, coverage and continuity, higher resource efficiency with concurrent usage by multiple verticals, boosted 
capacity and greater reliability. 5G-SOLUTIONS is in direct support of 5G-PPP’s aspiration to see new connected 
digital markets, and it contributes to the EC’s broader industry digitisation and policy objectives in support of the 
Digital Single Market, maintaining Europe’s leadership position in mobile telecommunications.  
 
A key advantage of 5G-SOLUTIONS is that two of the consortium partners (TIM & TNOR) have key roles in 
the project (i.e. project coordination and technical management) and are also the coordinators of the 5G-EVE 
and 5G-VINNI ICT-17 projects, respectively. Both of these actors  are committed to upgrade and support their 
5G facilities during and after the completion of t heir ICT-17 projects until the completion of 5G -SOLUTIONS. 
This will enable the validation of the vertical use cases to the latest available 5G 3GPP releases by Q3 2021 until 
Q2 2022 to ensure that the latest features will be supported before actual widespread 5G deployments in Europe.  
 
In particular, 5G-SOLUTIONS will provide: 
(a) a wide set of innovative and heterogeneous use cases spanning across five industry vertical domains in a 
complementary way. The use case scenarios covered in 5G -SOLUTIONS have been carefully selected as they 
require advanced 5G capabilities and performance, and they are expected to have a high future 
commercialisation potential. These scenarios will be developed and demonstrated with expert end-user actors 
in Living Labs, validating their technological performance conforming to target 5G KPIs specified per use case, 
as well as their business potential and ethical and social acceptance. For their validation, high-density locations, 
very high data rates and volumes as well as concurrent multi-vertical usage of resources will be addressed.  
(b) novel technological enablers for facilitating the execution of the field trials in an automated  and adaptable 
way, enabling efficient end-user engagement, and specifically: 
(i) a unified cross-domain end-to-end service orchestration enabling multi-domain slicing and 5G service 
lifecycle automation . Th is will be achieved by leveraging an existing state-of-the-art orchestrator 
(NOKIA’s Cloudband Director), which will be enhanced with new open -standards plugins, catering for 
multi tenancy needs at scale, extending beyond ETSI MANO. It will also enable automatic real-time service 
provisioning and multi -domain management of resources across different 5G infrastructure vendor 
facilities, thus bringing service automation and adaptation to a level that allows Zero-Touch Configuration. 
(ii) an innovative smart KPI visualisation system , leveraging cognitive machine learning techniques, big -
data analytics and cloud -computing approaches for facilitating the fast-real-time analysis, presentation, 
benchmarking and performance validation of reference 5G network KPIs against pre-defined target values, 
including use case specific KPIs as developed with expert end-user actors.  
(iii) easy-to-use intent-based APIs for stimulating innovation and fostering the development, portability, 
provisioning of and interaction with new user-friendly innovative applications by SMEs and vertical 
specific systems, irrespective of the underlying 5G networks, whilst guaranteeing high performance, high 
quality and responsible innovation. 
 
Our consortium comprises 26 partners covering 9-member states and associated countries, driven by industry 
heavyweights from European telecom operators (T ELECOM ITALIA, TELENOR and FORTHNET), relevant 
large industry 5G adopters  (PROCTER & GAMBLE , ENEL, IBM, GLAN, IREN, YARA ), leading telecom 
vendors (ERICSSON, NOKIA), SMEs (A2T, APPART, CEL, EBOS, ILS, IRIS, IRT, LIVEU, NURO, OMES) 
and renowned research organisations/academia (CTTC, NTNU, PIIU, UOP, WIT) that have close collaboration 
with relevant users or user communities . The majority of the consortium members participated  and/or still 
participate in 24 out of the 43  5G-PPP projects and in several 5G-PPP Working Groups , thus enabling 5G -
SOLUTIONS to build on and build from a broad canvas of previously supported 5G-PPP initiatives. 
 
This proposal version was submitted by Frini LAZAROU on 14/11/2018 13:54:55 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.

1.1 Objectives  
 
1.1.1 5G-SOLUTIONS strategic vision and central innovation  
 
 
5G-SOLUTIONS will conduct innovative field trials implemented over the 5G ICT-17 end-to-end (E2E) facilities of 
5G-EVE in Turin and 5G-VINNI in Norway and Patra . The respective coordinators in each of these ICT -17 
projects have key roles in the 5G-SOLUTIONS consortium, supporting a collective effort which aims to see a 
fast-track path to support the  new 5G network features as per 3GPP and 5G -IA trials release roadmap1. Hence, the 
central goal of the project is to demonstrate and validate the following imperatives, through the execution of advanced 
field trials and by directly engaging key industrial end-user actors:  
(i) the technological performance conforming to 5G network KPI requirements, defined by 5G-PPP2, as well as 
by other standardisation associations (e.g. ETSI 3GPP3, ITU (IMT -2020)4) and industrial alliances (NGMN5, 
5G-ACIA6, etc.), here on in  referred collectively as standardisation bodies ; where target KPIs have been 
identified and included in the Living Labs , which will serve as the benchmarking for the technological 
validation. 
(ii) the business aspect  through viable and sustainable business model  development and ethical assessment 
approaches, tested across heterogeneous industrial sectors that require the performance characteristics of the 
underlying 5G infrastructure.  
 
In particular, 5G-SOLUTIONS will validate more than 140 5G network-specific technological KPIs corresponding 
to 20 innovative and compelling industry use cases, in near real-time at high throughput, fidelity and accuracy, thus 
significantly accelerating and encouraging the uptake of 5G across the EU community . In order to fully reali se a 
sustainable 5G ecosystem, both technical and economic aspects will be assessed, together with the understanding of 
the related legal, social and ethical issues . These will include a prominent focus on “vertical” requirements for 5G, 
in growing interaction with, engagement of, and input from key industry verticals, including those highlighted by the 
5G-PPP expert groups.  
 
In pursuit of this vision, 5G-SOLUTIONS has assembled a network of leading pan-European actors in both horizontal 
industries (telecom vendors , operators and service providers ) and from five representative vertical industries , as 
mentioned above, the majority of which are members of 5G-PPP. The vertical industries have been selected and 
prioritised based on 5G -PPP published recommendations7, on the basis that they are  expected to have the 
highest potential commercial impact and citizen/end-user benefits over 5G networks.  A comprehensive, 
heterogeneous and complementary set of future-oriented use cases and services from these verticals has been selected, 
and these are aligned with the 5G-PPP recommendations8 (See Section 1.3.4.1). 
 
1.1.2 Objectives and measurable outputs 
 
5G-SOLUTIONS Overall Project Objective: To conduct advanced field trials of innovative and thematically 
diverse digital services that require 5G capabilities and performance in the vertical domains of Factories of the 
Future, Smart Energy, Smart Cities, Smart Ports and Media & Entertainment, directly engaging with end-user 
actors, so as to validate the technological performance of 5G technology in successfully serving them, as well 
as validate the business models and potential of these use cases prior to commercial deployment. 
 
The aim of the project will be realised through six (6) key interdisciplinary objectives that are designed to address 
the specific technical and societal challenges regarding innovation, dissemination and sustainable business models. 
Measurable results, quantified targets and related WPs are specified for each objective as summarised in Table 1.1 
below.

1.2 Relation to the work programme  
5G-SOLUTIONS addresses the RIA action of ICT-19-2019: Advanced 5G validation trials across multiple vertical 
industries topic’s challenge to propel the European 5G vision closer to deployment by  conducting innovative use 
case trials in the field across five impactful vertical industries, so as to validate that key reference 5G-PPP KPIs can 
be met. The 5G-SOLUTIONS objectives match the Commission’s ambitions in the aforementioned topic and address 
the aspects listed in the call’s specific challenge and scope as shown in Table 1.2.

Table 1.2: Alignment to ICT-19-2019 
Specific Challenge from the call text How 5G-SOLUTIONS will address the Specific Challenge 
The challenge is to get the European 5G 
Vision of "5G empowering vertical 
industries" closer to deployment with 
innovative digital use cases involving 
cross industry partnerships. It requires 
technological and business validation of 
5G end to end connectivity and associated 
management from two perspectives:  i) 
within the set of requirements specific from 
one application domain; ii) across all sets 
of heterogeneous requirements stemming 
from concurrent usages of network 
resources by different vertical domains. 
5G-SOLUTIONS’s vision is in line with the European 5G Vision and in 
support of developing new connected digital markets and contributing to 
the wider policy objectives of industry digitisation of the Digital Single 
Market. 5G-SOLUTIONS will demonstrate and validate the feasibility of 
serving in field trials, new innovative use cases that are expected to have 
a high business potential (as outlined in Section 1.3.4.1) that demand 
beyond today’s network technological capabilities. Both the 
technological and the business aspects arising from such innovative use 
cases will be validated in the Living Labs involving cross industry end-
user actors and their performance will be measured and benchmarked 
through specific target KPIs. Section 1.3.4 (Methodology) addresses how 
these two perspectives (single and multi-concurrent usage of resources by 
verticals) and their respective sets of requirements will be managed. 
Scope from the call text How 5G-SOLUTIONS will address the Scope 
a) Trials of various scales, depending on 
the target technology, in view of 
demonstrating that performance 
conforming to 5G PPP KPIs requirements 
are met in the context of specific vertical 
use cases. Target 5G technologies and 
architectures should also support specific 
performance requirements stemming from 
the considered vertical use case. 
20 innovative use cases over 5 vertical domains will be conducted in the 
field, testing in total more than 1 40 quantitative technological KPIs 
against predefined target values, obtained from the industry and the 
various standardisation bodies (part of WP1 work). The execution of use 
case trials will undergo an iterative feedback-loop process of validating 
the KPI s against three 3GPP releases (R1 5 up to including R17 if 
available by summer 2021 ) over the duration of the project . Different 
target technologies (slicing, virtuali sation, MEC, etc. ) will be used  to 
serve each vertical domain. The specific performance requirements from 
such vertical domains are al ready known from the vertical stakeholders 
involved and are listed in the KPI tables separately for each use case, as 
listed in Table 1.6 in Section 1.3.4.1. 
In addition, 5G technology and 
architecture trials are also targeting 
concurrent usage of resource by 
multiple verticals, addressing the 3 
classes of ITU requirements (eMBB, 
mMTC, URLLC use cases). In practice, 
the 5G infrastructure (RAN, back/ 
fronthaul, Core) will be shared among 
multiple verticals and applications, 
each asking for independent service 
guarantees and very different service 
requirements. Operations of one 
application in one vertical domain 
should not affect the performance of 
other domains/ applications. The trials 
should hence demonstrate that 5G 
architecture and technologies (notably 
slicing and virtualisation) enabling 
multi domain management of resources, 
beyond the ETSI NFV Management and 
Orchestration (MANO) and with cross 
domain orchestration capabilities are in 
line with these concurrent performance 
requirements. 
Alongside human-centric applications it is acknowledged that 5G needs 
to support a wide variety of Internet of Things (IoT), Massive Machine 
Type Communications (mMTC) and Ultra -reliable Machine Type 
Communication (U-MTC). The highly demanding disruptive capabilities 
of 5G require orders of magnitude of improvement over the current  4G 
technology and infrastructure and in this sense, the Living Labs have been 
grouped and structured around four field trial c lusters: (i) Industry 4.0, 
encompassing the Factories of the Future domain  primarily addressing 
URLLC use cases (WP4), (ii) Smart urban environment, encompassing 
Smart Energy, Smart Cities and Smart Ports, primarily addressing mMTC 
use cases (WP5) , (iii) Enhanced User Experience, covering Media & 
Entertainment, primarily addressing eMBB use cases  (WP6), and (iv) 
Multi-vertical concurrent validation  (WP7) demonstrating and capturing 
evidence through the relevant performance KPIs that network slicing and 
virtualisation are in line with concurrent performance requirements  and 
also, that there is no interference between vertical use cases in the 
presence of concurrent usage of resources.  
In order to support network slice management, dynamic service lifecycle 
automation and to enable automatic and concurrent real-time 
orchestration across different ICT-17 facilities, a CDSO  (NOKIA’s 
Cloudband Director) will be leveraged, to bind all 5G-related services to 
be piloted and to dynamically control their flows , subsequently 
facilitating the demonstration and testing of such innovative use cases in 
parallel. 
Trials leverage results of 5G PPP 
phases 1 and 2 and go beyond the proof 
of concepts of phase 2. 
5G-SOLUTIONS’s baseline will be pivoted around the foundational 
work of 5G-PPP projects, and incorporates the knowledge and experience 
of the consortium partners who are collectively involved in 24 out of the 
43 5G-PPP projects, as follows: 
▪ Phase 1:  5G-ENSURE ( TIM), 5G-EXCHANGE ( TIM, TNOR), 
GOGNET ( NOKIA, IBM, WIT), FANTASTIC -5G ( CTTC, TIM),

and the upgrading of these facilities even beyond the end of their projects.  
It is expected that the first results from 5G -SOLUTIONS will be 
demonstrated in large 5G showcase events, both within and outside 
Europe, such as the MWC, Global 5G and EuCNC events in 2020-2022.
1.3 Concept and methodology 
 
1.3.1 Concept 
 
The 5G-SOLUTIONS conceptual approach is based on:  
1. Formulating a wide set of innovative, heterogeneous use cases spanning across f ive vertical industries in a 
complementary way. The use case scenarios identified and described in 5G-SOLUTIONS are expected to have 
a high future commercialisation potential and 5G relevance, will be developed based on state-of-the-art innovation 
methodologies, and will be demonstrated with expert end-user actors in Living Labs, validating their technological 
and business performance conforming to target 5G KPIs specified per use case, taking i nto consideration high-
density locations, very high data volumes and concurrent multi-vertical usage of resource. 
2. Providing the technological enablers for facilitating the execution of the field trials over specific ICT -17 5G 
facilities, and in particular: 
a. Engaging a unified Cross-Domain Service Orchestration (CDSO) based on automation enabling multi-
domain slicing and 5G service lifecycle automation . This will be achieved by leveraging an existing 
orchestrator ( NOKIA’s Cloudband Director), which will be enhanced with new open -standards plugins, 
catering for multi tenancy needs at scale . Subsequently, this CDSO will  enable the automatic real -time 
provisioning and multi -domain management of resources , concurrently across heterogeneous ICT -17 
testbeds from different vendors and operators, thus bringing service automation to a level that allows zero-
touch configuration. 
b. Introducing a novel value-added concept for the development of a  smart KPI visualisation system, for 
automating the analysis and presentation of the results  obtained from ICT-17 facilities and presenting 
them through an intuitive user-friendly dashboard in graphical form in near real time. This will be achieved 
by leveraging big-data analytics, cloud-computing and cognitive machine learning approaches to extend the 
current state of the art in network performance monitoring , in turn creating a compelling real time KPI 
visualisation benchmarking capability in the field. 
c. a set of open-standards easy-to-use intent-based APIs, including application APIs for facilitating the 
development, portability, provisioning of and interactions with new user-friendly applications and solutions 
that require 5G capabilities  by SMEs and/or vertical specific systems . These APIs will support the digital 
transformation underway in enterprises and industry verticals, enabling them to prosper in multi-dimensioned 
business ecosystems.  
 
This proposal version was submitted by Frini LAZAROU on 14/11/2018 13:54:55 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
G                Page  10  
This conceptual approach creates a unique partnership opportunity between the technological and business (vertical) 
partners to drive joint commercial exploitation of the associated technologies and 5G services towards telcos, telco 
vendors and SMEs for creating even more innovative applications leveraging 5G technology capabilities. 
 
 
1.3.1.1 5G-SOLUTIONS high-level architectural concept 
The 5G-SOLUTIONS technical approach is based on a modular architecture in which the various technological 
enablers are integrated together via open interfaces and APIs.  These enablers will facilitate the measurement and 
visualisation of 5G KPIs  of the vertical use cases in near real -time whilst exercised in the field, as well as 
benchmarking and access from multiple locations, whilst promoting openness for 3 rd party developers for the 
development of new innovative applications. The architecture features automatic resource scaling, by leveraging 
virtualisation technologies and cloud automation scripts to elastically scale according to workload demand. This 
provides the necessary flexibility for the system to adapt to new interfaces, data sources, GDPR compliant data 
processing, machine learning and represen tation requirements as may be required during the interfacing with the 
ICT-17 facilities.  
 
Figure 1.1: 5G-SOLUTIONS high-level architectural concept 
 
 
The high-level architectur al concept  of 5G-SOLUTIONS and its constituent elements are based on the 
aforementioned objectives and d escribed below. With reference to Figure 1. 1, t he technological enablers  to be 
implemented in 5G -SOLUTIONS and  the interconnect ed 5G infrastructure  (i.e. measurement portals, slicing,  
virtualisation, 5G testbed orchestration and infrastructures from ICT-17 5G-EVE Turin and 5G-VINNI Norway and 
Patra facilities) are indicated in blue and grey colours, respectively. 
 
 
Innovative vertical industries use cases validated in Living Labs  
The use cases , which will be validated in the Living Labs,  have been carefully selected to represent compelling 
services that are expected to have a high future business potential and economic impact in strategic vertical industry 
segments that require 5G performance capabilities and which cannot be offered with the current operational 
capabilities of 4G . As representative examples, s uch use cases  have been  identified in the vertical domains of 
Factories of the Future, Smart Energy, Smart Cities, Smart Ports, and Media & Entertainment, which will benefit 
the most from 5G network deployments.  
 
These vertical domains, whose use cases will be technology-wise and business -wise validated in Living Labs , 
will directly engage end -user actors (industrial and their customers) and have been carefully grouped in three 
complementary Clusters (i.e. Industry 4.0 , Smart Urban Environment  and Enhanced User Experience ) as 
depicted in Figure 1.2, mapp ed with the eMBB, URLLC and mMTC service classes and aligned with the 5G -PPP 
Vision10.  
 
The description of such heterogeneous use cases, including their business drivers, their technological perspective, 
their test objectives, requirements and pre-defined indicative sets of target KPI values to be validated, are described 
in detail in Section 1.3.4.1.

Figure 1.2: Smart mapping of 5G-SOLUTIONS Living Labs to ITU-T service classes 
 
 
Technological enablers 
 
Cross-Domain Service Orchestrator (CDSO) enabling dynamic service lifecycle automation 
 
NOKIA’s Cloudband Network Director (CBND) will serve as the  CDSO, which leverages E2E virtualised service 
functions and slicing, as per ETSI NFVI/NFV -MANO architecture11. It will be enhanced and expanded with new 
open-standards plugins to enable its integration with heterogeneous 5G facilities from ICT-17, in turn catering for 
multi-tenancy needs at scale and supporting network slicing imperatives. Examples to demonstrate such network 
slicing and virtualisation capabilities include: 
▪ Allocating certain network bandwidth per slice  – The CDSO can orchestrate this by triggering the needed 
configuration in the SDN controller, assuming that the latter supports bandwidth allocation per network. 
▪ VNF multi-tenancy – The CDSO can onboard and configure VNF's more than once as separate tenants.  
▪ Segregation – The CDSO can orchestrate the allocation of storage and Virtual Machine resources.  
 
Using the CDSO will make it simple to host, orchestrate, automate, and manage virtuali sed network functions and 
services, whilst benefiting from open -source innovation, making it a perfect candidate for facilitating the 
demonstration and testing of multiple and diverse service trials across the heterogeneous 5G ICT-17 facilities. In 
particular, the CBND automates network services delivery and operation in a distributed, multi-tenant, multi-vendor 
environment, while optimising and governing the usage of the infrastructure resources. CBND, an NFV orchestrator 
(NFVO) according to the ETSI-NFV reference architecture, is a ready-to-use software with two main roles:  
▪ as a resource orchestrator, it administers, monitors and optimizes NFV infrastructure resources and provides an 
aggregated view across geographically distributed NFVIs;  
▪ as a network service orchestrator, it onboards network services, which are a composition of VNFs, connected 
through forwarding graphs , which define service chains.  CBND automates network service events, including 
deployment, configuration, monitoring, updates, termination, and deletion. 
 
Multiple VNFs, including the forwarding graphs and service chains connecting them, are integral parts of the network 
service descriptors expressed using TOSCA, a standard domain -specific modeling language for network services. 
Together with an open source workflow engine and an open source policy engine, this ensures that  the CBND can 
manage any NFV service. The CBND can be easily extended and integrate d with many domain managers through 
plugins. Its northbound interface simplifi es integration with OSS systems.  Network Services in CBND include the 
VNF's that compose the network service and the network connections on these VNFs and PNFs (physical network 
functions) that may also play a role in the end to end service.

the Network Services flow.  
 
In addition to the above, 5G dynamic service lifecycle 
automation is required to be able to promote operational 
efficiency in network slicing and virtualisation. In this respect, 
5G-SOLUTIONS will explore zero-touch automation  
mechanisms in CDSO, so as to have all operational processes 
and tasks executed in an automated  way. Although such 
mechanisms are currently being explored by ETSI zero touch 
network and service management industry specifications 
group12, the actual implementation is in early stages and is 
being explored by the industrial partners. CBND’s highly 
flexible structure and ability to cope with any interface by 
adding the required plugin, brings service automation to a level 
that allows Zero Touch Configuration (ZTC). NOKIA is in 
advanced discussions with early adopters of ZTC to define and 
implement ZTC using CBND’s existing assets.  It is expected 
that automated lifecycle management will lead to OPEX reductions 13 and that service framework managem ent 
and admission control at the true user-service level may be necessary14. 
 
Smart KPI Visualisation system 
 
The use of a smart KPI visualisation system is considered as an important element to 5G-SOLUTIONS to automate 
and accelerate the analysis, benchmarking and presentation of the results from field trials, whilst being in the 
field, by using advanced cognitive big-data analytics and cloud-computing for rapid and automated processing of the 
vast amount of data obtained from the ICT-17 facilities. The smart KPI visualisation system will interact with the 
ICT-17 facilities’ measurement portals through relevant open-standards intent-based APIs. With reference to Figure 
1.1, the modular architecture of the smart KPI visualisation system consists of the following modules: 
 
Data collection and pseudo -anonymisation module: This is a core component of the system responsible for 
parallelised loading of the various data feeds collected from ICT-17 facilities. Data is ingested in native format until 
it is processed, pseudo-anonymised and encrypted with GDPR in mind, before storing it into the system’s database. 
Data is then prepared to be sent to the machine learning module for subsequent analysis.   
 
Real-time d ata processing and Machine Learni ng optimisation modules: These modules are responsible for the 
necessary data ingestion actions, data homogenisation  and calculations for presenting and benchmarking the KPI 
values in real-time, during field trials, against pre -defined target values  for each use case s cenario. Such values

include, amongst others, data aggregation both in time and space, forecasting, prediction and fault recognition 
services. This will be realised by fusing relevant assets from APPART’s telco analytics platform and deep-learning 
algorithms for graph data with IBM Watson’s cognitive platform and assets from previous 5G -PPP projects (e.g. 
machine learning components from COGNET) , so as to  (i) optimise the modules at system level due to t he fast 
processing speed of the parallelised execution of the use cases, (ii) automate the analysis and presentation of results 
and create a real-time KPI visualisation benchmarking capability in the field. 
 
Web-based graphical environment : Th is is based o n web technologies and is available to Living Lab end users 
through an intuitive web-based dashboard. Once the end-users are authenticated to have secured access to the cloud-
based KPI visualisation system, they gain access to a dashboard that provides them with a choice of the use cases to 
be executed together with the corresponding KPI parameters and a selection of the graphical reports to display the 
outputs and results. In each report, the data is also available in a tabular format.  
 
5G-SOLUTIONS consortium’s intention is to offer the smart KPI visualisation system as a free cloud-based 
service to other ICT-19 stakeholders in order to accelerate 5G vertical service KPI measurement results. 
 
Open-standards easy-to-use intent-based APIs 
 
Starting with use case driven requirements, and with reference to Figure 1.1, the following set of “friendly to 
application developers” 5G facilitator APIs, will be implemented in 5G-SOLUTIONS, in order to simplify access, 
stimulate innovation and foster the development of new innovative applications for 5G networks: 
▪ Cross-domain management and orchestration interfaces to enable  (i) the onboarding of different vertical 
applications into service provisioning and management (API A); (ii) the interfacing of the CDSO with the local 
orchestrators (API B) of the ICT-17 facilities. The functionality of APIs A and B will be incorporated into  
NOKIA’s CBND plugin implementation. CBND is a service orchestrator with an embedded Openstack/Mistral 
workflow engine and such workflow adjustments will be implemented in the plugin via Mistral. 
▪ Measurement portal intent-based APIs (API C) to enable the interfacing with the measurement platforms of 5G-
EVE and 5G-VINNI ICT-17 facilities, so as to collect the data to be processed for the KPI measurements. 
▪ Application intent-based APIs (API D) offering an application abstraction layer to simplify and enable easy 
interfacing of new applications to any 5G infrastructure provider at the interworking layer. By capturing 
business intent and activating it throughout the network, application developers can bridge the gap between what 
businesses need and what the 5G network can deliver. 
 
 
1.3.1.2 5G-SOLUTIONS roadmap alignment to standards and ICT-17 projects 
The 5G-SOLUTIONS roadmap follows the 3GPP , the IMT -2020 and the 5G -PPP implementation roadmaps 
according to the evolution and upgrades of the 5G-EVE and 5G -VINNI ICT-17 facilities as shown pictorially in 
Figure 1.5. This is achieved through 3 iterative and consequential testing cycles in Phase 3 (as defined in Table 1.4 
in Section 1.3.4) each lasting for 6 months , followed by an evaluation period of 2 months to ensure a smooth and 
aligned evolution of the vertical industry validations in the Living Labs. The 5G facility infrastructure provider 
partners, i.e. TIM with 5G -EVE Turin, TNOR with 5G -VINNI Norway and UOP with 5G -VINNI Patra are 
committed to support 5G-SOLUTIONS after the completion of the 5G -EVE and 5G-VINNI projects by July 2021. 
In this respect, additional budget and/or effort has been assigned to these partners (see Section 3.1.4 task 2.1 
and Section 3.4) in order to cater for the support and upgrades of their 5G facilities after the completion of their 
ICT-17 projects, so as to be able to support the validation of the vertical services  with the latest available features 
and releases, i.e. either a more mature version of 3GPP Rel.16 (e.g. Rel.16B) or even Rel. 17 provided that such as 
version will be available by Q3 2021.

1.3.2 Positioning of the project 
5G-SOLUTIONS envisages achieving up to Technology Readiness Level TRL 6 (‘technology demonstrated in an 
industrial environment’) as defined in Annex G of the work programme. The expected outcome will be functional 
field-trial demonstrators in the form of Living Labs, which will run in a near -operational environment (e.g. linking 
to isolated and production-congruent testbeds in order not to compromise operational systems for testing purposes).  
 
 
Figure 1.6: 5G-SOLUTIONS project positioning 
 
5G-SOLUTIONS will leverage, extend, integrate and advance  assets and technologies from completed 5G-PPP 
projects, as well as implement/advance commercial assets, raising their current TRL to 6-7 as listed in Table 1.3 in 
Section 1.3.3. In particular, and with reference to Figure 1.6 and Table 1.4: 
▪ The use cases in the Living Labs will start from TRL 3, evolve to TRL4-5 after testing Phase 3 Cycle 1, reaching 
TRL 6 after the completion of Phase 3 Cycle 3 by M34. 
▪ The smart KPI visualisation system components will start from TRL 4, evolve to TRL 5 after testing Phase 3 
Cycle 1, reaching TRL 6 after the completion of Phase 3 Cycle 3 by M34.  
▪ The methodologies to conduct the validation testing (i.e. for the definition of test reports format, parameters, test 
points, benchmarking of results as well as for the technological and business validation of 5G E2E connectivity 
and management across and within the verticals) will evolve from a starting TRL 3 to TRL 5 after testing Phase 
3 Cycle 1, reaching TRL 6 after the completion of Phase 3 Cycle 3 by M34.  
▪ Assets from 5G -PPP Phases 1 -3 (see Section 1.3 .3) leveraged and extended from TRL4/5 to 6/7 after testing 
Cycle 3 by M34. 
▪ NOKIA’s CBND, acting as the CDSO will start and remain at TRL 9 after the introduction of the plugins. 
 
Upon the completion of the project, the validated use cases can be offered to friendly end -user customers of the 
vertical partners, which will allow them to be proven in the market (as extension of WP8). The technical partners 
who will have a commercialisation benefit will support these customers in addressing potential technical difficulties, 
maintain and evolve the use cases TRL to 9, to enable them to be ready for commercialisation one year after the 
completion of the 5G-SOLUTIONS’ project.   
 
1.3.3 Linked research projects and related baseline assets 
5G-SOLUTIONS will build on the outputs and findings of completed 5G-PPP Phase 1 and Phase 2 projects (to be 
completed by mid -2019, coinciding with the commencement of ICT -19 projects) , ongoing Phase 3  projects 
(leveraging their ICT-17 facilities) as well as other relevant projects and commercial assets to seed its technology, 
including incorporating interdisciplinary knowledge and expertise. The project partners  are, in many cases , prior 
and/or current collaborators in 5G-PPP Phase 1, 2 & 3 projects. This ensures knowledge transfer of lessons learned, 
reuse of assets, testbeds and knowledge, and a strong working relationship together in support of a collaborative 
desire to see coherent industry impacts from the outputs of 5G-SOLUTIONS. Table 1.3 provides a summary of the 
most directly relevant and foundational contributions to 5G-SOLUTIONS from 5G-PPP Phase 1  & 2, ongoing 
Phase 3 projects (ICT-17 facilities) and commercial assets, and shows how project partners will leverage and use 
their assets, including current and target TRLs.

1.3.4 Methodology 
 
The 5G-SOLUTIONS project will be executed over three contiguous and sequentially aligned  phases of 
development, as listed in Table 1.4. This will allow the project to address the requirement analysis and methodologies 
and prepare in detail the vertical  use case scenarios  and associated target KPIs  (WP1), design and develop the 
necessary interfaces to interwo rk and obtain data from  ICT-17 facilities at orchestration , management and 
infrastructure levels (WP2), design, de velop and integrate the technological enablers, such as the smart KPI 
visualisation system and related APIs (WP3), before validating the use cases of the vertical industries in Living Labs 
(WP4-WP7). Commercialisation, IP management and international netwo rking will be covered in WP8, and 
dissemination, communication, trainings and community-building activities in WP9. 
 
Both the technological as well as the business perspectives will be covered in each use case. 5G connectivity and 
associated management and orchestration will be demonstrated within the set of KPI requirements that arise from 
specific vertical domains. In particular, the Factories of the Future vertical use cases to be demonstrated represent 
Industry 4.0, the Smart Energy, Smart Cities & Ports use cases represent the wide variety of Smart Urban 
Environment, and the Media & Entertainment use cases represent the Enhanced User Experience. Each vertical 
domain with its associated use cases requiring single usage of resources is elaborated in Section 1.3.4.1 and covered 
in relevant Living Labs  (LLs), managed in WP4 -WP6. An additional Multi Living Lab (WP7) will validate 5G 
performance capabilities from the perspective of multi-vertical concurrent usage of resources across all sets of 
heterogeneous KPI requirements so as to prove that no performance degradation occurs.

Figure 1.7: 5G-SOLUTIONS Living Labs – Integrated deployment and evaluation approach 
 
Continuous improvements will be achieved through feedback from LL operation, providing the basis for information 
sharing, operation, learning and improvement, as shown pictorially in Figure 1.7 .  The design and implementation 
activities in 5G-SOLUTIONS will be driven by the Co-operative Inquiry Methodology15. This is a type of research-
action methodology focused on performing research with users rather than on users. Co-operative Inquiry is based 
on the principals of focused workshops (i.e. Living Labs) that engage researchers and users (‘co-researchers’) in the 
development of a framework of inquiry and the exploration of their experiences and impressions of a research topic. 
5G-SOLUTIONS ultimately aims to validate and affirm reference industry 5G KPIs in innovative use cases, thus 
advancing the frontiers of 5G te chnology and bringing them one step closer to commercial deployment and 
exploitation. 
                                                 
15 J Heron, P Reason , The practice of co -operative inquiry: Research 'with' rather than 'on' people , Handbook of action research, 2006, 
http://www.peterreason.eu/Papers/Handbook_Co-operative_Inquiry.pdf

1.3.4.1 Implementation of the technological and business validation through Living Labs (LLs) 
The purpose of the Livi ng Labs is to validate the capabilities of both the 5G technology and the Use Cases 
(UCs) of the vertical industries so as to enable their commercial exploitation . During the projects’ conception 
phase, 5G-SOLUTIONS performed a stakeholder’s preliminary ris k-analysis for the LLs, an d generate d the 
descriptions for the identified and prioritised use cases. As such, verifying the key target 5G KPIs in the content of 
those industry segments is expected to motivate a very high business and economic impact (see section 2.1). During 
the pr oject, each LL will deploy a layered testing practice to drive development, involving significant industry 
representative tests, verifications and validations: (i) tests using specific use cases oriented for dedicated single or 
multi-concurrent vertical industries, and (ii) test, measurements, validation and demonstration of LLs in the field.  
 
Technological Use Case validation 
Table 1.5 provides an overview of the UC  field trials and their class type as per ITU M2083 , a mapping to the 
corresponding ICT-17 facilities locations in which each UC field trial will be conducted, as well as the ultimate end 
users of each UC. During proposal elaboration, a gap analysis has been conducted to identify any additional remote 
5G RAN (gNB and/or MEC) and other infrastructure relevant equipment required to be installed within each field 
trial location as an extension to 5G-VINNI facilities. Annex 2B in Section 5 provides a description of the services to 
be provided by 5G-VINNI. In particular, 5 new 5G RAN nodes will be installed in total as follows:  
▪ Two new 5G RAN nodes by UOP acting as 5G private networks to validate the stringent URLLC UC 
requirements within two factory locations, one in Ireland (GLAN) and the other in Brussels (PGBS); 
▪ One new 5G RAN node by UOP in IBM’s campus premises in Dublin-Ireland, whose traffic will be backhauled 
to 5G-VINNI Patra ICT-17 facility.  
▪ Two new 5G RAN nodes by TNOR in NTNU at Trondheim and YARA premises at Herøya Norway, whose 
traffic will be backhauled to 5G-VINNI Norway facility. Furthermore, the intention of TNOR is to enable 2 
additional 5G RAN nodes for free (i.e. at no additional cost to the project) in locations in Norway. 
Budget has been assigned to both TNOR and UOP  partners for the provision of such extension 5G RAN 
infrastructure, as outlined in the ‘other direct costs’ Table 3.4b in Section 3.4.

As one of the key targets of 5G-SOLUTIONS is the validation of KPIs for end users and services, the project will 
also combine QoS (Quality of Service) indicators, which are used for measuring the service quality perceived by 
users for the emerging communication services , as well as Quality of Expe rience (QoE22), which is a direct 
measurement of human perception of the quality of communication services,  and in particular media and 
entertainment, resulting to a more promising and beneficial approach for future communication systems performance 
evaluation. The Mean Opinion Score (MOS) is a widely used indicator for assessing the quality of multimedia signals 
based on end user subjective expectations on a scale from 1 -5 (1 bad to 5 excellent). MOS audiovisual tests will be 
carried out according to ITU-T P.911, ITU-T P913, ITU-T P.920 and ITU-T P.1301 specifications to provide results 
in terms of MOS-AVQS23.  
 
Business Use Case (UC) and business model validation 
Business UC validation is an early step in the process of  business portfolio development. Therefore, the business 
potential of each UC will be validated directly by the end -user actors to ensure that each of the use cases to b e 
trialed is well-positioned to respond to the needs of the market. 
 
The business UC validation will use the lean start-up methodology that centres around the main motivations of a 
business. The inputs of the business UC validation include apart from the business case itself, end-user feedback 
from the UC research in the field trials. The corresponding outputs are validations that will allow the business UCs 
to progress to the next step of creating a service pro duct portfolio. The 5G-SOLUTIONS commercialisation team 
will assess the business potential of each UC based on their needs as well as from questionnaires, surveys and 
focused group workshops directly engaging the customers of the vertical consortium partners. The aim would 
be to validate whether or not the UC will accomplish its goals within each business case , considering relevant 
business model variants. To achieve these goals, the following will be considered:  
- Research on the business potential of each UC: this will help increase the existing customer knowledge for the 
potential of the product. 
- Competitive analysis: review competing solutions, including preferred business model, within the marketplace 
to evaluate if this would affect the investments and returns included in the business case. 
- Internal market research validation : conduct reviews comparing previously performed market research with 
additional analysis against published sources and initial prospects for customer adoption. This effort will ensure 
that the service has a targeted market, that the market is searching and waiting for such as a service, and that the 
service can serve or alleviate existing problems that prospective customers currently experience. 
- Feedback arriving directly from end-users: failing to reach outside the organisation to prospective customers 
may cause misinformation to research findings. Therefore, to avoid over -generalisation of the customer base, 
feedback will be received from prospective customers of each vertical end-user organisation participating in the 
LLs throu gh focused surveys and questionnaires. Such feedback will be analysed to provide key customer 
insights and help improve the service offering making it appealing to the market.   
 
An indicative set of  metric parameters considered for the business validation  of each UC are listed in Table 1. 7a. 
These metrics will be interrogated (as listed in Table 1.7b) and quantified as part of the business validation process 
with the end-users. The proposed spectrum of metric parameters embraces all the use cases.

Metric parameter  
B1: Personnel cost 
People are the biggest cost in most enterprises, therefore, with these services can we do more 
with same resources ? can we do more with less resources ? are more expensive resources 
required? which are more specialised and hard to find? 
B2: Overhead cost How can the new service reduce non -people costs? energy costs? green:  reduce CO2? less 
infrastructure, less buildings, less transport?

How does 5G accelerate the provision of new innovative services to customers / citizens and 
which of them are critical for business (compe titive differentiation) and for public services 
(deliver return-on-taxes to citizens)? 
B4: Safety How does 5G improve confidence in technology acceleration  with respect to  safety of the 
people, safety of the processes, safety of the ecosystem? 
B5: Data privacy How does 5G improve confidence in protection of the individual in the digital age of their 
data and their identify? 
B6: Accessibility How does 5G help a wider community to share in the benefits of an enhanced digital age: 
more accessible in cost? types of location? device types? disabilities?

validated, as required by the ICT-19-2019 call, and measured as stated in the following table: 
▪ BA1: Leverage the effect of EU R&I funding in terms of private investment in R&D for 5G systems in the order 
of 5-10 times in turn evidencing a 5-10-fold increase in private funding relative to EU funding; 
▪ BA2: Target SME participation under this initiative commensurate with an allocation of 20% of the total public 
funding in turn evidencing a minimum of 20% of public funding dedicated to the SME sector; 
▪ BA3: Reach a global market share for 5G equipment & services delivered by European headquartered ICT 
companies at, or above, the reported 2011 level of 43% global market share in communication infrastructure.

worldwide R&D investment in the ICT sector, and subsequently discerning the proportion of the R&D ICT 
expenditure related to 5G. The substantiation of  this value will benefit from a poll/questionnaire amongst 
industry stakeholders, such as 5G network vendors, mobile network operators, and UE manufacturers. 
Investment in 5G, with respect to the total telecom R&D budget, will gradually increase with time as 5G

Living Lab 1: Factories of the Future (FoF) 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
Introduction 
Factory digitisation will be a pivotal goal for 2020 and Industry 4.0 initiatives have been driving the emergence of 
new manufacturing scenarios based on increased sensing, as well as the collaborative functions of a new generation 
of robots or ‘cobots’ , with the ultimate goal of increasing the efficiency of factory production lines. We are also 
seeing an evolution towards data-driven ecosystems by exploiting product lifecycle data from connected goods , 
whereby diverse data collection scenarios will be supported by energy eﬃcient communication schemes and scalable 
data analytics. Regarding Augmented Reality (AR), we are seeing the rise of new remote services that facilitate 
eﬀective knowledge sharing in the factory. It is envisaged that future communication solutions can ensure seamless, 
real-time and secure connectivity between different globally distributed 
production sites and new actors in the value chain (e.g. suppliers, 
logistics). Innovative strategies and their design principles are gaining 
increasing acceptance and will inﬂuence on present and future 5G 
requirements25.  
The main use cases identiﬁed in the context of the Factor ies of the 
Future25 LL are as follows:  
Use Case 1.1: Time-critical process optimisation inside digital factories  
Use Case 1.2: Non-time-critical communication inside factories  
Use Case 1.3: Remotely controlling digital factories 
Use Case 1.4: Connected goods 
Use Case 1.5: Rapid deployment, auto/re-configuration and testing of 
new robots 
 
Context – Business Situation & Drivers 
The manufacturing sector in the EU account s for 2 million companies that employ 33 million people. The sector 
contributes 15% of the EU’s GDP26, and given the manufacturing sector’s great potential for growth and job creation, 
the EU has set itself the target of increasing th is contribution to GDP to 20% by 2020 25. However, in contrast with 
this ambition, global transitions, such as declining energy prices, diminishing re sources, new competition from 
emerging markets and an aging workforce, have diminished its growth and have seen the share of industry in GDP 
terms decline in recent years27. In response to this decline, rejuvenation of the existing manufacturing sector is a key 
European agenda for encouraging industrial growth in an effective, efficient, and sustainable manner 27. Indeed, the 
4th Industrial Revolution has started, which is fuelled by cyber-physical-systems and IoT technology, to realize highly 
efficient, connected and flexible Factories of the Future (FoF).   
 
Solution – Technology Perspective 
To enable the execution of representa tive FoF use cases, t he approach will involve both horizontal and vertical 
slicing. On the one hand,  horizontal slicing involves computational off-loading, e.g. multi-access edge computing, 
and addresses the diverse network capacity  and latency requirements e.g. 10,000x capacity at the edge with <1ms 
latencies (“factory floor”), compared to core network, due to the huge numbers of sensors, other networked devices 
and time-critical applications. It requires over-the-air resource sharing across network nodes, and as such the 5G air 
interface will be an appropriate enabler. As indicated in Table 1.5, portable 5G RAN nodes will be installed inside 
each of the factory premises of GLAN (Ireland) and PBGS (Brussels), as well as in NTNU (Norway), the first two 
acting as stand-alone private 5G networks for validating the relevant field trials requiring URLLC class service type. 
                                                 
25 White Paper: 5G and the Factories of the Future. Available from: https://5g-ppp.eu/wp-content/uploads/2014/02/5G-PPP-White-Paper-on-
Factories-of-the-Future-Vertical-Sector.pdf  
26https://ec.europa.eu/commission/commissioners/2014-2019/oettinger/announcements/speech-hannover-messe-europes-future-digital_en   
27 Future of Manufacturing in Europe. Frost and Sullivan, 2016.  
This proposal version was submitted by Frini LAZAROU on 14/11/2018 13:54:55 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
G                Page  23  
This will ensure that the results obtained during the validation of this use case will be as realistic as possible and that 
the URLLC requirements can be met. For vertical slicing, on the other hand, which entails separate virtual networks 
within the 5G network, technologies at the air interface, RAN and NGC levels will be setup and configured. At the 
RAN level (i.e. at base s tation) access point and depending on factors such as traffic type, traffic load and QoS 
requirement, the RAN architecture of each of the slices can be dynamically configured. The  5G node will allocate 
radio resources for the slice and enable all radio and network functions associated with the slice.  
 
Main Participants and their role:  
Part Role  
IRIS 
LL leader. Provide support to all factory sites in the UCs in terms of organisation, planning, and set up of the 
core communication network platforms at each site for optimising the existing communication network as 
appropriate, and building the interfaces between transceivers and sensors for wireless communication.  IRIS 
will also leverage its expertise in Process Analytical Technology solutio ns for real-time process monitoring 
and control within UC1.1 in PBGS, whereby its Hyper-Spectral Imaging (HSI) system will be integrated to a 
Global Control System Platform (PATBox) for processing the data obtained from the analysers, and using the 
5G nodes as the communication interface with the cloud. Cloud-based supercomputing will be used to enable 
updated machine learning algorithms to be used for improving the current capabilities, which are 
predominantly based on chemometric tools.  
GLAN 
Participation in UC1.1, based on the maintenance function within  GLAN in their dairy and nutritional 
ingredients processing factory plant. Typically, key assets and equipment have been maintained using 
scheduled and usage-based maintenance strategies. Predictive maintenance uses key data feeds and agents to 
constantly monitor condition feeds and recognise patterns leading to equipment failure allowing for timely 
and effective intervention. The key benefit is that assets can be sweated for longer and avoid u nplanned 
outages. GLAN will also participate in UC1.3, whereby an AR module will be developed by  OMES, which 
displays a GLAN powder plant with current status. The AR module will use Microsoft HoloLens and display 
plant operations using a 5G gateway data collection UE. 
NTNU 
YARA In collaboration with TNOR, the NTNU Manulab Robotics and Industry 4.0 laboratories will be equipped 
with a 5G infrastructure for ultra -low latency closed -loop control of moving and stationary robots. In 
particular, NTNU will be involved in UC1.1, UC1.2, UC1.3 and primarily in UC1.5, which will monitor new 
robots in a factory for remote operation by real-time audio/video-feeds requiring high data rates. YARA will 
support NTNU in the execution of the field trials in UC1.5. 
PBGS 
PBGS will participate in UC1.1, to enable full automation of a digital plant, leveraging advanced technology, 
such as visual recognition of quality control on, for instance, bottles on a line, and hyperspectral imaging of 
complex products and vision systems on advanced robotics. The data needs to be collected and optimi sed 
across plants. For UC1.2, in view of the large number of products and complex supply chains fro m the 
production plants to distribution and warehousing, there is a high need for tracking of materials (e.g. spare 
parts) and tracking of product stocks. While the tracking of product is currently done with low -bandwidth 
devices, and since the Distribution Centres (DCs) of the future depend fully on fast wireless data transfer, 5G 
opens up new opportunities to expand the required scope with UHD+ cameras and HSI technology, to track 
stock in large DCs, requiring large data transfer without latency, which ca n be piloted at  PBGS’s facilities. 
For UC1.3 related to next generation plant planning/scheduling to greatly increase plant productivity by better 
utilisation of the assets, 5G will enable  PBGS to bring this to the next level across sites and with new 
algorithms for dynamic, reactive scheduling. For UC1.4 home services will be validated for laundry that 
require connected machines to continuously track and anticipate consumer laundry (imaging & spectral data). 
OMES 
For UC1.1, OMES with its client GLAN will enhance the operation of their Smart Manufacturing Execution

plant) – will be used for 5G validation to ensure efficiency, speed, capacity, latency, reliability, accuracy and 
timeliness in data input. Efficiency, Intelligence and Data Analysis within the FoF is dependent on the future-
proofing of communications to this Hub via 5G. For UC1.3, OMES will develop an AR module of a GLAN 
powder plant to validate key KPIs through the testing of multiple business scenarios within the plant.

Use Case (UC) 1.1: Time-critical process optimisation inside digital factories 
The drive for instant optimisation to increase production line efficiency is seeing increased real-time monitoring of 
the performance of sub-components, the measured quality variations of produced goods, the interactions by operators 
and changing factors in the environment. This involves the use of sensors, some of which  communicate at low bit 
This proposal version was submitted by Frini LAZAROU on 14/11/2018 13:54:55 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
G                Page  24  
rates but with ultra-low latency and ultra-high reliability, and also vision-controlled robot arms or mobile robots that 
can require reliable high-bandwidth communication. Beyond machine-type communications, we are also seeing the 
emergence of new scenarios for time-critical communication incorporating the collaborative functions offered by a 
new generation of robots, the introduction of wearables on the shop floor, and augmented reality. More and more 
devices are becoming wireless and mobile, thereby requiring the transfer of “heavy” data (3D models, large historic 
data sets, etc.) for fast intervention, maintenance or assembly tasks. Significant volumes of information need to be 
shared and utilised for on-the-spot collaborative decision making. Robots and operators are collaborating in real-
time, with the robot adapting to operators’ faculties when interacting with the operator’s wearables, the surrounding 
sensors and the machine control systems. Greater levels of automation will be facilitated with u ncaged robots, 
augmenting the efficiency of operator tasks, increasing production yield, quality output and overall operator safety. 
While ISO 10218 standard already defines robotic collaborative operation, 5G can play a differentiating role  in the 
case of ultra-fast and ultra-reliable access to moving objects. Adapt instantaneously variable capacity and mobility 
needs to changing environments , will require flexible convergent and seamless connectivity offer across different 
radio access technologies22.

Use Case 1.2: Non-time-critical communication inside factories 
While in UC1.1 the involved machines and robots are part of closed time critical control loops, UC1.2 relates to less 
time-critical communications that involve the locali sation of assets and goods in on -site production and logistic 
processes, non-time critical quality control, or data capturing for later usage in virtual design contexts. Similarly, the 
communication with operators on the shop floor may not always require ultra -low latencies, given that human 
response times are much higher compared to machine -level respon se times. Concerning logistics, accurate 
localisation of forklifts, vessels, trolleys, auto guided vehicles etc., can significantly decrease error rates in picking 
and packaging, by validating the source and destinations of picked goods or parts in real ti me with intelligent 
warehouse management systems (WMS). Successful capture of sensor data on the shop floor is another use case that 
requires less time critical communication inside the factory, buy which is crucial for fuelling further digitisation of 
the factory, and for facilitate virtualised design processes that integrate simulator data with real -life, data sensed 
during production. The successful combination of these data, will contribute to minimising product lead times and to 
the design of superior products that can be produced with a minimal number of defects. Guaranteeing the full 
availability and reliability of future automated industry applications will be reliant on indoor coverage enabling the 
connectivity of complete locations (e.g. including all floors, all rooms, etc.)25.

Use Case 1.3: Remotely controlling digital factories 
While in both UC1.1 and UC1.2, local on-site communication is assumed within the plant, in the case of UC3.3, the 
public wireless access network also plays a role in the E2E communication between remote workers and the factory. 
The simplest setup of this use case involves remote control applications running on tablets or smart phones  for 
example. However, in view of the trend of new AR devices, it is likely that new remote services may arise that 
facilitate the creation of virtual back office teams. Such remote teams may use the data coming from smart devices 
This proposal version was submitted by Frini LAZAROU on 14/11/2018 13:54:55 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
G                Page  25  
for preventive analytics and easy access to work instructions, whereby, e.g. they would be able to view the camera 
or iPad/Google Glass of a local worker. Additionally, the application of AR in the plant will facilitate:  
▪ Augmented-reality support in production and assembly: Precisely positioned picture-in picture fade-ins, showing 
the operator the next step and helping to avoid misplacement and unnecessary scrap.  
▪ Augmented-reality support in maintena nce and repair : Repair machines without training due to augmented 
information and operational guidance.  
Cross-functional communication, effective knowledge sharing and collaborative design platforms will be facilitated 
by solutions for communities of practice . In this use case family, there is a less stringent need for low -latency. 
Interaction times up to seconds are acceptable for remote servicing machines. However, high availability is key for 
allowing (emergency) maintenance actions to occur immediately. Bandwidth is important for video-controlled 
maintenance, with real -time augmented content mixed into the video signal. Moreover, latency is particularly 
important for real-time, remote motion control of local robots. Edge computing wit hin the network is  required for 
fulfilling the low latency requirements. Security threats are introduced due to the opening up of the machines to allow 
remote reconfiguration. As such, the cyber-representation of a factory or supply chain needs to be prote cted, with 
mission-critical actions being shielded from non-authorised parties.

Use Case 1.4: Connected goods  
The consolidation of physical goods will be of strategic importance to the manufacturing industry. Product lifecycle 
data, combined with personalised usage and context data is extensive required and exploited by business models in 
the manufacturing industry. Reinforcing this product-service relationship will become increasingly important in the 
production of connected goods, and will see manufacturing plants evolve to a data -driven eco-system. Ultimately 
this will augment production-related data with usage-related data collected during their lifetime. To boost such data 
collection scenarios, reliable and cost-effective communication is also required. Smart data filtering and scalable data 
analytics will fuel a new way of data -driven, computer-aided design. Device autonomy is a key requirement  for 
realising the true potential of connected goods, and as such, n ew low-power, low-cost, long-range communication 
technologies need to be integrated within the factory communication network28.

Use Case 1.5: Rapid deployment, auto/re-configuration and testing of new robots 
While in UC1.1, UC1.2 and UC1.3 the RAN properties of the 5G communication are being tested and evaluated in 
various settings and with different requirements, UC1.5 focuses on the possibilities of utilising the core 
functionalities of 5G in order to achieve one major feature of the Industry 4.0 in the FoF, such as significantly lower 
expenses and reduced time in order to either commission or reconfigure of robot ised manufacturing. In UC1.5 the 
goal is to demonstrate how to achieve deployment of new robots into existing plants through automatic on-boarding 
of industry requirements. This encompasses auto-configuration of (mobile) robots and the corresponding 5G service 
configuration needed for interconnection / interworking across solutions from different vendors. The possible vendor 
lock-in caused by incompatibilities, use of different standards and different use of existing standards as well as the 
complexity resulting in extensive commissioning time and excessive man hours needed for the integration, are often 
seen as major obstacles for modern automation in various industries.

Living Lab 2: Smart Energy  
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
Introduction29 
Over the last two decades, the power supply industry has been the subject of a deep 
transformation. On one hand, the unbundling, namely the process of splitting vertically 
integrated utilities into a number of generation, transmission, distribution and energy retailing 
companies has been the basis for the introduction of competitive electricity markets; on the 
other hand, the continuing increase in renewable energy sources (RES), the introduction of the 
active demand  concept, the deployment of energy storag e systems  (ESSs) and finally the 
expected transition from fossil fuels based to plugin electric vehicles (PEV), represent key 
challenges and opportunities, requiring a deep renovation in power systems operation. The transition from traditional 
electricity grids to smart grids  is driven by the large -scale deployment of telecommunications infrastructures, 
supporting innovative real time control systems, aimed at coordinating the action of traditionally uncoordinated 
equipment and grid players towards a set of  common objectives. In the light of the above, this LL is aimed at 
providing evidence about the potential benefits from large-scale adoption of 5G technology in the smart grid sector; 
a preliminary evaluation of expected 5G KPIs reveals that the added valu e brought by the new generation of 
communication technology lies in its level of reliability, low latency and wide coverage.  
This LL will target three use cases referring to the broad area of Demand Side Management (DSM). DSM refers to 
the changes in electricity use by consumers from their normal consumption patterns in response to incentive payments 
designed to induce lower electricity use at times of high wholesale market prices or when system reliability is 
jeopardised. In a broader sense, DSM also embeds the topic of overload avoidance and optimal self-consumption, in 
those scenarios where the peak power affects the energy bill, and local RES have an impact on the net power 
withdrawn from the grid.  
 
Context – Business Situation & Drivers30  
The renovation of electricity grids is driven both by political, regulatory and technological aspects. On one hand, 
there is the political will to reduce the carbon footprint on a global scale, and on the other, the technological progress 
in the area of RES, PEVs and ESSs. This results in the continuous update of the regulation by national electricity 
authorities, which poses new stringent requirements and opens the way to new use cases, where communication 
technology represents a key enab ler.  In the area of DSM, many business opportunities can be identified. Active 
consumers may take advantage of the time varying charging nature of electricity price and be interested in an optimal 
usage of local energy sources; t his class of consumers, in  an aggregated form, has been recently accepted by the 
regulation for participating in  the Dispatching Markets, where the operator of the electricity transmission network 
buys the balancing power needed to operate the network. Consequently, players like retailers, aggregators, service 
providers, telco operators and start -ups from the green energy economy play a fundamental role for enabling 
consumers to play the foreseen active role, and all of them become key elements of the new electricity value chain.

The following use cases require 5G network capabilities, such as high reliability and low latencies (<10ms). 
 
Use Case 2.1: Industrial Demand Side Management 
This use case deals with DSM at the level of business consumers (large, medium or small enterprises). The focus is 
on the optimal scheduling of industrial loads during normal plant operation, the computation and actuation of 
flexibilities offered on the Dispatching Market and the control actions needed to keep the peak power consumption 
limited. The first aspect covered by this use case is the planning and aggregation of loads. A distributed monitoring 
and load shifting control system (based on sensors, met ers and in -cloud data analytics  and control tools), will be 
setup to perform a real-time schedule of loads and assess the energy behaviour of each activity/production, with the 
aim of evaluating possible actions of power reduction to be offered on the Dispatching Markets; this action may be 
performed by the customer as a single actor of the market, if the power reduction constraints set by the Regulator are 
met, or in aggregated form with other prosumers (by means of an Aggregator). 5G technology is expected to play an 
important role, as both data communication from the field to the cloud and communications among the Aggregator 
and involved customers must be reliable, fast and with minimal delay ( latency). The second aspect concerns the 
peak power consumption, which represents one of the critical paramete rs for this class of customer segment. The 
simultaneous use of electrical devices may involve peak loads that can result in the tripping of commercial meter s 
due to overload detection.  
 
With the introduction of new tariff schemes accounting for the peak power consumption in addition to the energy 
component (e.g. maximum demand) and the presence of fluctuating Renewable Energy Sources (RES), the problem 
of keeping the peak power limited is quite important: it appears crucial to rely on a technological solution to promptly 
switch off the loads responsible for the peak/overload and, therefore, to reschedule the load in a more efficient way. 
5G technology can play a crucial role: a post-commercial meter will be used to detect the power peak/overload and 
generate a n alert , which will be transferred to a pre-selected set of control devices  that will reduce the power 
consumption and trigger the computation of a new load schedule as a recovery action. Hence, the objective of this 
use case is to demonstrate in the field that 5G technology can be effectively used for offering new grid services and 
drastically reduce the tolerance implemented on the meters before disconnection, without having an impact  on the 
customer perception and quality of service.  To enable the testing and validation of this use case a number of 
distributed indoor sensors (post fiscal meters) , Energy Management Systems and Aggregator Management system 
will be used (included in IREN’s budget under “other direct costs”).

Use Case 2.2: Electrical Vehicle Smart Charging  
Smart charging is a form of DSM in which the choice of the charging station used for recharging a PEV and the 
power absorbed during the process are under the control of a charging point operator, according to a set of grid 
boundary conditions and drivers’ charging preferences. Also, the driver experience may involve a variety of 
interactions between the driver and the charging infrastructure through apps and the charging station dashboard, 
depending on the charging point operational policies and business models. As indicated in Figures 1.8 and 1.9, EVs 
penetration in the markets is rising and expected to grow even further in the coming years; by 2040, 54% of new car 
This proposal version was submitted by Frini LAZAROU on 14/11/2018 13:54:55 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
G                Page  28  
sales and 33% of the global car fleet will be electric31. This new paradigm in mobility implies a strong interaction of 
EVs and electricity distribution grids, posing new challenges and opportunities in the way the next generation 
networks will be operated. In this regard, the 5G network can be used for allowing a reliable real time scheduling of 
charging sessions and provide a fast reschedule in case of an overload, in case a contractual threshold is overcome 
due to an excessive number of simultaneous charging sessions, or in case the electric power generated from 
renewables suddenly falls short of the predictions.  
 
 
To enable the testing and validation of this use case, a set of public charging points equipped with 5G communication 
devices will be used, under the control of a charging platform , enabling innovative services interconnecting the e -
mobility stakeholders (integration with H2020 NEMO and FP7 MOBINCITY projects is envisaged in different test 
sites). This equipment is included in the budget of ENEL and IREN under “other direct costs”.

Use Case 2.3: Electricity network frequency stability  
This use case deals with the involvement of active demand in the provisioning of the electricity services needed to 
maintain the electricity network frequency at its rated value (e.g. 50 Hz in Europe). Basically, the network frequency 
depends on the difference between the demand and supply, and remains con stant so long as this difference is zero. 
Any imbalance between the demand and supply sides results in a deviation from the nominal network frequency, 
which is typically resolved by the Transmission System Operator (TSO) by asking the generators to provide or release 
the power needed to clear the imbalance (balancing service). The Dispatching Market, namely the market where the 
TSO buys this service from legacy generators, has been recently opened to active demand, and Plugin Electric 
Vehicles (PEVs) aggregates appears the most promising form of active demand to this purpose. 
 
Since network frequency instability can occur within  seconds or less, a fundamental requirement to enable PEVs 
smart charging to frequency regulation functions is the availability of highly reliable and low latency communications 
allowing a fast and coordinated action of distributed PEVs aggregates. Keeping in mind that the current smart meters 
installed in the charging stations take measurements every minute, and that the measurements do not include network 
frequency, in the absence of a highly performing communication infrastructure, each charging station should react 
alone and be equipped with a new, potentially expensive, frequency meter.  Hence, t he deployment of 5G 
communications in charging stations could dramatically decrease the number of frequency meters needed to provide 
the balancing service, and consequently the related total cost of ownership . The smart charging system involved in 
use case 2.2 can be extended to create the superposition of two control signals working on different time scales: a

at https://data.bloomberglp.com/bnef/sites/14/2017/07/BNEF_EVO_2017_ExecutiveSummary.pdf

slow control signal, computed according to the requirements of use case 2.2 under the assumption of nominal network 
frequency, and a fast control signal, computed by a new controller installed in the charging stations, driven via 5G 
by the real time measurements of network frequency. 
 
To enable the testing and validation of this use case, a set of 5-10 public charging stations equipped with 5G modems 
will be used. One of the charging stations will be enabled to take real time measurements of network frequency and 
forward them to the other charging stations involved in the provisioning of the balancing service. The charging 
stations will be equipped with local controllers driven by the frequency measurements received by the master.

Living Lab 3: Smart Cities & Ports  
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
Introduction 
In Europe, cities account for 75% of the population consuming 80% of the EU’s energy 32. On 
one hand, this influx of people can create new opportunities for cities but on the other  hand it 
poses major economic, environmental, social and safety challenges as well, 
since many cities were built on infrastructure designed for smaller, less 
active population33. Therefore, the need for innovative solutions facing the 
rising demands and different challenges, is growing. The vision of a smart 
city “incorporates the six “s” , i.e.  a shared, secure and scalable 
infrastructure that enables human possibilities in a manner that is smart, safe and sustainable.  
This vision is achieved by a smart network connecting sensors, machines and citizens to cloud-
based internet of things (IoT) applications”34. 
Likewise, ports are complex systems involving a wide number of stakeholders, such as port operators, authorities 
and shipping companies. As global trade is expanding, ship sizes and cargo volumes are increasing, placing additional 
pressure on ship berths and yards. Ports are therefore becoming increasingly interested in smart solutions to help 
optimise and improve their operational efficiency and reduce logistics costs.  
 
Context – Business Situation & Drivers 
Cities and ports constitute complex ecosystems comprising a range of stakeholders, developing and deploying new 
services, that passes through technological, social, organisational, and business domains. Understanding the rollout 
of technologies and their relative importance in the ecosystem requires understanding the business drivers that affect 
their deployment and uptake, and an overview of the smart city marketplace35. 
 
Solution – Technology Perspective 
Through the u se of digital and telecommunications technologies traditional networks and services become more 
efficient for the inhabitants, business’ and ports benefit36. It is estimated that 50 billion devices will be connected to 
mobile networks by 2020, while a large proportion of communications will occur between machines and not humans.

5G RAN node. This includes the smart port and logistics to the plant cargo loading area, which will be 
operated in a mixed traffic environment. 
 
The goal is not only to conduct field trials in isolation but also include their capabilities as part of wider offerings to 
the “Smart City co -creation” community. UC3.1 and UC3.2 will be validated during the first two testing cycles, 
whereas UC 3.3 “Smart City co-creation” will be trialled in testing cycles 2 and 3 (see Figure 1.5 and Table 1.4). 
 
Use Case 3.1: Intelligent street lighting  
The primary objective is t o accelerate the use of intelligent lighting in smart cities and increase the environmental, 
financial, safety and security benefits that societies can have. With intelligent street lighting over 60% of power can 
be saved44, and light pollution can be significantly decreased 44. By dynamically adjusting street lighting based on 
traffic conditions (pedestrians or vehicular) both security as well as safety of the inhabitants can be improved . In 
addition, road safety is maximised, whereas the operational costs are minimised37.
