Use Case 3.2: Smart parking 
The primary objective is to allow drivers to look for inter-city parking spaces so as to easily spot the most convenient 
and available parking places. Smart parking solutions aim to reduce congestion, emissions and improve traffic safety 
allowing at the same time higher quality of li fe for the residents. A smart parking system can benefit not only the 
drivers and the operators but the city councils as well. Smart parking saves time and costs for the drivers, whereas 
municipalities are able to provide a more efficient traffic guidance increasing their profits while complying with 
relevant emissions requirements38.

Use Case 3.4: Smart buildings – Smart Campus 
Currently there is a huge type of IoT sensors installed across the IBM Technology Campus including CO2, brightness, 
room temperature sensors, etc. A significant percentage of the IoT data collected from the sensors above is stored in 
a central data warehouse on campus by means of a central Business Management System (BMS) Data Integrator, 
which collects data from individual BMS systems that are respon sible for power, on campus weather stations and 
lighting etc. The purpose of UC3.4 is to enable the continued IoT evolution of the IBM technology campus from a 
set of individual smart buildings into to a smart IoT environment that provides a safer and more efficiently managed 
working environment for all IBM staff, customers and visitors and also to use the knowledge gained to help drive 
advancements in cognitive IoT to a global scale by reflecting it in IBM products and services. Currently , there are 
thousands of IoT sensors of varying types in operation in the IBM campus, reporting back to a multitude of safety 
and workplace management systems. There are varying standards and sophistication of IoT endpoints and varied 
proprietary software management systems  to manage their output. The endpoints range from state-of-the-art fire 
detection sensors right down to inexpensive heat sensors placed in computer racks in internal lab rooms by operations 
staff. Given the IBM campus is a series of automated and/or smart buildings, significant benefits are envisioned if a 
technological solution were designed and deployed that could help transition the IBM buildings into a smart campus.

Use Case 3.5: Autonomous assets and logistics for smart port 
The purp ose of UC 3.5 is to  demonstrate the capabilities of 5G technology to support real -time operation and 
integration support for autonomous assets in a logistics hub at Herøya, Porsgrunn, Norway. The smart port will be a 
hub, where autonomous assets are received and served with logistics support. The autonomous test site includes the 
smart port as well as the logistics solution to the plant cargo loading area, which will be operated in a mixed traffic 
environment. The test site will have a dedicated autonomous vessel (Birkeland) with autonomous land -based cargo 
handling assets. This UC will explore the enhanced service offering enabled by 5G technology.

Use Case 3.6: Port safety - Monitor & detect irregular sounds 
Irregular noise or sound detection technology, such as for explosions or gunshot detection, is considered a major 
safety and security part of a smart port design. The deployment of such detection systems (e.g. sensitive microphones 
and UHD+ 360 o CCTV cameras) through the use of a reliable 5G network, transmitting real -time audio -visual 
information on events to the ports operations centre, is of outmost importance to port authorities by allowing them to 
act immediately and find out the exact location of the incident.

Living Lab 4: Media & Entertainment (M&E) 
Introduction: 
M&E services need to cope with increasing demand in terms of data rates, number 
of simultaneous users connected and/or more stringent QoS requirements. High 
quality and high-resolution audio -visual services are important drivers for 
increased downlink data rates , where 5G promises to provide cost -effective 
alternatives to today’s Content Delivery Network (CDN) approaches. At the same 
time, user generated content , as well as the use of  cellular technology for 
professional and semi-professional media production are key drivers for increased 
uplink data rates.  Cellular, especially when used in bonding multiple links, has 
been replacing the traditional uplink method of satelli te trucks transmission and enabled live high -quality 
transmission to all sorts of media content providers. 5G will enable this viable and immensely growing area of cellular 
and IP-based live media production as a business to grow further, supporting new business models, such as production 
in the cloud , at lower costs .  5G will seamlessly integrate services over different network technologies (fixed, 
wireless), topologies (including e.g. unicast, multicast and broadcast) and capabilities (e.g. caching and multi-link), 
which may be needed to cover all M&E use cases. The main uses cases identified in this LL are the following: 
Use Case 4.1: Ultra High-Fidelity Media;  Use Case 4.4: User & Machine Generated Content; 
Use Case 4.2: Multi CDN selection;   Use Case 4.5: Immersive and Integrated Media and Gaming; 
Use Case 4.3: On-site Live Event Experience;  Use Case 4.6: Cooperative Media Production. 
 
 
Context – Business Situation & Drivers 
5G networks will catalyse the media industry chain, from production and contribution to distribution. 5G networks’ 
ability to dynamically respond to such needs will be the key driver for the provision of next generation media services.  
 
Production and contribution business scenarios:  In terms of professional media production and contribution 
operations, 5G will become the cost-affordable companion to be employed, saving space and specialised maintenance 
of equipment, replaced by smaller and general -purpose communications equipment. New business models include 
IP media workflows, remote live production, where the video assets are in the cloud and the involved team members 
are in their homes or offices, as well as enhanced media production services, given that cloud resources and AI/big-
data processing solutions can be used in real time with the live high -fidelity video uplink in a 5G network.  Further 
business drivers are described include: increased productivity and revenues by enabling producing and handling more 
live events simultaneou sly, significantly reduced costs by reducing size and travel of big production teams and 
equipment trucks to event sites, reduced costs compared to traditional media contribution over dedicated satellite, 
reduced costs due to enabling usage of cloud-based production software, increasing viewers engagement by providing 
more content and at a higher quality and higher overall QoE (such as more fluent and reliable video) content on TV 
and online including on social networks, using fewer modems and SIM cards in multilink bonded transmission (even 
from the same 5G operator), using multilink on the same operator for example by using “multi-slice” – a technology 
of bonding two modems on two different network slices. 
 
Distribution business scenarios: According to Cisco’s Visual Networking Index 40, video content is expected to be 
responsible for 75% of the mobile data traffic  by 2021.  At the same time, media companies and content providers 
are affected by rising CDN costs. 5G is expected to reduce content distribution costs and offer a competitive business 
advantage to Mobile Network Operators ( MNOs) that will be able to provide transparent multicast and broadcast 
capabilities, at a considerably lower network load. Caching close to the edge provides an interesting comme rcial 
opportunity for MNOs.  
 
Solution – Technology Perspective 
Taking into account that the media traffic is the main traffic type, volume-wise being delivered by the networks, the 
new 5G networks will play a major role in media distribution. The solution must be transparent in different levels, 
from the media delivery protocol perspective to be universally adopted, and from the networking efficiency to avoid 
overheads with extra messaging. This can become a reality by using content delivery analytics to measure the speed 
and availability of different delivery paths over the network. 5G slicing, Multi-access Edge Computing (MEC), Fog 
and Mist Computing architectures can make the difference in order to exploit in an isolated and scalable way geo -
based network and QoS analytics with almost zero latency. In this regard, SDN over NFV virtualisation technologies 
bring new possibilities to make an efficient and dynamic setup and provision of the infrastructure. The use of multiple 
IP-based connections bonded together , enables higher bandwidth, higher reliability and lower delay. An inherent 
multicast and broadcast mode with supp ort for large cells and a single -frequency mode provides a highly efficient 
mean for distribution of high -quality and/or immersive content to many concurrent users. Target devices include 
                                                 
40 https://www.cisco.com/c/en/us/solutions/collateral/service-provider/visual-networking-index-vni/mobile-white-paper-c11-520862.pdf  
This proposal version was submitted by Frini LAZAROU on 14/11/2018 13:54:55 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.

regular smartphones, VR/AR glasses, TV sets, public displays as well as in -car entertainment systems (which are 
expected to gain an increasing role in the advent of automated driving).

Use Case 4.1: Ultra High-Fidelity (UHF) Media  
Rapid progress in display and capture technologies is enabling a new, highly immersive production and viewing 
experience with ultra -crisp, wide-view pictures with deep contrast and multi-channel sound. Both linear and non -
linear content will be used for testing the Ultra High -Fidelity Media (UHFM) experience. In order to guarantee a 
high quality of experience for UHFM, 5G network should be able to support efficient network management , fair 
resource allocation, high speed transport capabilities and strategies, e.g. by means of local and network caching of 
content. UC 4.1 involves media streaming to devices using a variety of applications supported by the partners under 
different network configurations. 
 
 
Use Case 4.2: Multi CDN selection 
Media services distributed through multiple CDNs need to be shielded from content delivery degradation and outages. 
ETSI 5G MEC architecture supports smart edge delivery decisions by exploiting geo-based QoS/QoE analytics in a 
capillary, scalable and zero latency manner. MEC can also host edge cloud storage services to make content 
distribution significantly more efficient. Caching popular contents at the network edge saves traf fic on the network 
backhaul and core making distribution costs lower and network capacity thinner. To this end, active monitoring by 
smart proxies paired to gNodeBs in combination with enhanced client-side analytics can predictively decide to switch 
to alternative CDNs or to cache a content in order to prevent degradation or improve the QoE. A generic test scenario 
involves the utilisation of various CDN vendors. By deploying smart proxies and caching on the RAN along with the

Use Case 4.3: On-site Live Event Experience 
In highly-populated live events, such as sports venues, music concerts, or carnivals, lots of users try to upload images, 
live videos and recorded clips as well as watch other participants content or background content related to the event. 
At the same time, special groups of users require continuous Service Level Agreements (SLAs) higher than those of 
the mass. The challenge for media service providers is to offer a good QoE to their clients in a dense client 
environment. Currently, the providers sharing the radio access, backhaul and core network  try to optimise their 
quality independently causing a dramatic degradation of the QoE. There are also special users such as emergency 
services and first responders, that require a steady QoS. 5G network must be able to provide extra resources for 
specific users, groups or services. UC 4.3 involves the generation and simulation of various subscriber profiles in 
terms of bitrate and quality requirements and the evaluation of the corresponding QoE. In addition, this use case will 
be validated with tens of real end-users in large live showcasing events of Patra’s carnival  (Q1 2021 & Q1 
2022). End-users, participants in the carnival,  will be provided with 5G enabled smartphones and/or applications 
(e.g. for uplink streaming) so that they can test the experience and provide us with feedback together with QoE 
evaluation, also helping us in validating the business potential of this particular use case. In addition, we will also 
demonstrate cross network c onnectivity on demand  through the 5G -VINNI facilities in Patra and in Norway. 
Uplink network performance and the quality of the uplinked/streamed content will also be measured and evaluated 
by end-user viewers.

5G networks should be able to support on demand high upload bandwidth and streaming from various heterogeneous 
devices/objects (e.g. cameras, health and wellness measurement equipment, building sensors, etc.).  Similar

Use Case 4.5: Immersive and Integrated Media and Gaming 
Media will become immersive and highly interactive to provide ambient media consumption at home but also on the 
move, with content capable of following the users and adapt to their ambient for viewing. New 5G capabilities will 
enable immersive video experience, to retransmit holographic type video beyond telepresence (2D) closer to a virtual 
presence experience in 3D 360o. Gaming will expand into a full immersive multi -sensorial environment which will 
result in a more realistic experience, improved ability for users to collaborate and no limitation on the number of 
simultaneous users41. Apart from ultra -fast connections and low latencies, Immersive and Integrated Media and 
Gaming requires a uniform user experience, i.e. one that does not significantly change due to the mobility or position 
in the cell. Uniform experience can be achieved through Massive MIMO and channel bonding. UC 4.5 involves the 
setting up of a collaborative game using a distributed approach as well as the testing of various AR/VR applications 
that will be provided by the partners.  In addition, UOP will perform a First-Person View (FPV) scenario involving 
both real time video experience and control  of a remote vehicle/drone involving simultaneously two slice types of 
eMBB and URLLC. 
 
 
Use Case 4.6: Cooperative Media Production 
Content will be captured and shared immediately, utilising 5G enabled video cameras, from anywhere to anywhere 
with additional data, such as location and date, automatically pre-attached. Different users in multiple locations will 
work upon the content simultaneously, which should be able to be automatically repurposed for different 
requirements i.e. second screens, interactive games. UC 4.6 involves geographically distributed journalists covering 
the same event (e.g. a football game, elections, etc.) from different key places. One or more remotely connected

Introduction 
One of the challenges of 5G is to validate its technological and business 
performance across all sets of heterogeneous requirements stemming from 
concurrent usage of network resources by different vertical domains. In this 
respect, relevant field trials will be conducted concurrently with multiple vertical 
use cases grouped over the three separate classes of ITU requirements (eMBB, 
mMTC and URLLC). The purpose is to validate and capture evidence through 
the relevant performance KPIs t o what extent slicing a nd virtualisation are 
capable of successfully managing multi -domain resources,  and how these 
capabilities are in line with such concurrent performance requirements and also, 
that there is no interference between vertical use cases in the presence of concurrent usage of resources  (i.e. 
strict isolation is maintained) . To support network slice management , dynamic service lifecycle automation and 
enable automatic real -time and concurrent orchestration across the 5G-EVE and 5G -VINNI facilities, the CDSO 
based on NOKIA’s CBND will be leveraged, to bind all 5G-related services to be piloted and to control their flows.  
 
Therefore, this LL leverages, combines and executes in a combined and concurrent manner those use cases from 
LL1-LL4 whose target KPI requirements (i.e. high throughput, low latency, high density of devices) fall under 
such classes of service  as outlined in Table 1.6 . In particular , each of the  service classes SC5.1-SC5.3 will 
incorporate the parallel execution of a number of use cases in each of the LLs. All service classes (SC5.1-SC5.3) will 
then be executed concurrently within each ICT-17 facility. In addition, a LL4 use case (e.g. UC 4.3) will be executed 
across 5G -VINNI Norway and Patra  facilities to demonstrate cross -border multi-site capabilities, including the 
triggering and handling of end-to-end value-added connectivity on-demand.

Context – Business Situation & Drivers  
As Europe aims to become a leader in 5G network deployment from 2020 onwards, the challenge is to identify which 
is the best context to launch 5G services. This context will include eMBB, mMTC and URLLC services, as currently 
being standardised within 3GPP and ITU. Moreover, commercial launches require a close collaboration between the 
telecom sector and the different vertical industries in order to achieve the scale and the return on investment for 5G42. 
It is important that concurrent usage of network resources by different vertical  domains can be demonstrated in 
realistic and relevant field trials , to validated efficient and flexible resource utili sation while ensuring SLAs and 
predictable QoE. 
 
Solution – Technology Perspective 
Vertical industries address their connectivity and communication requirements with dedicated specific solutions. 5G 
technologies, slicing and virtualisation , will provide a common base that delivers an open, cost -efficient and 
interoperable eco-system enabling a solution platform for the different verticals. 5G must also cater in an economical 
way the diverse requirements and business needs of a multitude of verticals. In addition, 5G infrastructure and 
architecture will integrate heterogeneous technologies  and enable network slicing, so that the multiple concurrent 
execution of vertical operational services is performed regardless of their diverse requirements. Therefore, in this 
multi LL (MLL), the relevant use cases will be demonstrated while ensuring performance and KPIs according to the 
following three Service Classes (SC 5.1, SC 5.2 & SC 5.3) as they will be executed in parallel and concurrently 
over the ICT-17 facilities (A1, B1-B3, C1-C3) as listed in Table 1.8.  
 
Main Participants and their role:  
The main participants of this MLL are listed in the respective use cases of the verticals in LL1-LL4.

Service Class (SC) 5.1: Enhanced Mobile Broadband (eMBB) 
eMBB aims to satisfy people’s increasing demand for a digital lifestyle focusing on services with high bandwidth 
requirements43. Thus, as the demand for mobile broadband will continue to rise enhanced mobile broadband becomes 
critical. The eMBB SC involves a number of use cases from LL1-LL4 requiring high data rates and traffic volumes. 
In this scenario, different cases with different requirements, including wide -area coverage (low density areas) and 
hotspot (very high-density areas, such as Patra carnivals in 2021 & 2022), are also covered.

Service Class (SC) 5.2: Massive Machine Type Communication (mMTC) 
The mMTC SC involves a number of use cases from LL1 -LL5 requiring high numbers of devices (e.g. >106) per 
km2  being either stationary or at high speeds (up to 100km/h). Additionally, this service class requires a large number 
of connected devices that transmit a low volume of non-delay sensitive data. Devices need to be low cost and have 
long battery life44.

1.3.5 Gender Analysis 
The 5G-SOLUTIONS consortium supports that ‘an in-depth understanding of men and women's needs, behaviours 
and attitudes can improve the scientific quality and societal relevance of the produced knowledge, technology and/or 
innovation’45. As such, it also leads to produce goods and services better suited to potential markets, an aspect 
particularly important for 5G-SOLUTIONS, which is geared towards a commercialisation roadmap and trajectory. 
 
The 5G-SOLUTIONS consortium acknowledges the gender imperatives as stated in the EU regulation 1291/2013 of 
11/12/2013 establishing Horizon 2020 and is committed to participate in promoting equality between women and 
men in research and innovation. The consortium wholeheartedly supports the objectives of the framework programme 
on gender balance. However, acknowledging that there are currently significantly more men than women in the 5G 
industry, in 5G-SOLUTIONS, as part of the management of the project,  attention and effort with be put towards

ensuring a gender balance at all levels ( General Assembly, planned research activities, Living Labs, External 
Advisory Board, etc). We are committed to incorporating sex and gender analyses, where relevant, to the engineering 
of the 5G -SOLUTIONS system and use cases. We recognise that t he end-users of the system and use cases have 
different characteristics (gender identities, sex, age, ethnicity, profession, occupation, education, income, household 
and living arrangements, familiarity with and attitudes towards technology, etc.) and the role that the gender plays 
with regards to the developing technologies and services will be analysed 46. 5G-SOLUTIONS will pay attention to 
basic physiological differences between females and males (e.g. in vision, hearing, voice pitch, etc.) when it comes 
to measuring Quality of Experience . Through task 10.5 in WP10 we will study and report on the differences of 
perception and reaction to the  usage of the use cases  based on gender in view of incorporating the necessary 
requirements in the design of the system and monitor their implementation. In terms of usage, the research and 
innovation will certainly benefit both men and women equally, either as direct or indirect end -users. Alhough we 
acknowledge that most application developers are men, an effort will be made through the project to encourage, 
where possible, the inclusion of women in an effort to contribute to wider initiatives on encouraging women to 
embrace digital and ICT careers. In addition, given that our field trials are planned in heterogeneous sectors, we shall 
consider gender specificities in each sector . For example , although women make up ~47% of the labor force,  the 
majority (73%) of the engineering workforce in manufacturing plants are men47, which is relevant for Living Lab 1. 
Therefore, there is a need to grasp the differential effects that the development of the 5G-SOLUTIONS system and 
use cases will have on these particular groups of men and women. By doing so, the project hopes to meet previously 
unmet needs or even open new markets for applications in the industries relevant to 5G-SOLUTIONS (i.e. Industry 
4.0, Energy, Smart Cities & Ports, Media & Entertainment) that would be better adapted to actors in these domains. 
 
During the requirements gathering (task T1.1) and at the Living Lab field trials, we will ensure that the expectations 
of different groups of potential end-users are captured and will sex-disaggregate the data, as per the recommendations 
of the EIGE 48, to find out whe ther different expectations regarding the interfaces, features , functionality etc., exist 
based on gender . 5G-SOLUTIONS will also ensure gender balance in the conduct of primary research , at project 
team and decision-making levels, as well as in end-user participation in the Living Lab field trials and the audience 
of its capacity building

1.3.6 Inter-disciplinary approaches and stakeholder knowledge 
5G-SOLUTIONS adopts an  inter-disciplinary approach, integrating info, data, techniques, tools , methodologies 
and concepts from diverse technolog ies, engineering and innovation disciplines and ethics, to assess the emerging 
technologies and further develop their application . The inter -disciplinary elements to be integrated , as outlined in 
Section 1.3, include cross-network service orchestration, 5G service cycle automation, leveraging 5G radio and core 
network facilities from ICT-17, and high-performance cloud computing, cognitive machine learning techniques and 
big data analytics, enabling the engagement of f ive vertical industries for the testing of numerous innovative 
heterogeneous use cases with a strong commercialisation potential and ethical added value and social acceptance. 
The adopted inter-disciplinary elements will enable the effective and efficient monitoring, presentation and validation 
of reference KPIs in (near) real-time using privacy preserving mechanisms with GDPR in mind.  The project’s 
consortium has the relevant expertise (as evidenced in Section 4) to carry out the interdisciplinary aspects of the 
project, integrating knowledge from several stakeholders beyond academic disciplines as follows:  
▪ by leveraging and/or advancing assets and results from involvement in Phase 1 -3 projects in which several 
consortium partners have been engaged, such TIM, TNOR, NOKIA, LMI, IBM, CTTC, NURO, IRT, UOP, WIT, 
as outlined in Table 1.3; 
▪ by leveraging the expertise from NOKIA through the use of their CBND Network Director to build the necessary 
plugins to enable cross-domain service orchestration;

1.4 Ambition 
The limitations of the existing state of the art 4G technology mean that new value-added services and novel business 
models that have stringent requirements for the network, cannot currently be exploited by vertical industries. The 
ambition of 5G -SOLUTIONS is to demonstrate the viability of such services and business models in a pre -
commercial, industrial setting.  We will achieve this by validating key KPIs, with differentiated performance 
requirements, and with concurrent usage of resources by multiple verticals, as elaborated in Section 1.3.4.1. This, in 
turn, will provide extensive and valuable feedback to the broader industry towards standardisation and operational 
readiness of both their next generation infrastructures and technologies before wide commercial deployments of 5G 
mobile networks throughout Europe.  5G-SOLUTIONS will also develop collaboration models from the outset to 
ensure enhanced cooperation with 5G -PPP projects and Working Groups. These will take account of existing 
technology solutions coming from projects , as well as the latest white papers and joint demos emerging from the 
Working Groups. It is envisaged that these will be advanced during formal Steering Board and Technology Board 
meetings, in addition to bilateral engagement between projects/Working Groups.  
 
1.4.1 Advancing the state-of-the-art 
5G will bring new unique service capabilities for consumers and industrial stakeholders from vertical industries. As 
an enabler, 5G will ensure user experience continuity in challenging situations, regardless of the users’ presence 
either in a highly dense area or whilst being at high-speed or even at remote locations. A number of metrics depending 
on the nature of the service, such as high throughput, low-latency, energy efficiency, reliability, servicing a massive 
number of objects are important for the successful delivery of the next generation of services. 5G -SOLUTIONS 
involves appropriate vertical industry users to demonstrate pre-commercial trials in 20 innovative use case services 
in Living Labs and over 5 vertical domains, arranged in such a way so as to address the three different types of 
traffic profiles for eMBB, URLLC and mMTC in a separate and/or concurrent manner. Furthermore, it will validate 
the technological performance conforming to target 5G KPIs specified as well as the business potential for 
each use case, directly involving end -user actors (industrial and consumers) and taking into consideration high -
density locations and concurrent multi-vertical usage of network resources. In addition to the innovation brought by 
the novel use cases, the following technological enablers complement 5G-SOLUTIONS innovation concept: 
 
1. Unified Cross-Domain Service Orchestration (CDSO) enabling dynamic service lifecycle automation  
Current Status: To justify, capitalise and provide a return on 5G investment, telecom operators need a solid 
business case with 5G service lifecycle automation ( i.e. zero-touch automation) that leads not only to opex 
reduction but also to revenue-producing services. So, in order for 5G to advance, it has to be justified and proven 
with revenue and profit capabilities. 
 
Limitations/Challenges: Although network slicing and virtualisation may be agile, they are not operationally 
simple as they have to be integrated operationally with the rest of the elements of the services being created and 
supported. Therefore, 5G dynamic service lifecycle automation is required to be able to improve and promote 
operational efficiency and versatility, otherwise many of the benefits of network slicing and virtualisation will 
not be fully supported since they will not be managed efficiently. 
 
Progress Beyond State -of-the-Art: 5G-SOLUTIONS will exploit zero-touch automation mechanisms  in 
NOKIA’s CBND to address this issue, so as to have all operational processes and tasks executed automatically. 
Cloudband is an ETSI NFV MANO carrier -grade service orchestrator with commercially proven reliability, 
automation, repeatability and security. 5G-SOLUTIONS will leverage this technology to support multi-domain 
management of resources, above and beyond the ETSI MANO, as well as the automatic real-time E2E cross-
domain provisioning of services across various  and heterogeneous 5G ICT-17 facilities from diff erent 
vendors. Since NOKIA’s CBND  can be flexibly deployed for any combination of NFV Infrastructure / 
Virtualised Infrastructure Manager (NFVI/VIM) and VNF Manager, it can serve VNFs from multiple 5G 
infrastructure vendors49. This makes it simple to host, orchestrate, automate, and manage virtual ised network 
functions and services, whilst benefiting from open -source innovation, making it a perfect candidate for 
facilitating the demonstration and testing of multiple and diverse service trials across heterogeneous 5G testbeds. 
 
                                                 
49 https://networks.NOKIA.com/products/cloudband?s_cid=smm2013_tmc0593_ar  
This proposal version was submitted by Frini LAZAROU on 14/11/2018 13:54:55 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
G                Page  42  
2. Novel value-added concept for the development of a smart KPI visualisation system 
Current Status: In 5G there are significant and complex performance -reporting requirements based on the 
softwarisation and virtualisation of network resources. Existing performance-reporting systems require offline 
post-processing of data due to the huge volume of data collected that needs to be analysed. However, this is 
cumbersome and time consuming whilst being in the field since iterations and adjustments need to be made onsite 
during field trials.  
 
Limitations/Challenges: This ultimately requires (near) real-time KPI reporting and benchmarking of results 
based on a hierarchy of complex decision -making techniques that analyse historical , temporal, frequency and 
real-time network data. 
 
Progress Beyond State-of-the-Art: 5G-SOLUTIONS will deploy a KPI visualisation system, designed and built 
within the scope of this project, which will be an intelligent E2E mobile network high-performance data analysis 
and reporting system. It will be implemented as a web-based service in the cloud, to help verify the performance 
and validate network and subscriber-based KPIs in different industry use cases in near real-time from several 
locations. The time gap between the actual event and the parsing to feedback test case results is estimated to be 
in the order of a few seconds, and hence is a significant advancement , which will incentivise and accelerate 
complex 5G validation. 
The processing of data feeds from various ICT-17 facilities, will also allow the results to be visualised in a 
graphical form through an intuitive dashboard against the thresholds predefined by the target KPI values, 
as specified by the 5G-PPP expert groups and other standardisation bodies. The cognitive analytics approach 
is proposed for rapid and automated analysis of the vast amount of data, wherein the use of machine learning 
techniques implements self-awareness, self-optimisation, self-healing and self-protecting methodologies 
enabling cognitive performance reporting in near real-time. 
This technology is required for managing a demanding infrastructure comprising multiple stakeholder needs in 
the present and for other 5G actors in the future. Novelty arises from the fact that no one yet has solved the 
scalability and flexibility needs for 5G networks in the context of vertical validation, parallelism, scale, 
heterogeneity and near real-time needs as defined by 5G-SOLUTIONS. 
 
3. Open-standards easy-to-use APIs for promoting and supporting openness for new applications 
Current Status: The introduction of vertical industries use cases in 5G networks imposes major architectural 
changes to current mobile networks, so as to concurrently support a diverse variety of stringent requirements. In 
addition, 5G should pave the way for a larger number of partnerships and Business to Business to Customers 
(B2B2C) business models through APIs deployed at different levels (assets, connectivity, enablers)50. 
 
Limitations/Challenges: Multi-access Edge Computing (MEC) is widely accepted as a key technology in order 
to enable ultra-low-latency requirements, as well as a rich computing environment for value-added services closer 
to end users 51. However, implementing MEC is in its infan cy and its deployment in vertical industries and 
commercial settings requires significant effort, not least in the context of viable business models. Incorporating 
standards in this environment is also a current bottleneck. 
 
Progress Beyond State -of-the-Art: 5G-SOLUTIONS will develop external interfaces and APIs, at both 
management, application, measurement and orchestration levels, based on the latest open standards, such as the 
ETSI MEC ISG52, ETSI NFV and Open source MANO (OSM). These will support openness, interworking and 
integration with 3 rd parties, and strengthen the engagement with 3 rd party developers, vendors and service 
providers. The consortium technological partners will ultimately exploit such interfaces for their value-added 5G 
application propositions. This will create a  standardised, open environment for efficient and seamless 
integration and interworking of applications from such actors across multi-vendor computing platforms at the 
edge of the mobile networks.  
 
1.4.2 Innovation Potential  
5G-SOLUTIONS comprises considerable innovation potential, which we now outline in terms of  Unique Value 
Propositions (UVPs) as shown below: 
 
UVP1: Increase use-case participation and validate multi-perspective KPIs in LLs through end-users 
5G-SOLUTIONS brings together a large set of interdisciplinary partners with different expertise areas ranging from 
the telecom industry (operators and vendors), thematically diverse and complementary vertical  domain experts, 
industrial leaders, SMEs, academia and research organisations. Partners from different vertical sectors will ensure an

interdisciplinary approach is inherent in the project since verticals such as energy and media will naturally have 
diverse technology and business -model requirements. A wide set of heterogeneous 5G representative use cases 
spanning across five vertical industries will be demonstrated in a complementary way. The use case scenarios 
identified and described in 5G -SOLUTIONS arise directly from vertical partners. All use cases, which are highly 
innovative from 5 significant  industry vertical domains, have a high commercialisation potential , require 5G 
performance capabilities and will be demonstrated with end-user actors in Living Labs, both separately as well 
as concurrently. The validation of separate 5G KPI sets in such key use cases will be addressed simultaneously from 
two perspectives: the technological perspective, brou ght into the project by the technological experts, and the 
business-centric perspective introduced by directly engaging end -users in the Living Lab s. This validation will 
ultimately boost the adoption of new, improved, compelling and innovative applications to the end-users. 
 
UVP2: Integrated semantic cutting-edge technologies to reduce fragmentation 
Acknowledging that even though each of the following sectors is at the cutting-edge of its technology and that there 
are multiple initiatives that promote each one of them, including 5G-PPP projects, still they are addressed separately 
and not in an interrelated and integrated environment. Hence, 5G -SOLUTIONS will integrate the following in a 
unified environment: 
▪ High-impact vertical use cases with a  high future business potential in end -user driven thematic Living Labs 
based on Factories of the Future, Smart Energy, Smart Cities, Smart Ports and Media & Entertainment. 
▪ Open-standards easy -to-use application-layer intent -based APIs for promoting and su pporting openness in 
developing new vertical applications by 3rd parties. 
▪ Network slicing and E2E cross-network service orchestration, provisioning and management of shared resources 
across different 5G vendor infrastructures, including dynamic service lifecycle automation. 
▪ Cognitive AI and machine learning  big-data analytics and cloud -computing to automate the analysis and the 
presentation of the KPIs against target values in (near) real-time thus producing results during the field trials. 
 
UVP3: Open standards Cross-Domain Service Orchestrator (CDSO) 
A unified CDSO based on automation enabling multi-domain slicing and 5G service lifecycle automation will cater 
for the multi tenancy needs supporting network slicing imperatives, so as to enable automatic real-time provisioning 
across heterogeneous 5G testbeds. This will be realised by using and extending an existing proven E2E service 
orchestrator (NOKIA’s CBND), enhancing it with new plugins to enable its integration with the 5G ICT-17 facilities, 
as well as improve operational efficiency and versatility in network slicing and virtualisation. This will enable 
the validation of key sets of 5G KPIs in diverse vertical use cases in an automated way. 
 
UVP4: Accelerate the development of 5G technologies towards commercial deployment 
5G-SOLUTIONS is in direct support of 5G -PPP’s aspiration to see new connected digital markets, and contributes 
to the EC’s broader industry digitisation and policy objectives in support of the Digital Singl e Market, maintaining 
Europe’s leadership position in mobile telecommunications. 5G -SOLUTIONS will accelerate the development of 
5G technologies out of the R&D phase and towards commercial deployment by providing valuable feedback to the 
5G industry. Thus 5G-SOLUTIONS will ensure 5G products and services will be able to cope with the market’s 
requirements. 
 
UVP5: Supporting openness, enhancing knowledge and fostering collaboration  
5G-SOLUTIONS’s intention is to open source the majority of the innovation an d technology advancements with a 
view to increasing Europe’s innovation capacity. In this respect, and further to the open access to research data and 
to all scientific publications to be produced, a comprehensive set of open-standards easy-to-use APIs will be designed 
and developed, including northbound application APIs for facilitating the development, portability and provisioning 
of new user-friendly 5G applications and solutions by SMEs. These APIs will become one of the key facilitators of 
5G technology, supporting the digital transformation underway in enterprises and industry verticals, enabling them 
to prosper in multi-dimensioned business ecosystems.  
 
The project will also result in a stronger, more competitive and innovative telecommunications industry fostering 
cooperation between key actors including research, academic institutions and end -users. 5G -SOLUTIONS 
members will have the opportunity to intersect in important aspects of actual field test trials, as well as partner in 
use cases that promise to have substantial research and commercialisation potential, with the support of domain 
experts in the 5G technology space. 5G -SOLUTIONS members will also have the opportunity  to build early 
knowledge and competences for their respective organisations, in turn accelerating growth of knowledge, expertise 
and a valuable network of partners to help accelerate their progress in a growth area where 5G is anticipated to have 
a multi-billion Euro impact for industry, clients, partners, end users etc., on a global scale.

Section 2: Impact
2.1 Expected impacts  
 
The challenge of providing solid impact analysis is crucial for all the actors in the 5G value chain, starting from 
vertical industries and SMEs . In fact, all these stakeholders can bring together the necessary set of expertise, 
expectations, solutions, and strategies for the operational roll-out of 5G services in the market. As all worldwide 5G 
programs and initiatives  have acknowledged, 5G technologies will not be deployed and adopted without a 
compelling demand by a wide set of business cases expressed by leaders of vertical markets. We are currently 
at the turning point in history when the 5G usability is being demon strated, and when its full success or failure is 
determined.  
 
As shown in Figure 2.1, the expected outcomes of the project, measured through the achievement of relevant 
technological, business, dissemination and communication KPIs as defined by the vertic al industries, will generate 
impact in the 5G domain.  
 
 
Figure 2.1: 5G-SOLUTIONS delivering Impact from Objectives 
 
5G-SOLUTIONS aims at maximising the impact to the realisation of the 5G Vision by conducting advanced field 
trials representing key segments of the 5G market in complementary and combined ways in order to demonstrate and 
prove the capabilities of the 5G technology. Such domains, identified in Factories of the Future, Smart Energy, Smart 
Cities, Smart Ports and Media & Entertainment, as of 201 7, collectively represent ~46%53 of the European Gross 
Domestic Product (GDP). 5G-SOLUTIONS is therefore likely to generate business and economic impact in key 
economic sectors, as well as accelerate 5G network deployment that would transform many aspects of the life of 
European citizens, e.g. the way they work, entertain themselves, etc. In addition, the project will endorse a business 
analysis, based on  the Living Labs ecosystem approach. As an impact paradigm, the business model that 5G -
SOLUTIONS will follow is the open innovation one. This paradigm developed in recent years is particularly suited 
to the 5G context, both for the virtualisation approach of the network as well as for the possibility of having a strong 
impact on future developers and especially on SMEs. 
 
The 5G-SOLUTIONS consortium will endorse the idea to advance further the telco industries from the classic value 
chain model to a more innovative one; through the employment of its open source components, the project will impact 
the business with a sustainable community of SMEs and institutions, both collaborating and/or competing, 
whilst creating value for customers and end-users. The dissemination & communication activities (in Section 2.2) 
are geared towards reaching these communities.

Expected Impact 1: Validated core 5G technologies and architectures in the context of specific vertical use cases 
and deployment scenarios, from high to low density regions. (Linked to project’s Objectives 1-3). 
5G-SOLUTIONS will contribute to this impact by means of directly engaging end-users as participants in vertical 
Living Labs demonstrating in the field that the 5G disruptive performance capabilities and flexibility enable the 
offering of realistic, innovative and advanced service scenarios  over key vertical domains (i.e. Factories of the 
Future, Smart Energy, Smart Cities, Smart Ports and Media/Entertainment) in a complementary way. The use case 
scenarios covered in 5G -SOLUTIONS have been carefully selected as they require 5G performance 
capabilities. These scenarios will be demonstrated with expert vertical stakeholders in Living Labs, validating both 
the core 5G technologies and architectures (e.g. 5G NR, network slicing, slice lifecycle automation, SDN/NFV, 
Multi-access Edge Computing (MEC), softwarisation, management and orchestration) of the underlying 5G end-
to-end ICT-17 infrastructure s, together with  their corresponding technological performance in conforming to 
target 5G KPIs specified per use case. Both low and high-density locations (e.g. encompassing a large number of 
devices and users) will be used in order to validate them credibly under realistic conditions.

Expected Impact 2: Validated core technologies and architecture for differentiated performance requirements 
originating from eMBB, mMTC, URLLC use cases, notably for end to end slicing and virtualisation. (Linked to 
project’s Objectives 1-3). 
Through the interaction with renowned industry vertical stakeholders, a number of innovative use cases have been 
identified in key vertical industries. Many of these use cases are variations of a subset of basic 5G service classes 
(eMBB, mMTC and URLLC), w hich have been consolidated and agreed to be covered in the context of 5G -PPP 
and different Standards Developing Organisations ( SDOs). Network slicing and virtualisation aim for building 
dedicated logical networks that exhibit functional architectures cust omised to the respective tel ecommunication 
services over such service classes. Therefore, 5G-SOLUTIONS will practically demonstrate fine-grained end-
to-end network-slicing and virtualisation and its impact on user experience and network performance, will b e 
evaluated under various traffic conditions, through an agile -based iterative process  as outlined in Section 1.3.4 . 
Results and lessons learned will be documented in reports in each Living Lab (deliverables D4.2-D7.2) with relevant 
recommendation/best practices derived from the experience gained on network slicing and virtualisation. 
In LL1-LL4 (i.e. covering separately each of the vertical industries in the Factories of the Future, Smart Energy, 
Smart Cities, Smart Ports and Media/Entertainment) the differentiated performance requirements of 5G will be 
validated and in MLL, the performance and flexibility of the 5G facilities will be validated during concurrent 
multi-vertical usage of resources by multi-tenants. In particular, the architecture and network slicing will monitor 
and dynamically adapt the resources to the required demand to achieve network slice efficiency.

Expected Impact 3 : Viable business models for innovative digital use cases tested and validated across a 
multiplicity of industrial sectors, including demonstration of required network resource control from the vertical 
industry business model perspective. (Linked to project’s Objective 4).  
All use cases in 5G-SOLUTIONS have been carefully selected as they are expected by their respective vertical 
industry leaders to have a high future commercialisation potential and 5G relevance. As part of task T8.2 under 
WP8, business development plans will be developed  over 3 clusters of services , i.e. (i) Industry 4.0 covering 
Factories of the Future use cases, (ii) Smart Urban Environment covering Smart Energy, Smart Cities and Smart 
Ports use cases and (iii) Enhanced User Experience , covering Media & Ent ertainment industrial sectors . These 
business development plans will be fed by end user (industrial and consumers) inputs who will validate the business 
potential of such use cases in the Living Labs. 
 
According to the 5G -PPP Architecture white paper 54 published in January 2018, short service creation, high data 
rates and volumes, device autonomy and identity have been expressed by vertical sector stakeholders, as key for a 
successful commercialisation, and therefore these KPIs will be monitored, measured and benchmarked in each of 
the 3 iteration cycles of field trials and taken into consideration in the business model of each use case.  
 
The business aspect of each of the following UCs will be validated according to the business UC validation 
methodology in Section 1.3.4.1 and the corresponding business metric parameters to be quantified and 
developed in task T1.5  based on cost and risk an alysis. The business validation  of each use case will be 
performed by end -user partners of the consortium, who will directly engage a number of the ir customers for 
subsequently providing feedback for their usefulness, applicability, social acceptability, etc. This is essential to 
evaluate and estimate the level of adoption by the industry and society  so as to enable the service from a 
particular use case to be evolved and be mature enough to add it to the portfolio of the end-user stakeholders.

5G Contractual Public-Private Partnership (cPPP) 
5G-SOLUTIONS welcomes the Innovation Union63 where world-class science leverages the removal of “obstacles 
to innovation” (improving skills, setting standards, improving time to market), and where the public and private 
sectors work together. In particular, it stands in full support of the 5G-PPP where public and private actors cooperate 
in implementing technological priorities in 5G. 5G-SOLUTIONS participates to this effort by bringing researchers 
and industrial organisations together in a determined and focused consortium. The project plans to link research as 
closely as possible to the needs of the marketplace and service providers, aims to be an exemplar of this in action 
and anticipates that opportunities arising from 5G-SOLUTIONS will have an impact on the EU employment and 
R&D targets, as well as accelerating commercial interest in 5G use cases across multiple industry domains/verticals.  
 
Impact on 5G-PPP 
5G-SOLUTIONS objectives and results are expected to be a key stimulus to the activities of the 5G IA (with many 
of its consortium partners having a primary role in it), of the 5G-PPP at large and as part of the program development 
activities for all the 5G-PPP projects. The following contributions are expected to the major Working Groups (WGs) 
in the 5G PPP ecosystem (5G PPP, 5G IA and Networld2020):  
• 5G IA Trials WG, providing contribution from the results from 5G-SOLUTIONS field trials. 
• 5G PPP Pre-Standardisation WG, stimulating and supporting the bidirectional interactions with 5G Standards 
Developing Organisations (SDOs) as detailed in Section 2.2.2. 
• 5G PPP Spectrum WG, contributing to coordinated EU actions.  
• 5G PPP 5G Architecture WG, contributing to next releases of the 5G PPP architecture, currently at v2.0. 
• 5G PPP SDN / NDF and Network Management & QoS WGs, contributing to the evolution of the software 
network architecture and tools selection based on inputs from the experience in 5G facilities of the project. 
• Networld2020 SME WG, contributing to define engagement strategies towards 5G Trials for SMEs 
developing solutions for the control of the 5G network and the for the vertical applications. 
 
5G-SOLUTIONS consortium members are aware of the contractual commitment of the 5G -PPP as well as the 
organisational structure as described in the 5G-PPP contract and its technical annex. In particular, they acknowledge 
the roles and commitments of the European Commission, the PPP board, the Networld2020 ETP, and the 5G 
Infrastructure Association. 5G -SOLUTIONS consortium members will continue to participate in the 5G -PPP 
Steering and Technical Boards, and participate in a number of WG s that are relevant to the project and contribute 
to their outputs, such as whitepapers, showcases and workshops. Personnel time and funding have been allocated 
in the project budget to take this participation into account through its dissemination channels . In additio n, 
representatives of consortium members participate in the 5G IA Governance and Office  as follows: Chairman of 
the Board, Dr. Colin Willcock ( NOKIA), and Board members: Raffaele de Peppe ( TIM), Håkon Lønsethagen

2.1.2 How the Expected Impacts set out in the Work Programme will be monitored 
 
The sets of KPIs defined in each Living Lab will be monitored during the project progress, and in particular during 
each of the 3 iteration cycles of 5G -SOLUTIONS Phase 3, by applying Azdic’s impact mapping technique 64, thus 
constituting the main driver for 5G-SOLUTIONS’s ongoing impact assessment imperatives. In this respect, impact 
analysis and monitoring will be applied  to the LLs to collect, analyse data and present the results against the 
reference target KPIs. These will be re -examined and fine -tuned in task T1.1. For the development of 5G-
SOLUTIONS components to TRL 6, verification and validation in the LLs will be conducted to achieve carrier-grade 
levels. KPI measurements will be recorded and will be compared to reference KPIs indicated in the LL descriptions 
in Section 1.3.4.1. It should be noted that the estimate of potential improvements in 5G networks against the current 
4G technology is substantial, evidencing the real need for the proposed work and associated innovation.  
 
2.1.3 Other impacts 
Together with the impacts identified in Tables 2.1a and 2.1b, 5G-SOLUTIONS will eventually produce a positive 
impact on different actors and areas that will benefit from the results of the project, as described in the following 
sub sections. The consortium believes that 5G will become the underlying fabric of an entire ecosyst em of fully 
connected intelligent sensors and devices, capable of delivering benefits at every rung of the ecosystem’s ladder, 
providing seamless, continuous connectivity for business applications, but also transforming the daily lives of 
European citizens.  
 
2.1.3.1 Impact on SMEs 
SMEs have a great added value in providing innovative concepts and solutions that could be used in various places 
of the 5G value chain. SMEs are important stakeholders in the overall development chain towards future 
communication networks65. In particular, the development of innovative applications – that is an essential part of the 
Living Lab approach - requires SME involvement. High-tech SMEs will be early adopters of 5G technology and will 
build the future market of 5G services. These arguments led us to include the activities planned in  WP9 task T9.2 
(see Section 3.1.4) that will enable us to identify the right stakeholders.  In particular, a public competition will be 
organised in M24, requesting SMEs and spin-off of research institutes, who are willing to contribute to the project’s 
experiments, to submit their ideas on how to best exploit 5G-SOLUTIONS’s results for developing new applications. 
The SMEs with the best ideas will be selected and 3 prizes (€10.000 each) will be given to them (relevant budget has 
been assigned to A2T for this purpose). Such SMEs will be external non-consortium members.  
 
 Measure of achievement: The SME involvement will be assessed through direct evaluation of targets proposed 
and actual achievements as benchmarked in the project ’s activity reports. It can also be assessed through the 
dissemination and communication plan (Deliverable D9.2), showing exactly which SMEs were contacted. Table 2.2 
outlines relevant target KPIs, which are based on previous experiences from A2T’s and TIM’s engagement in H2020 
projects, FP7 accelerators and ENEL’s Open Innovation Program, focusing on contacting, onboarding and engaging 
SMEs, including start -ups and (public/private) research spin -offs, selecting innovat ive ideas. Considering the 
complexity of engagement and selection, a multi-stage involvement processes to reach adequate quality standard of 
participating parties with the following KPIs have been set to measure SME contact, relationship and participation 
effectiveness.

2.1.3.2 Impact on the telecommunications industry 
As indicated in a study carried out by Ericsson and Arthur D. 
Little66 (Figure 2.3), with 5G technology, telecom operators are 
looking at an additional 36% revenue from 5G -enabled 
industry digitalisation market opportunities (in 10 industries) 
by 2026, compared to the 10-15% annual growth a decade ago 
and the current 1.5% annual growth for current operator service 
revenues. This represents an anticipated $619 billion (€504 
billion) revenue opportunity for telecom operators addressing 
industry digitali sation with 5G technology, broken down as 
follows: $204 bil lion (€166 billion) for network development 
(connectivity and infrastructure provisioning), and $337 billion 
(€275 billion) from service enablement services and $79 billion 
(€69 billion) from application and service provisioning. 
 
Given the above opportunities, 5G-SOLUTIONS will help the 
telecom industry by providing research and evidence through the outcomes from the Living Labs, which will 
support telecom operators, telecom vendors as well as the consortium’s partners who have products and 
services in the network management, SDN, NFV and vertical applications market. Table 2.3 presents the impact 
that 5G-SOLUTIONS aims at bringing to key specific actors of the telecom industry.

2.1.3.3 Impact on the European economy 
Apart from the ICT sector, 5G has the potential to create new jobs and stimulate growth in all industries that are able 
to exploit wireless mobile technology to become more competitive, to create new business models and to offer new 
services67. At European level, according to the study “Identification and quantification of key socio-economic data 
to support strategic planning for the introduction of 5G in Europe ”68, aiming at forecasting the qualitative and 
                                                 
66 https://www.ericsson.com/assets/local/narratives/networks/documents/report-bnew-17001714-uen-rev-a.pdf  
67 http://www.europarl.europa.eu/RegData/etudes/BRIE/2016/573892/EPRS_BRI(2016)573892_EN.pdf  
68 https://connectcentre.ie/wp-content/uploads/2016/10/EC-Study_5G-in-Europe.pdf

This proposal version was submitted by Frini LAZAROU on 14/11/2018 13:54:55 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
G                Page  51  
quantitative socio-economic benefits of 5G, in particular in vertical industries, 5G is expected to generate economic 
benefits of €62.5 billion/year by 2025. 63% of these benefits wi ll arise for business and 37% will be provided for 
consumers and society. Input-output analysis69 suggests that 5G investment in the EU will lead to multiplier effects 
with a value €141 billion. These effects are likely to create 2.3 million jobs in EU.  
 
The vertical domains, covered in 5G-SOLUTIONS, address industry segments that directly address 46% of 
the European GDP (as analysed in Section 2.1) and which will benefit from the pan -European 5G network 
deployments.  As such, verifying the 5G KPIs in the content of those industry segments is expected to have a 
substantial business and economic impact for the partners, and to the EU as a whole when disseminated through 5G-
PPP. 5G-SOLUTIONS’s indirect impact on the European economy will be to contribute to accelerate 5G 
deployment in Europe, by demonstrating that 5G KPIs are feasible and attainable, starting from 5 key 
industrial segments, where 5G business practical applications carry tremendous potential. 
 
2.1.3.4 Scientific impact: Improving European innovation capacity and integration of new knowledge 
The challenge-based third pillar of H2020 emphasises the need to take the societal problems themselves as a starting 
point for research and innovation work. The technical work of the project requires an interdisciplinary approach of 
the project ( high-impact vertical use cases, fusing telecom big-data graphical analytics with cognitive machine 
learning techniques with cloud -computing approaches for near real -time presentation of 5G network multi-
perspective KPIs, data privacy, etc.) that can only be provided by a combination of researchers, technology suppliers 
and industrial end-users. 
 
In order to interpret and illustrate the process of knowledge creation, s everal concepts have emerged, in  particular 
related to  the non -linear nature of innovation and the multiple input and feedback loops required between the  
stakeholders in an innovation system. For example, 5G -SOLUTIONS will allow us to construct, study and analyse 
data on graphs, which represent the performance capabilities of pre-commercial 5G networks illustrating in the field 
the interactions between vertical industry companies and end-user customers. Such developments would not only be 
useful to 5G-SOLUTIONS project but also to the broader 5G research communities which would benefit from the 
results of the project. 
 
In addition, Europe presents a linguistically inhomogeneous environment , which is also reflected in the way  the 
telecommunication industry is evolving. This multilingual and multi-cultural aspect will allow 5G-SOLUTIONS to 
provide real data from real end-users in the field , which reflect this diversity and provide better adaptability to 5G 
markets outside of Europe. This will provide 5G-SOLUTIONS with a significant competitive advantage when 
compared with US-centric 5G technologies and services. The innovations identified in the project will complement 
its shared commercialisation strategy and will be evidenced by formal EUPO and USPTO patent filings. 
 
2.1.3.5 Societal, environmental and other impacts 
5G-SOLUTIONS has considerable potential to create positive societal and environmental impacts, ultimately through 
the deployment of 5G technologies in a wide number of sectors. Such impacts will fundamentally reshape not only 
the way European citizens work, communicate, travel, keep healthy or entertain themselves, but also the societal 
design of the entire European countries, in such a way that the structural and infrastructural differences between the 
single EU states could b e reframed by the key driver of a more efficient, well-being oriented, socially accepted, 
and environmentally-friendly European way of life. According to the study “Identification and quantification of 
key socio-economic data to support strategic planning for the introduction of 5G in Europe ”70, a wide array of 
benefits, of societal, environmental and other types, are foreseen. During 5G-SOLUTIONS, impacts of societal, 
environmental nature and for citizens will become apparent during the field trials. An overview of the most important 
impacts, classified under the Living Labs and specific use cases (UCs), are as follows: 
 
Factories of the Future (LL1) 
Productivity gains in the manufacturing sector  will be reali sed thanks to process optimi sation inside digital 
factories (UC 1.1 & 1.2), remote controlling of factory equipment  (UC1.3), connected goods (UC1.4) and rapid 
deployment of new robotic machinery (UC1.5) . It is estimated that 5G data exchange capabilities will enhance 
productivity by at least 1%/year creating productivity gains of €14.5bn/year in the EU manufacturing sector64. 
 
Smart Energy (LL2) 
The 5G-SOLUTIONS Smart Energy LL will align the project ’s objectives with the needs of the European market. 
The E U energy market is very heterogeneous in terms of both maturity and structure; this leads to investment 
                                                 
CONNECT, Trinity College Dublin, InterDigital 
69 Input-output analysis is a quantitative economic technique that examines the interdependencies between different parts of an econom y to 
examine ‘trickle-down’ impacts. 
70 https://connectcentre.ie/wp-content/uploads/2016/10/EC-Study_5G-in-Europe.pdf . The study was prepared for the European Commission 
DG Communications Networks, Content & Technology by Tech4i2, Real Wireless CONNECT, Trinity College Dublin, InterDigital 
This proposal version was submitted by Frini LAZAROU on 14/11/2018 13:54:55 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
G                Page  52  
cancelling, negatively affecting competitiveness in Europe. 5G-SOLUTIONS addresses this shortcoming by working 
towards an open and secure Smart Grid by:  
• Reducing both CAPEX and OPEX of energy utilities  by enabling real-time monitoring and control of the 
Smart Grid, powered by 5G technology, without the need for a dedicated/private telecom network and without 
compromising the security and reliability of the network.  
• Exploiting the revenues from the most promising segment of the energy market, such as the Smart Charging 
services for Electric Vehicle fleets, expected to be boosted by a rate of 25% in the next decade according to a 
market analysis by Deloitte71. 
 
Smart Cities & Ports (LL3) 
5G will transform wireless communications supporting the proliferation of IoT devices and the inexorable growth in 
mobile data arising from the widespread use of innovative services in Smart Cities. In particular, the need for 5G is 
more than just increased speed or bandwidth; it is about achiev ing the execution of millions of machine -type 
transactions, maintaining ultra -low latency, efficiently using the radio spectrum across diverse operating 
environments, providing wider and deeper coverage and constant data collaboration demanded by the IoT . 5G-
SOLUTIONS will improve the Smart Cities and Smart Ports industry, by: 
▪ Reducing environmental pollution through the use of intelligent street lighting (UC3.1) that will monitor the 
traffic flow and automatically switch on and off based on vehicle and pedestrian traffic, advising also the drivers 
of the availability of parking slots (UC3.2). 
▪ Providing a wider approach to smart city co-creation and exploring in collaboration with another H2020 Smart 
City Lighthouse project (+CityxChange) (UC3.3). 
▪ Reducing both CAPEX and OPEX of energy consumption in smart buildings  (UC3.4) by connecting and 
remotely controlling devices, such as air conditioners, refrigerators, lighting and heaters via app ropriate 
smartphone applications. 
▪ Reducing OPEX and time and improve effectiveness of ports and harbours by maximising the availability 
of space and resources and optimising logistics operations (UC3.5).  
▪ Improving safety and reducing crime within port areas through the deployment of automated sound location 
detection systems (UC3.6) transmitting real -time information to the port authorities enabling them to act 
immediately.  
 
Media & Entertainment (M&E) (LL4) 
5G will considerably transform user habits and expectations when it comes to media consumption and production. 
The overall user experience will broaden and deepen rapidly, in terms of types of services (on-demand content, user 
and semi-professional generated content, games etc.), conditions of consumption (on the move, at home, etc.) as well 
as user devices (TV sets, smartphones, wearables, watches, and VR/AR devices). 5G shall enable at least six main 
use cases of M&E services 72 (UC4.1 to UC 4.6) with expected shifting impacts, yet unquantified in economic 
terms, on the way citizens learn, study and entertain themselves.  
 
2.1.4 Barriers and obstacles on the road to achieve the Expected Impacts and how to overcome them 
The advantages and unique value propositions of a European-wide action like 5G-SOLUTIONS have been largely 
described in Section 1.4. However, the consortium is well aware of a number of potential barriers and obstacles , as 
listed below, which – if not properly managed – could limit the expected potential impact of the action.  
 
Barriers / obstacles Steps to achieve the impacts and overcome the barriers / obstacles 
Fragmentation: The approach to 
5G development in many countries 
around the world benefits of 
government sponsored “5G” 
investments73. 5G -PPP could risk 
not to be properly coupled with 
national infrastructure investments 
to implement live 5G networks 
embracing vertical industry 
stakeholders. 
5G-SOLUTIONS originates from various private and public in vestments, 
linked to larger scope strategies of the involved industries  development. 
Also, five 5G-SOLUTIONS consortium partners (i.e. TIM, TNOR, LMI, 
NOKIA, CTTC) are key members and decision make rs of the 5G -IA and 
four consortium partners (i.e. TIM, LMI, NOKIA, WIT) are leading six 5G-
PPP Working Groups (Pre -standardisation, Spectrum, 5G architecture, 
Software networks, Network Management and QoS, Trials). Therefore, 5G-
SOLUTIONS has the potential to overcome the risk for fragmentation and 
turn synergies through the project in a real value at EU level. The industry 
partners will provide a bridge from 5G -PPP and also leverage upon their 
involvement in national infrastructure pilots and investments.

Lack of Common Standards : 
Given the substantial infrastructure 
investments behind the ICT-17 
facilities, which 5G -SOLUTIONS 
will use for conducting field trials , 
the existence of consolidated 
standards represents a solid 
foundation for long -term 5G 
services that the market will accept. 
5G-SOLUTIONS has set a plan of concrete actions to generate impact on 
standardisation (see Expected Impact 4 Section 2.1.1 , and Section 2.2.2 ) 
and the consortium builds on many leaders of standardisation in 3GPP, 
ETSI, IETF, ITU, etc. We will adopt the latest consolidated releases of 5G 
related standards from 3GPP and ETSI NFV and will submit parts of our 
innovative solutions to SDOs. We will also use the 5G -SOLUTIONS to 
validate standard releases and collaborate with SDOs. By adopting this 
active role in the standardisation process, we aim to turn a potential obstacle 
into an opportunity. 
Regulation: The regulatory aspects, 
above all on spectrum allocation, 
access to network resources by 
verticals and measure data traffic, 
may cause problems in the ac tual 
deployment of live 5G networks. 
Aspects, such as  electromagnetic 
environmental pollution or 
concentration of 5G technologies on 
a reduced number of stakeholders, 
thus resulting in network -neutrality 
concerns, may run into regulatory 
obstacles for wide adoption of 5G. 
5G-SOLUTIONS is aware of these issues and has planned specific 
activities to take them into account from the very beginning. A specific 
project task (T8.1) will study the market impact of 5G-SOLUTIONS. Even 
though the involvement of 5G -SOLUTIONS in regulation is out of the 
project’s scope, it is important to note that several of the operators are 
actively involved with policy makers and all levels of licensing bodies and 
will constantly monitor and inform consortium members of evolution in this 
domain. In addition, the Secretary General of the Independent Regulators 
Group (IRG) in Europe, Ms. Delphine Bernet -Travert will participate in 
5G-SOLUTIONS’s External Advisory Board, so as to provide valuable 
advice to the consortium on regulatory ma tters related to the impact 
dimensions that National Regulatory Authorities may have upon, such as 
spectrum policies and 5G-supporting implementation rules. 
Security and privacy: From the 
point for view of the vertical 
industries we can end up collecting 
end-user position and contextual 
data, thus raising potential concerns 
on security and privacy. 
5G-SOLUTIONS will introduce mechanisms for the anonymisation and/or 
encryption of any personal data to be logged in its KPI visualisation system. 
A specific partner (CEL) participates in our consortium with expertise on 
these aspects, who will monitor them (further elaborated in Section 2.2.5.1) 
also introducing privacy by design approaches and ethical considerations in 
5G-SOLUTIONS. 
End-users adoption of 5G 
services: Despite the numerous 
positive forecast analyses on 5G 
deployment and market 
expectations, it could be possible 
that the roll -out of the 5G services 
will be slowed by ec onomic factors 
directly impacting the end-users. 
Obviously, this will represent a significant barrier to the realisation of the 
expected 5G-SOLUTIONS project impacts for the involved industry, but 
the societal implications of this are well beyond the proje ct’s control. The 
5G-SOLUTIONS innovative use cases strongly contribute to demonstrate 
real vertical sector requirements. This demonstration is an important step in 
the cost-benefit relationship, carried out in the business, marketing plan and 
sustainability in task T8. 2. 5G-SOLUTIONS will provide telecom and 
service operators, as well as SMEs with real world evidence of real 
markets where to better position their 5G service offerings.
2.2 Measures to maximise impact 
2.2.1 Dissemination and Communication  
The impact of the project is supported by the implementation of a comprehensive dissemination and communication 
plan that will describe the strategy, released at M3, revised in M20 and maintained throughout the end of the project 
until M36 (Deliverable D9.2). This section outlines how the project will establish and organise the dissemination and 
communication actions to promote the project and the adoption of its outcomes beyond its lifetime. The plan will 
also describe how 5G-SOLUTIONS will liaise with other projects of the 5G-PPP programme in order to contribute 
to and benefit from the related activities at the 5G-PPP programme level. 
 
 
2.2.1.1 Joint Dissemination Strategy  
Target audiences and Objectives 
The general objectives of the joint 5G-SOLUTIONS dissemination strategy are to disclose project results that can be 
used by the target audience to progress their own work, i.e. to build upon the knowledge generated by 5G -
SOLUTIONS, fertilising the advancement of technology, science, industry and policy. 5G -SOLUTIONS has 
identified a number of target audiences, which are listed in Table 2.4a. The specific joint dissemination activities will 
be tailored to the needs and profile of the target audience for dissemination.
