Communication Channels 
The integrated approach to communication adopted by 5G -SOLUTIONS, combines a mix of traditional and 
disruptive communication channels as listed below: 
• Interaction with peer projects , in particular within the scope of the 5G -PPP, including participation and 
contribution to EC concentration and cluster meetings. 
• Publications of high -quality results in international media , such as  peer-reviewed magazines and journals 
including special issues in journals. 
• Contributions and participation to international conferences, workshops and summits. 
• Events: The project will engage in the organisation of established conferences and workshops. In this context 
project consortium members, having the necessary experience and track record, will organise special  sessions, 
panels, and workshops in top conferences as appropriate. In consent and in cooperation with other projects of 
the 5G-PPP, the project will contribute to the organisation of a targeted initiative for all stakeholders of the 
5G infrastructure business, scientific and research community.  
• Workshops: The project will organise 4 industrial workshops (2 hosted by TIM, 1 by CTTC and 1 by TNOR) 
and 1 pre -standardisation workshop (hosted by IRT) organised jointly with other 5G -PPP projects, to draw a 
complete picture of the achievements in Europe.  
• Showcasing: The 5G-SOLUTIONS consortium has plans to use and showcase its results in at least 2 public 
events (e.g. Patra carnivals in 2021 & 2022) . This is expected to generate the largest industrial and societal 
impact on the various involved stakeholders, hence paving the way to a faster adoption of 5G technologies. 
• Participation in large industrial international exhibitions: The 5G-SOLUTIONS showcases will serve as the 
instrument to document and quantify the benefits of the 5G -SOLUTIONS results and to communicate these to 
industry stakeholders in relevant industrial exhibitions. Specifically, 5G-SOLUTIONS will participate with an 
exhibition booth in 2 major international events, such as the MWC 2021 and MWC 2022, as well as in one large 
professional media exhibition, such as the NAB (USA), IBC (USA), BroadcastAsia or CABSAT (Dubai). 
• White papers in conjunction with the European Technology Platform Networld2020 and industry fora. 
• Interactions with worldwide forums, institutes, and standardisation organisations (see Table 2.9).  
• Online presence : A modern, dynamic and user-friendly 5G-SOLUTIONS website will be  designed and 
maintained by EBOS acting as a web portal for public dissemination of project information and results. The web 
portal will be regularly updated and will employ state -of-the-art social media mechanisms  (e.g. Blogs, 
LinkedIn, Facebook, Twitter) to announce new information concerning the project, its results, upcoming events, 
etc. and to engage the target audience groups. 
• Promotional material: Layout and printing of flyers, posters, other materials as needed including but not limited 
to A 3/A4-format brochure s, A4 -format information folde r, A0/A1 -format poster, A5 -format double sided 
distribution leaflet and a 5G-SOLUTIONS project PowerPoint presentation template.  
• Project documentation: Deliverables, technical reports, posters, and presentations will be made publicly 
available in the project’s website and through social media channels.  
• Logo and Templates: A common template and logo support ing the identity creation / branding of the project 
will be produced and used in all project presentations and publications. 
• Newsletters: Two electronic newsletters per year will be released presenting the main achievements.  
• Training activities: Training in 5G-SOLUTIONS will be designed and delivered through a dedicated task (task 
T9.4 led by CTTC) to support 5G network stakeholders across Europe, maximising the use and impact of the 
project’s outputs. It will be used to provide the opportunity for hands -on experience on how to use its KPI 
visualisation system to conduct innovative use case validation, as well as its APIs for enabling easy interfacing 
of new services to the 5G interworking layer.  Training will be offered through workshops, webinars, online 
documentation and community mailing lists. Training supports and facilitates academic and inte rnational 
collaboration and helps the adoption of 5G-SOLUTIONS results in particular in open source communities (e.g. 
OpenAirInterface). Training will aim at keeping participants’ knowledge and capabilities sharp during and after 
the project. Therefore, training activities include:  
• Agreeing on a concrete methodology for the design of the training programmes.  
• Developing “dynamic” online courses in a modular format so that they can be continuously updated.  
• Developing an official enrolment process, controlled by a secure authorisation system.  
• Developing a competencies matrix and credit system for all courses, linked to on-line assessment activities, 
to allow certification (and periodical re-certification) of participants.

2.2.2 Joint standardisation contribution and open source communities 
The 5G-SOLUTIONS consortium is formed of key vertical market players including operators and vendors from the 
telecommunications industry, as well as expert partner representatives who participate in the project with the common 
goal of validating the maturity of 5G services as a baseline for a concrete go-to-market strategy.  
 
In this respect, standards adopti on is key. In fact, the 5G radio/core technologies and the ir corresponding control 
solutions for slicing, resource virtuali sation and abstraction, cognitive and cross-domain multi -tenant service 
orchestration and network management are amongst the hot topics of many 5G standards developing communities.  
3GPP is working on the completion of release R16 (2019) for 5G New Radio to cover the 5G Non-Stand-Alone and 
Stand-Alone operation models with advanced plans for work items and then R17 (from 2020 onwards). 3GPP is 
specifying a 5G reference network architecture , including features like network slicing, efficient user plane and 
efficient content delivery [3GPP TS 23.50174, 3GPP TS 23.50275]. In the area of management of virtualised networks, 
ETSI NFV ISG is progressing towards the NFV Rel. 3 completing the detailed specification of the various interfaces 
identified for the orchestration [ETSI -MANO76] and the virtual infrastructure layer to m ake NFV ready for 
deployment and operation. 3GPP is also working in the management of network slices [3GPP TS 28.530 77, 3GPP 
TS 28.53178], and ITU-T has recently established a high -priority work item on network slicing orchestration and 
management [ITU-T Y.NSOM79] aiming at delivering a first release of the reference architecture by the end of 2018. 
The ETSI MEC ISG is progressing towards its 2nd phase and specifically works to advance the MEC architecture 
towards a Multi -Access Edge (mobile, but also Wi -Fi an d fixed access), to promote the migration from VM to 
containers at the edge and seamlessly integrate with ETSI NFV. Similarly, IETF is also working towards the 
standardisation of protocols and approaches to Service Function Chaining (SFC WG), abstractions (ACTN WG), 
Autonomic Networking ( ANIMA WG ) and Network Configuration models and protocols ( NETCONF WG ). 
Similarly, the development of 5G control and management solutions counts on a solid base of several Open Source 
Software, developed under the control of the Linux Foundation or ETSI, which have become the de facto standard 
for many SDN and NFV systems. Of particular interest to 5G-SOLUTIONS is the mainstream software solutions for 
SDN controllers ( OpenDaylight80 and ONOS81), the NFV MANO stacks ( ETSI Open Source MANO 82 and 
ONAP), the virtual ised infrastructure management ( OpenStack, Kubernetes, LXC/LXD) and  the overall 
integration (OPNFV).

The 5G SOLUTIONS consortium includes partners with key leadership roles in many of the aforementioned SDOs 
and initiatives (Table 2.9), which provides assurance that the concrete expectations of the project in terms of adoption 
of standards and mainstream OSS solutions for the preparation of the foundations of marketable 5G services will be 
fulfilled. The specific actions and resources (task T8.3) in order  to implement the joint two-fold interaction 
with SDOs aiming at a mutual benefit (win-win strategy) are: 
 
Inbound from 
SDOs and Open 
Source 
community 
5G-SOLUTIONS will develop  a smart KPI visualisation system  and leverage/extend an 
existing Cross-Domain Service Orchestrator (CDSO) enabling dynamic service lifecycle 
automation, APIs towards application providers and relevant interoperable interfaces towards 
ICT-17 5G facilities made of multiple 5G technologies and NFV/MEC control solutions. This 
will create a unique user-friendly 5G environment in which 5G network KPIs associated 
with innovative use cases in heterogeneous classes (i.e. eMBB, mMTC and URLL C) can 
be validated (e.g. from 3GPP R15, R16 and beyond as per ICT-17 upgrade roadmap). These 
activities will allow to: 
• Produce feedbacks to SDOs ( e.g. reports and presentations ) and Open Source 
communities of interest (e.g. filing of bugs and feature requests) on the applicability and 
performances in field of the latest standards and software releases. 
• Make 5G-SOLUTIONS a “community field trial” for SDOs and OSS communities of 
interest where to host interoperation tests and/or hacking events . This opportunity 
builds on the successful background of many partners in 5G -SOLUTIONS who have 
opened their trials to host similar events (e.g. Ericsson as part of the OPNFV lab, etc.) 
Outbound from 
SDOs and Open 
Source 
community 
The key research innovations to be developed in 5G-SOLUTIONS are required to enhance and 
fill in the gap of the current state-of-the-art for 5G when moving towards 5G services for 
operations in the field (e.g. multi-domain network slicing, cross-domain multi-tenant end-to-
end orchestration, smart real-time performance monitoring for KPI evaluation, etc.). This 
research in 5G -SOLUTIONS h as great alignment with the needs of SDOs and can 
concretely contribute interesting features to mainstream OSS software . The 5G -
SOLUTIONS partners have identified some preliminary ideas of potential contributions to 
SDOs and OSS community, summarised in Table 2.9. 
 
To maximise impact  on standardisation , 5G -SOLUTIONS will pursue a proactive approach in the project ’s 
execution phase through task T8.3 (deliverable D8.3) that consists of the following planning actions: 
1. Setting up the standardi sation activity roadmap by M8 (Deliverable D8.3) and continue the updating of  this 
roadmap based on the project’s work progress and in conjunction with the SDOs progress. 
2. Coordinating the project and standardi sation groups through constant monitoring of activities and regular 
conference calls with standardisation experts.  
3. Seizing opportunities to push technology contributions into ongoing specifications. 
4. Coordinating with standardisation experts to draft contributions ahead of standard meetings. 
5. Continuously promoting the project at standardisation-related workshops, panels, and summits.

2.2.3 Management and Protection of Knowledge and Data 
For the success of the project, the partners already agreed on explicit rules concerning IP ownership, access rights to 
any Background and results for the execution of the project, the protection of Intellectual Property Rights (IPRs) and 
confidential information. 
 
In order to ensure a smooth execution of the project, and with reference to the Consortium Agreement , the project 
partners will grant each other and their affiliated companies, royalty -free Access Rights to their Background and 
results for the execution of the project. This will allow the researchers to execute the project to the best of their ability, 
without being hindered by administrative issues. The Consortium Agreement will define furt her details concerning 
the Access Rights for Exploitation to Background and results. Within the scope of the 5G-SOLUTIONS project, the 
consortium is committed to regulate IPR and confidentiality issues in line with H2020 guidelines. To achieve this, 
the pa rtners will build their Consortium Agreement (CA) on the basis of the MCARD -2020 model by 
DigitalEurope84. 5G -SOLUTIONS partners plan to have it signed before the Grant Agreement is signed.  More 
specifically, the Consortium Agreement will address the following IPR items: 
• Background provided by partners will be carefully listed in the CA in order to be established at project launch. 
This is a major step to enable the deployment of both open source building blocks (the open source components 
must be specified with their associated license) and equipment vendors functions or equipment (proprietary 
solutions with an R&D license that must be granted to a dedicated list of project partners) in the Living Labs.  
• Foreground developed in the course of the project will  be owned by the partner producing it (ownership and 
joined ownership rules will be defined in CA). Such development could also take the form of open source 
contributions, which are leveraged by the 5G-SOLUTIONS project especially if they create or enhance modules 
that could lead to de-facto standards. In such a case, it will be every partner’s responsibility to comply with the 
license scheme of the targeted open source alliance. 
• The dissemination of the project’s results, including publications, will be driven by the policy specified in the 
CA. The first step of this process will be a prior notification to other partners who will have a reasonable time 
window in which they can object to the publication in order to protect potential IPR from exposure. 
 
2.2.3.1 IPR Management Plan methodology 
The IPR Management Plan in 5G-SOLUTIONS will be based on the following structured methodology: 
Rules and 
agreements for 
the ownership 
and access to 
IP elements 
Definition of the policies for the ownership and access of all the IP elements identified, with the 
guiding principles of fairness across IP contributors and ensuring the freedom-to-operate to the 
overall project, including the long-term sustainability of its pilots. 
• Ownership and access to Background IP elements : explain and detail the results of the 
identification of Background IP elements. 
• Ownership and access to Foreground IP elements : the focus is on detailing some of the 
information related to the identification of Foreground IP elements, such as licensing model, 
joint ownership conditions (if applicable), access conditions for other partners, etc. 
                                                 
84 http://www.digitaleurope.org/Services/H2020-Model-Consortium-Agreement  
This proposal version was submitted by Frini LAZAROU on 14/11/2018 13:54:55 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
G                Page  61  
Innovation and 
IP risk 
strategy 
The interdependencies analysed can help identify risks, such as: 
• During project execution: lack of access (by the indirect owner or by other project partners) 
to a specific Background element can hamper the execution of some activities in the 
workplan, the achievement of some Foreground elements and, ultimately, the achievement 
of some inventions. 
• After the end of the project : lack of, or unaffordable conditions in, access (by the indirect 
owner, or by other project partners) to specific Background/Foreground elements can block 
the usage of some Foreground elements and related inventions. The goal of this work is to 
identify the major innovation-related risks and to define a strategy to deal with each of them. 
• Innovation and IP risks analysis, to identify a number of risk parameters. 
• Innovation and IP risks management, providing a mitigation plan and a contingency plan. 
 
2.2.3.2 Management of Research Data 
The nature of the project is highly experimental, thus, in order to effectively and safely manage research data in a 
broader sense, it will be necessary to define a Data Management Plan (DMP) for making such data Findable, 
Accessible, Interoperable and Reusable (FAIR). In particular, the DMP  will define all procedures to be carried out 
to archive the data, including adopted standards and interfaces, and will make them available based on their nature.  
Research data types will include, at least: 
• Aggregated network data per flow/service slice p rovided to vertical industries, together with the relevant 
measured KPIs; 
• Aggregated network data per flow/service slice provided to the orchestration to enable its proper functioning 
and KPIs matching; 
• Aggregated network data about flow/service slice of network data gathered within each Living Lab; 
• Aggregated network data about flow/service slice of network data gathered at the interworking interfaces of 
different site facilities; 
• Specific flow/service statistics collected for debugging and/or failure management purposes; 
• Detailed data traces collected for specific purposes. 
• Software source codes, technical reports and manuals, managed as per the IPR methodology in Section 2.2.3.1.  
 
Dr. Pat O’Sullivan (ILS) will be responsible for the management of the project’s research data, storage and tagging 
procedures of research data, data classification and definition of access rules, etc. CEL will provide support for 
privacy and ethical issues. Knowledge will be securely stored and maintained in an internal document management 
system, such as EuresTools Workspace85 for the use by consortium partners. EuresTools Workspace provides a 
shared, secure work space in the cloud for project documents, spec ifically designed for H2020 projects.  The data 
within this work space will be maintained after the conclusion of the project for at least 2 years, so that the 
knowledge management will abide by the principles of discoverability, accessibility, intelligibil ity and 
availability also beyond the end of the project. The procedures related to the usage, management, maintenance and 
back-up of this repository will be defined in WP8 and in particular in deliverable D8.4 “Data Management Plan”. To 
support knowledge dissemination and impact creation, the project deliverables will be freely published on the project 
website for any user, as long as they are labelled as "Public" (as indicated in the list of deliverables in Table 3.1c in 
Section 3.1.5). In all other cases, a publishable version of the document will be produced and shared. Also, th e 
project’s website and its content will be available after the conclusion of the project for at least 2 years.  
 
2.2.4 Exploitation Plan, joint commercialisation strategy, business plan and sustainability 
2.2.4.1 Exploitation Plans  
Exploitation planning will start at the beginning of the project with market needs assessment (task T8.1) and will 
develop strategies and plans up to and including for mal patent filings. The exploitation strategy will follow two 
complementary directions: the first one linked to the Living Labs, and the second one relevant to the Open Innovation 
approach. According to Section 2.2.4. 2, as part of the innovation management process, three (3) key exploitable 
innovations of 5G-SOLUTIONS, having the strongest innovation and commercialisation potential, will be selected 
for both EU and US patent filing, thus meeting a key imperative from the consortium that the strategic IP from the 
project is protected “for” Europe and the associated competitive advantages are retained “within Europe”. 
The project will deliver robust industry demonstrators, field trialled with industry leaders, to TRL 6 or higher, and a 
set of commercialisation actions to support sustainable market take -up. Dr. Pat O’Sullivan (ILS) will serve as 5G -
SOLUTIONS Innovation & IPR Manager (IM) and be responsible for identifying and managing innovation from the 
project, advising the Project Management Board (PMB), on the scope and potential of the innovations arising from 
the project, and discerning IP at regular checkpoints. The IM will be supported by an Innovation &

the food & beverage industry. Produce a whitepaper relating to the benefits of 5G for driving increased 
operational efficiencies in the food and beverage industry, towards data-driven plants.

2.2.4.2 Joint Commercialisation Strategy and business development plan outline 
Turing brilliant research into successful commercial products is a complex task with more failures than successes. 
Most failures occur because there is a lack of Product/Market fit 86 or to put it simply, the product that is built is not 
what the market wants to buy. To orientate the outcomes from 5G-SOLUTIONS towards viable commercial solutions 
and assets , we will adopt a focused commercialisation strategy with measurable outcomes by embedding 
commercial best practice into the project’s lifecycle. All commercialisation tasks will focus on delivering solutions 
that are required by the market and a  comprehensive Business Development Plan ( deliverable D8. 2) will be 
developed and continuously updated as part of task T8.2 and will constitute a living document throughout the project. 
 
The completed Business Development Plan will aim to understand viable and commercially relevant solutions, assets 
and services from the project by taking a broad cross -consortium perspective, with credibility built on a foundation 
of embracing industry best practice for bringing new products to market. 
 
Commercialisation Process and Team 
Patrick Durkin from ILS (Commercialisation Manager) has significant experience in bringing new products to market 
and will both lead the commercialisation process and guide the consortium during the project, including the 
development of a detailed Business Development Plan that encapsulates the various innovation opportunities across 
the consortium (both part of task T8.2). The rest of the project’s commercialisation team members are the WP4-WP6 
Living Lab cluster leaders (i.e. IBM, IRIS and LIVEU) who will analyse and identify, together with their Living Lab 
partners, those use cases whose business potential has been validated and which have the highest commercialisation 
potential. Consequently, these partners will create the appropriate commercial structure to deliver s upport for their 
respective outputs beyond the end of the project. All are experienced in industry -oriented research and technology 
development at TRL 6-9 and critically, they all possess time-tested experience of commercialisation. A formal cross-
licensing agreement will be created by the commercialisation team members during the project to support the eventual 
commercial vehicle that is created, with the Business Development Plan providing the roadmap for future commercial 
exploitation (resources required, funding, go-to-market first steps etc.). 
 
Key exploitable results 
The key exploitable result s of 5G-SOLUTIONS are its innovative vertical use cases, which are planned to be 
promoted as commercial opportunities as an outcome of the project. The use cases are expected to be commercialised

The aim is to protect and retain the commercially strategic IP “for Europe” and “within Europe”, in turn giving 
commercialising actors within the consortium a strategic competitive advantage on a world -wide stage. Hence, the 
consortium’s intention to see patents filed in the names of those who have pioneered the inventive steps, as follows: 
▪ To protect the strategic IP within Europe, one  patent is anticipated to be filed in the joint work between 
APPART and EBOS and in particular, in the fusing of APPART’s telco analytics platform with EBOS front-end 
dashboards and cognitive machine learning analytics . This in turn will secure joint IP protection for APPART 
and EBOS in a commercial SME partnership.  
▪ The additional two patents will be discerned in an open and unbiased consortium-wide competition, where the 
Innovation & IPR Manager will work with the consortium ’s Living Lab partners to collectively agree  on the 
most commercially valuable/promising innovation from the innovative use cases validated at the Living Labs. It 
is also anticipated that a commercialisation weighting will be systematically applied in the adjudication process, 
with the end goal of securing patent protection in areas that the consortium has affirmed will guide a commercial 
trajectory, thus securing a competitive advantage to organisations in the consortium.  
 
Competitive Landscape 
5G-SOLUTIONS is focused on  validating the performance capabilities of 5G pre -commercial infrastructures in 
successfully empowering new innovative vertical industry services that cannot be currently offered by the existing 
4G mobile technology, since they require 5G performance capa bilities. Therefore, 5G -SOLUTIONS has several 
Unique Value Propositions as outlined in the Business Model Canvas and explained in Section 1.4.2, that have the 
potential to revolutionise the 5G market by commercially offering such compelling services after the project’s 
completion. 5G-SOLUTIONS will become a European alternative to US and Asia-based competitors. 
 
Revenue Model 
5G-SOLUTIONS revenue will be generated from selling, through a subscription-based model the innovative vertical 
services, through bundled products, considering that each service is addressed to different market segments, spanning 
from consumer to enterprise users. We anticipate three bundled products , corresponding to the clustering of 
services in 3 target groups as per LL clustering, i.e. (a) Industry 4.0, (b) smart urban ecosystem and (c) enhanced 
user experience. Furthermore, we anticipate 3 distinct types of end-users per bundled service: Personal, Professional 
and Enterprise with different levels of functionality appropriate to each type, and each with a different price point. 
Revenue model growth projections tables will be developed for each of the bundled products within the scope of the 
Business Development Plan (task T8.2). 
 
2.2.4.3 Sustainability beyond 5G-SOLUTIONS 
Sustainability of the 5G-SOLUTIONS’s work beyond the end of the project is a key objective set and agreed by the 
consortium. This will be achieved as follows: 
a) Through open sourcing significant aspects of the project’s innovation (see Section 1.4.1), existing 5G actors, 
SMEs, research and academic bodies, and other 5G -PPP projects will have the necessary access right and 
approvals to extend, advance and build upon 5G-SOLUTIONS’s work, in turn leveraging  same in current and 
future 5G projects. Consequently, 5G-SOLUTIONS will open source the majority of its innovation (section 
1.4.1) with a view to encouraging reuse and extensibility across Europe.  
b) Through the evolution of the use cases to commercial services that can be offered to consumers and businesses. 
The business potential of each use case will be validated in the Living Labs and the Business Development Plan 
(deliverable 8.1B) will analyse the results to identify and select those use cases which will be clustered and 
offered as a bundled service to the market. 
 
2.2.5 Data Management & Open Access Plan 
5G-SOLUTIONS is fully committed to open source, and the intention is to open source the majority of the innovation 
and technology advancements. This acknowledges the importance to Europe that future projects build on previously 
funded efforts as well as open dissemination and sharing. 5G-SOLUTIONS’s also intends to file 3 patents, as 
analysed in section 2.2.4.2. Hence, strategic Intellectual Property (IP) filings will be carefully managed in a way that 
will not impede the underlying aspirations to open source and make available the majority of 5G-SOLUTIONS’s 
innovation and technology to European researchers, SMEs, universities and industry to ben efit from and to build 
on/from. Specifically, special attention and consideration will be given to IP, information and data character ised as 
EU CONFIDENTIAL, guided by 5G-SOLUTIONS’s Innovation and Commercialisation Managers, as well as close 
consultation with 5G-SOLUTIONS’s ethics leader in the case of data privacy/confidentiality. Access will be granted 
only to authorised project participants where needed and where appropriate.

For any other project outcomes with public level of dissemination, wider dis tribution will be considered and 
examined in the Data Management Plan (DMP). With respect to data exploitation, the DMP will determine how other 
stakeholders may exploit the data and how the data can be verified after it has been deposited. The partners will also 
use EuresTools, as explained in Section 2.2.3.2, to store and curate 5G-SOLUTIONS data where open access is 
pursued. The project will use established standards and non-proprietary formats for data collection as far as possible, 
to support future exploitation of the data either by project partners or by external organisations where open access is 
implemented.  
 
Green Open Access will be considered as the publishing method of the results. This strategy is directly related to the 
“Open” paradigm that will be used for publishing project results. The initial version of the DMP will be conduc ted 
by M6 as part of WP 8 (task T8.4, deliverable D8.4), and will evolve during the lifetime of the project in order to 
present the status of the project's reflections on data management. The final version will be delivered in M32. All 
personal data will be preserved by the end-user companies at their discretion. No personally identifiable data will be 
shared or will remain with the partners after the project ends without prior consent. If individuals choose to withdraw 
from a user -trial, their personal data  will be removed from the databases.  Open access is supported by the 
dissemination and exploitation approach of 5G-SOLUTIONS results. 
 
2.2.5.1 GDPR & 5G-SOLUTIONS 
The 5G-SOLUTIONS consortium has carefully and thoroughly deliberated on GDPR implications for all aspects of 
the project during the proposal preparation. With the help of legal and privacy expertise in the consortium (see for 
instance the participation of partner CEL specially dedicated to legal, privacy and ethical aspects), as a general rule, 
the consortium has collectively affirmed that none of the data managed, shared, processed or analysed will pertain to 
personal data of any EU citizens, as the nature of the 5G-SOLUTIONS data sets are highly network, test, protocol 
and instrumentation related. In the exceptional case of personal data processing, Ms Carmela Occhipinti (CEL) will 
serve as the project’s Data Protection Officer (DPO) assisted by the data privacy single point of contact  of each of 
the consortium’s members, to manage such data (see Section 5.1.3). 5G-SOLUTIONS intention is to ensure robust 
and compliant policies for the handling of data, in compliance with the EU Data Protection Directive, GDPR and the 
national legislation. This effort will also tie in to the ethical protocol and data management plan for the project, which 
stipulates the ethical and data management principles that the 5G-SOLUTIONS partners will adhere to in their work.  
 
Privacy-by-design data protection context 
In order to be compl iant to GDPR and all other privacy regulations we will use a privacy-by-design approach; this 
means all project results will be developed with privacy and data protection in mind from the design phase. Privacy 
by design means building the principles, criteria and premises for good practices of privacy into technological tools 
that by their nature will have significant powers of intrusion. Privacy by design means that the technology is self -
regulating in terms of privacy. Instead of going as far as it goes in terms of data collection, storage or analysis, privacy 
by design shapes the very design characteristics of a technological device so that by its very operation advances the 
value of privacy. 5G-SOLUTIONS contributes directly and concretely to advance the ambition of privacy by design. 
It regards privacy as an end rather than as a necessary sacrifice to be made in order to achieve goals that otherwise 
would be in conflict with principles of privacy and data protection. 5G-SOLUTIONS builds privacy into the notion 
and system of personal data with a special attention to use case applications.  
 
From the legal perspective, privacy-by-design implies enhancing integration between policy-makers working with 
questions of citizens and industry actors who seek to innovate technological solution to data protection challenges 
within the scope of valid legal standards. In accordance with the notion of privacy by design technological innovation 
will seek to make ‘smart’ investments and design. Products of privacy by design thinking will not waste resources 
on developing technologies, whose realisation will provide services that fall outside the scope of the intention of the 
law. At the same time, privacy by design also expresses itself in the opposite direction. A close eye to the development 
of technological solutions to security challenges, will guide legislators, the courts and police and security services to 
save and better direct resources toward measures that have a real application in the evolving security landscape. 
 
From the ethical and societal perspective, privacy-by-design means developing privacy enhancing technologies in 
such a way as to be in correspondence with the needs, norms and expectations of society. Privacy enhancing 
technology should not aim or undertake more or other than the benchmarks that society itself sets. Privacy by design 
involves, on the one hand remaining vigilant to changes society in order to adjust technological innovation to reflect 
these changes and, on the other hand, keeping channels of communication open toward society at large such that 
technological changes do not catch citizens unprepared. Lack of transparency, according to the notion of privacy by 
design, is not only counterproductive, it is a direct cause of insecurity.

Section 3: Implementation
3.1 Work plan — Work packages, deliverables  
 
3.1.1 Overall Structure of the Work Plan 
The project is organised in nine (9) Work Packages (WPs) that correspond to the project’s objectives, coordinated by 
project management activities (WP 10). Each WP is led by a project partner particularly experienced in the 
corresponding area, so as to ensure the best practice and work efficiency.  
 
3.1.2 Work Packages Timing and Key Dependencies 
Figure 3.1 summarises the project structure, showing the names  of the WPs and the relationship between them. In 
addition to project management (WP10), the WPs are organised in 3 main groups: 
▪ Providing Technical Foundations (WP1-WP3): Conceive, design, implement 5G-SOLUTIONS technological 
enablers and interface with the 5G ICT-17 infrastructure to enable vertical service field trial validation. 
 
▪ Enabling Industrial Acceptance (WP4-WP7): Validate and transform core technical and business results to a 
state suitable for deployment in an operational environment. 
 
▪ Supporting Dissemination and Exploitation (WP8-WP9): Carry out activities during the project, and planning 
activities beyond the project, to prepare for and bring about the promised impact.

Objectives  
• To define in detail appropriate post -exploitable use cases linked to specific target 5G KPIs considering and 
bridging the vertical user point of view (PoV) with the service provider PoV and the solution provider PoV. 
• To analyse the challenges and define the requirements for the provision of a cross-domain, multi, concurrent 
E2E service orchestrator with network slicing and virtualisation capabilities and to define detailed role division 
and interaction between ICT-17 facilities and 5G-SOLUTIONS project. 
• To leverage, build upon and extend previous and ongoing work from EU funded 5G-PPP projects and the 2nd 
phase of 5G standardisation. 
• To produce a set of methodologies to enable (a) the technological and business validation of 5G E2E managed 
quality connectivity (including cross-border and hierarchical resource and service aspects) and associated 
control and management within and across verticals ; (b) the definition of the test report s format, parameter, 
test points, and benchmarking of the results for a unified and reliable outcome. 
 
Description of work 
 
Task 1.1 - Definition and detailed analysis of vertical use cases/scenarios, baseline and corresponding target 
KPIs (FNET, all partners)  
The aim of this task is to capture requirements from the end-user stakeholders, including the articulation of detailed 
use case scenarios and usability needs, and relevant target technological and business KPIs which will be validated 
in the Living Labs . Specifically, this task will be divided into two key sub tasks: (a) systematic  compilation of 
current use cases features and capabilities (b) requirements analysis. A requirements’ capture will involve the 
documentation of end-users needs  and opinions about new innovative vertical use cases that require 5G 
performance capabilities in the domains of Factories of the Future, Smart Energy, Smart Cities, IoT, Media & 
Entertainment. Such use cases will be mapped to specific target KPI and SLA values (e.g. throughput, mobility, 
latency, density, reliability, positioning accuracy, coverage, service provisioning time, QoS, QoE, etc.), which will 
set the baseline for conducting the actual measurements during the field trials.  
 
Task 1.2 – Analysis of challenges and requirements for 5G E2E multi, concurrent and cross-domain service 
management and orchestration including interaction with ICT -17 facilities (LMI, NOKIA, IRT, TNOR, 
WIT) 
The evolution of NFV is faced with the reality that the initial MANO architecture is not adequate to address the 
service providers’ underlying requirement to instil the agility of DevOps principles. Rather than setting up and 
managing services in network domains separately and manually, the expectation on 5G networks is that cross -
domain E2E s ervices will be provisioned, deployed, managed, and retired in a DevOps manner, with minimal 
manual intervention. In addition, where slicing capabilities are exposed by network domains, those E2E services 
will be deployable on network slices. We will also explore the integrity of OSS features being kept under cross 
data correlation from low level virtualisation and the vertical industry requirement, which is agnostic of the 
underlying telecom infrastructure. The core focus of Task 1.2 is to explore the above challenges in the context of 
a framework that aligns with industry standards, yet is innovative and provides leadership beyond what is included 
today in current approaches. 
End-to-end service provisioning with slicing capabilities [NOKIA]: In this task, we shall design how to leverage 
the NOKIA orchestrator to support end -to-end inter -domain lifecycle management. We  will make use of the 
available plugin interfaces to extend the functionality to allow management of closed loop services for network 
slicing. In addition, the plugins implementing the interfaces towards the network domain orchestrators will be 
designed to allow configuration and monitoring of the virtual and physical resources that are providing the network 
slices that the end -to-end services are running on. We will also investigate the issue of monitoring the verticals 
This proposal version was submitted by Frini LAZAROU on 14/11/2018 13:54:55 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
G                Page  71  
SLAs and analyse the data coming from the verticals to allow for efficient orchestration of the end-to-end services. 
The interaction and integration with the ICT-17 facilities (south-bound to 5G -SOLUTIONS) will also be 
accommodated, as well as north-bound to customer facing systems or portals.   
Proposed solutions of slicing issues between core and access in 5G mobile networks  [LMI]: The radio and core 
networks differ in the manner in which they implement slicing and in which such slices are configured. We will 
examine how services using network slices across the RAN and core networks can be provisioned and managed 
transparently. We will investigate how common slices can be created across the two domains, and how traffic can 
be routed and shaped between these slice fragments whilst preserving a common view of the end to end slide. In 
addition, we will investigate how services running across slices can be optimised using predictive o ptimisation - 
we will try to understand how common slicing patterns can be predicted, in an effort to formulate a set of training 
patterns that can be used to train predictive and proactive configuration changes.  
 
Task 1.3 – Leverage, build upon and extend previous and ongoing work from EU funded 5G-PPP projects 
and 2nd phase of 5G standardisation (TIM, NOKIA, CTTC, IBM, IRT, UOP, PIIU, TNOR, WIT) 
In this task we will capitalise on 5G-PPP Phase 1 findings, 5G-PPP Phase 2 and Phase 3 projects and will leverage 
assets and results for use in 5G -SOLUTIONS. The cooperation with the other projects in the call and with the 
relevant entities in 5G -PPP is ensured by this task. The results achieved from 5G-EVE and 5G-VINNI projects 
will be analysed in 5G-SOLUTIONS and shared with other 5G international initiatives, including GSMA, in order 
to consolidate a common vision towards the wide deployment of 5G technologies . This will be realised by a 
continuous exchange of information among the projects, facilitated by the activities of the Working Groups in 5G-
IA and 5G-PP as well as through the Steering Board and the Technical Board, where the Project Coordinator (PC) 
and the Technical Manager (TM) of the project are actively involved, respectively. 
A specific pre-standardisation workshop and dissemination events will be organised jointly with the other 5G-PPP 
projects, to draw a complete picture of the achievements in Europe. Videos and other dissemination material will 
also be prepared to illustrate the performed activities from a joint perspective. 
 
Task 1. 4 – Methodology for the definition of test reports format, parameters and test points, and 
benchmarking for the results (WIT, APPART, CTTC, EBOS, FNET, GLAN, IRT, IRIS, NTNU, OMES, UOP, 
PBGS, YARA) 
This task will focus on defining the methodology and toolset for a comprehensive and robust test analysis of the 
5G technologies and the vertical use cases being created within the 5G-SOLUTIONS project. Working closely 
with the partners defining the scenarios to be trialled in the Living Labs environment, we will specify formats for 
a suite of test cases to measure the functionality and performance of the innovative solutions being put forward. 
These test artefacts will be captured in a suitable test case management tool that will integrate seamlessly with the 
development process.  Based on the requirement to deliver outputs that have commercial value and potential, there 
will be a significant emphasis put on Quality of Service (QoS) to give  a qualitive measurement of test execution 
and on Quality of Experience (QoE) to gauge objective human experience. We will also ensure that the test strategy 
examines the improvement over previous 4G capabilities. Other test methodologies will include resource scaling, 
cross-domain interaction and entire platform testing. The test process will fit neatly into the project’s iterative agile 
development process and allow for implementation of a Test-Driven Development methodology incorporating unit 
tests and acceptance tests. 
 
Task 1.5 – Methodology for the technological and business validation of 5G E2E connectivity and associated 
management within and across verticals (TNOR, APPART, CTTC, CEL, EBOS, ILS, IRIS, NTNU) 
The methodology will entail acceptance test procedure s for conducting both the technological and business 
validation of the use cases considering the associated service management. In particular, as far as the technological 
validation is concerned, we will define the procedures for collecting the data feeds from the ICT-17 measurement 
portals, stating also how these feeds will be used and analysed by the KPI visualisation system to produce and 
present the KPI values in a graphical form. Threshold limits for the benchmarking of the results will also be defined 
per target KPI based on the requirements stemming from each vertical use case. The methodology will also define 
how the interaction with the vertical end-users will be achieved taking into consideration the specifics of task T1.1. 
For the business validation will use the lean start -up methodology that centres around the main motivations of a 
business. The inputs will include apart from the business case itself, end -user feedback from the ir direct  
engagement in the field trials  of the vertic al use cases . The corresponding outputs will be validations that will 
allow to identify those use cases that have the highest commercialisation potential so as  to progress to the next 
step of creating a service product portfolio. For this purpose, we will use a set of  questionnaires, surveys and 
focused group workshops directly engaging also the customers of the vertical consortium partners. A detailed set 
of metric parameters considered for the business validation of each UC will be developed, such as those listed in 
Table 1.7a, which will be interrogated and quantified as part of the business validation process with the end-users.

Description of work  
Task 2.1 - Interfacing and setup of ICT -17-2018 5G E2E facilities to enable LL operation (TIM, NOKIA,

This task entails the interfacing of the 5G-EVE Turin, 5G-VINNI Norway and 5G-VINNI Patra ICT-17 facilities 
with the Cross-Domain Service Orchestrator (CDSO) including configuration and setup in order to ensure the end-
to-end readiness of the 5G infrastructure and measurement portals for the field trials . This task also includes the 
installation and the configuration of 3 remote 5G RAN stations by UOP, i.e. 2 in Ireland (one in IBM campus and 
the other in GLAN factory) plus another 5G RAN station in PBGS factory in Brussels. Localisation is necessary 
in order to perform real measurements and validate the performance capabilities of 5G especially for the Factories 
of the Future use cases , which required ultra-low latencies and high reliability. Two more 5G remote nodes will 
also be installed and setup by TNOR in Norway in order to enable the validation of the measurements for Industry

4.0, Smart Cities and Smart Ports use cases. For the procurement of these 5 additional 5G RAN nodes, budget has 
been allocated to both TNOR and UOP (see ‘other direct costs’ in Section 3.4 ). Furthermore, the intention of 
TNOR is to enable 2 additional 5G RAN nodes for free in locations in Trondheim, Norway, to strengthen the

Task 2.2 – Cross-Domain Service Orchestrator (CDSO) plugins design & development for cross -domain 
orchestration (NOKIA) 
This task is responsible for identifying and implementing the necessary interface adjustments needed (implemented 
via plugins) at the CDSO to enable the end-to-end orchestration of the various services across different and diverse 
ICT-17 facilities. The CDSO implements generic interfaces with a plugin mechanism to include the required 
adjustments. This task includes the following activities: 
Deployment analysis [NOKIA]: Define where the CDSO will be deployed, identify the cloud resources on which 
it will be deployed and identify the required network resources. 
CDSO requirement analysis [NOKIA]: Identify & map the required systems which the CDSO needs to hook to 
and their existing API implementations. Mapping should also include which API on the managed system maps to 
which plugin on the CDSO and what kind of adjustment is required. The deliverable includes a matrix for each 
system the CDSO is integrated with, in which the API's and plugins are mapped with required data manipulation 
to needed to be performed at the CDSO to enable the access and the orchestration of the services to be executed in 
the LLs across multiple ICT-17 facilities.  
CDSO APIs design [NOKIA]: Design the actual pug-in implementation at the CDSO to enable service provisioning 
and orchestration across different ICT -17 facilities. The deliverable includes details of the mapping needed for 
each API implementation at the plugin. 
Design of security measures  [NOKIA]: Identify security risks and specify the actions needed to apply security 
measures to protect the CDSO from external cyber threats. 
Plan for dry-run acceptance testing [NOKIA]: Prepare an acceptance testing plan specifying how the CDSO will 
be tested and the dry-run tests that need to be performed at infrastructure level so as to ensure its readiness for the 
Living Lab field trials. This may require specification of a simulated/m ock environment, so this dry -run can be 
executed prior to the LL operation. 
 
Task 2.3 - Integration of CDSO plugins with the 5G ICT-17 facilities (NOKIA)  
Implementation, integration, deployment and testing of the CDSO plugin for cross ICT -17 facility service 
orchestration. It includes for each controlled system, hooking of the actual API's, testing that the implementation 
was done correctly, and that the system is functional end-to-end. It includes the following activities: 
CDSO installation and plugin implementation [NOKIA]:  Implement the necessary plugins so as to enable service 
orchestration. Install NOKIA’s Cloudband CBND in a cloud-based environment. 
Cross-domain service orchestration across the ICT-17 facilities [NOKIA]:  For each vertical application that needs 
to be onboarded to the CDSO, create the VNF Descriptors and all other required scripts and descriptors to allow 
automatic service orchestration and provisioning. This also includes packaging the required images in the 
supported format and implementing the required deployment actions (scripts) per vertical. 
Deployment and functionality testing  [NOKIA]: Perform dry run testing to verify that the vertical services are 
properly deployed and that service components function properly. The CDSO integrates with the vertical 
application manager via an API which is called from a plugin implemented and executed by NOKIA’s Cloudband 
CBND NFVO platform. This API includes "must" entries and "optional" entries which have default code in case 
they are not implemented. Dry run testing includes verification that all "must" API en tries are properly 
implemented, the code calling them is properly loaded into the NFVO and legal values are returned from the APIs 
according to the Plugin specification. Failure to implement any "must" API or failure to return a valid value, will 
result in a failure of this test. At a later stage, when the integration of the CDSO comes to a "wet" stage (i.e. actual 
integration with the real environment and vertical services that need to be executed), this implementation will be 
tested in the LLs, where not only the API calls will be tested but also the workflow logic. 
Living Labs integration support [NOKIA]: This task is intended to resolve integration issues when the LL are 
actually working in production. There’s a n eed to allocate resources for this task since after implementing the 
plugins and executing dry run testing, there may still be issues that may only be encountered when running the full 
verticals and performing the KPI testing.

Task 2.4 - Zero-touch automation mechanisms for 5G service lifecycle (LMI, NOKIA) 
Within the context of programs , such as ETSI Zero -touch Network and Service Management program or MEF 
Lifecycle Services Orchestration, there has been much industry discussion on automation and lifecycle concerns. 
Zero-touch automation mechanisms are inherently linked to the increase of  speed and removal of human 
interaction throughout the lifecycle of the processes, with a focus on pro-active management. In this task, we will 
examine the complex problem of managing services and machine learning features in deployed operations.  
Analysis of emerging Machine Learning lifecycle programs  [LMI]: We will investigate initiatives on Machine 
Learning lifecycle programs, with a key focus on the viability of a DevOps environment that encompasses machine 
learning models in production systems. 
Enablement or automation via Machine Learning [LMI]:  In this subtask, we will explore novel vertical industry 
automations, based on adaptive automation of 5G features combined with predictive analyses of data coming from 
the vertical industry service. We will also explore network application tracking to support the next generation of 
root case analysis features. By this we extend the core value of automation and accountability to be fundamental 
parts of dependable automation. 
 
Role of main partners: NOKIA will lead WP2, overseeing also the design, development and integration of plugins 
at the CDSO with the ICT-17 facilities, supported primarily by TIM, TNOR and UOP for the installation and setup 
of their ICT -17 facilities, as well as by  LMI for the zero -touch automation mechanisms to enable 5G service 
lifecycle management.   
 
Justification of resources: NOKIA will assign 1.4 FTE person resources in tasks 2.2 and 2.3  over a two -year 
period (i.e. 16PM/year), supported by TIM (0.8 FTE person in task T2.1 @10PM/year for 33 months) and TNOR 
(0.25 FTE person in task 2.1 @3PM/year for 33 months), UOP (0.75 FTE person in task 2.1 @9PM/year for 33 
months) and LMI (0.4 FTE person in task 2.4 @5PM/year for 2 years). 
 
Deliverables

configuration of the ICT-17 5G-EVE Turin and 5G-VINNI Norway and Patra facilities.

v2.0 & v3.0) and final version (v4.0) of reports defining the technical specifications and the low-level design to 
enable the implementation of the necessary plugins at CDSO. 
D2.3A, D2.3B: Zero touch automation mechanisms for 5G service lifecycle (LMI) [M8, M25]: Initial (v1.0) 
and final (v2.0) versions of  reports containing the proposed zero -touch automation methods for 5G service 
lifecycle management to be validated in the project.

Task 3.1 - KPI visualisation system specifications and design (APPART, EBOS, IBM, LMI, WIT)

and translating them into detailed technical specifications, which will be used to develop the low -level design of

high-level analysis of the technical architecture of the system along with the technologies util ised will also be 
provided. The deliverable will be used as input for task 3.2 to enable the development of the system.

Task 3.2 - KPI visualisation system components development, real-time collection and analysis of data feeds, 
and privacy aspects (APPART, EBOS, IBM, LMI) 
Based on the detailed low-level design provided in deliverable D3.1, this task will focus on the development of all 
software components comprising the KPI visuali sation system. This involves the functionality  from the data 
collectors, the data parsers, the KPI calculations  based on the developed deep learning algorithms and machine 
learning optimisation to enable real -time graph data presentation, and the web-based graphical front -end 
visualisation environment for each of the metric parameters to be validated per  use case  scenario. The data 
collected from disparate feeds through the ICT-17 measurement portals will be analysed using cognitive machine 
learning techniques, including  open and linked data, ad -hoc data querying, filtering and retrieval, supporting 
SQL/MongoDB type of querying and or graphical queries, creation  of data displays, master data management 
support, metadata integration, access and retrieval. Define entities for specific KPIs to drive optimisation against 
reference values. Define computational components and algorithms, selecting, configuring and extending existing 
libraries in R and Python. Special care will be given to the security measures applied for data protection along with 
all privacy aspects that need to be taken care of such as data anonymi sation, data encryption, storage of sensitive 
data, etc. Produce the KPI visualisation system  technical documentation containing detailed guides to allow 
successful service delivery, indicating necessary physical requirements, minimum hardware, software and 
guidelines of use from both, tool and technical ser vice interface, where the consortium will pay special attention 
to create substantial and clear documentation to allow end-users from LLs to make use of the system. 
 
Task 3.3 - APIs and interfaces design & development (EBOS, APPART, A2T, IBM, WIT) 
The aim of this task is to define and design the following APIs which will be developed based on open standards:  
▪ Measurement portal intent-based REST API (see API C in Figure 1.1) to enable the interfacing with the online 
measurement platforms of ICT-17 facilities. REST APIs enable software developers to define API calls with 
a high granularity, which simplifies the logic required to provision complex services, thus providing  
interoperability between online software systems. By using stateless protocol s, such as HTTP/HTTPS and 
standard operations, REST APIs have fast performance, reliability, and the ability to scale, by re -using 
components that can be managed and updated without affecting the system as a whole, even in its runtime 
mode. Such APIs will support only secure connections with authentication. 
▪ Application-related intent-based declarative API (see API D in Figure 1.1) to enable the interfacing of new 
services to the 5G interworking layer. This type of API will describe the desired system behaviour and will 
meet 3rd party developers’ demand for agile, economical end-to-end services and application delivery through 
5G, by delivering benefits including ease of use, automation of complex logic, portability, multi -vendor 
interoperability, scalability, etc. 
For these API types, a definition and technical specifications will be provided including their low-level design, all 
of which will be documented in deliverable D3.2A-D. Based on the design blueprints, the software development 
of the APIs will follow.  
 
Task 3.4 - Integration of KPI visualisation system with the ICT -17-2018 E2E facilities and dry -run 
interworking tests (APPART, TIM, EBOS, UOP, TNOR, WIT) 
The key objective of this task is to describe the procedure , to perform the integration of the KPI visualisation 
system with the measurement portals of the 5G-EVE Turin and 5G-VINNI Norway and Patra ICT-17 facilities, as 
well as to perform dry-run interworking tests to verify proper operation, functionality and communication between 
them prior to live deployment in Living Labs . The integration will be achieved through the intent -based APIs of 
the ICT-17 measurement portals and the measurement portal APIs developed in task T3.3. 
 
Task 3.5 - KPI visualisation system deployment as a Service in the cloud and LL driven improvements 
(EBOS, APPART, IBM, WIT) 
Create the necessary packages for container -based system deployment as a service in the cloud, to enable 
concurrency in use -case execution, to quickly match sp ecific LL configurations and to easily deploy the KPI 
visualisation system in the LLs, by focusing on the following aspects: micro-service-oriented architecture / micro-
services orchestration. Setup, configure and deploy the system in the LL pre -trials to ensure proper operation, 
concept verification and usability testing. Test procedures description and acceptance tests execution to verify 
proper functioning of all developed components  will also be provided . In this task, an evaluation of the 
performance capabilities of the KPI visualisation system will be conducted after every implementation cycle, based 
on the outcomes of deliverables D4. 3-D7.3 in order to perform potential incremental improvements  in the 
functionality and performance of the KPI visualisation system. 
 
Role of main partners: APPART will lead WP3, overseeing also the design, development and integration of the 
KPI visualisation system with the ICT -17 facilities, supported primarily by EBOS, WIT, IBM and LMI  and for

Objectives  
• To setup the test environment and perform the relevant planning and LL operational management for Industry 
4.0 field trials. 
• To conduct advanced field trials in the vertical sector of Factories of the Future to  validate the technological 
and business performance of use cases over 5G.  
• To use the test results and data, to deliver impact analysis and impact assessment reports to systematically

Description of work  
Task 4.1 - LL planning, setup & operational management (IRIS, GLAN, NTNU, OMES, PBGS, TNOR) 
This is the management and monitoring task whose objective is to provide the test -bench to the stakeholders, so 
as to be able to demonstrate through actual field trials that the underlying 5G ICT -17 facilities are capable of 
supporting the stringent KPI requirements needed for the successful delivery of innovative vertical services that 
require 5G performance capabilities. The process in developing the LLs and their use cases, will be agile, so that 
a constant interaction cycle of progress will be delivering the results incrementally as services. To this end, the 
LLs will be following the Deming Plan – Do – Check – Act cycle. There will be a constant interplay between the 
LLs’ progress and the research developments. Provide the overall planning as well as the setup activities for the 
deployment and testing of the use cases  in this Living Lab (LL) . Prepare the evaluation of the LL, including 
indications on the baseline conditions (in  terms of criteria for defining the sample), relevant assumptions to be 
considered (if any), workflow, checklists and templates, reference/target KPIs to be met/benchmarked according 
to deliverable D1.1, and key roles and interactions within this process. Particular attention will be dedicated to the 
planning phase by defining a Gantt chart of the expected tests, analysis and feedbacks loops before the final 
delivery of the evidences form the LLs. Once this procedure will be structured, and before actually implementing 
it, it will be presented to and validated with all relevant partners in order to check its feasibility and maximize its 
efficiency. 
This task includes also the monitoring phase, which will allow the project staff to take stock of relevant data, define 
datasets for impact analysis, process collect measurements, and organize outcomes into actionable information. 
The results generated will be compared to the reference target KPIs to assess the performance of the 5G network, 
provide feedback for refinements and, eventually, final recommendations, which will be fed to the evaluation and 
lessons learned tasks. The leader of this task will also monitor the implementation progress of the execution of the 
use cases, in coordination with the LL leaders and the WP1, WP2 and WP3 leaders to guarantee the compliance 
with the project objectives.

G                Page  77  
Task 4.2 - LL1 execution: Factories of the Future (IRIS, GLAN, NTNU, OMES, PBGS, TNOR, YARA) 
The focus of LL1 is to organise and perform a set of use cases, outlined in Section 1.3.4 through an agile-based 
iterative process. The LL1 vertical will validate KPIs from representative use cases, which have been identified by 
the 5G-PPP community and the 5G -SOLUTIONS consortium vertical partners as important for the stakeholders 
of the Factories of the Future industry. The use cases will be performed within the factory facilities of our process 
industry participants (PGBS in Belgium and  GLAN in Ireland) using new portable 5G nodes having integrated 
core and RAN functionality, which will be installed within the factories by UOP and serve as standalone private 
5G networks. An additional 5G node will be installed in Norway to enable the execution of UC1.5. This is critical 
to enable the execution of realistic scenarios capturing and measuring the stringent requirements related to  real-
time latency. Also, the interfaces between transceivers and sensors for wireless communication within the factories 
will be developed. The execution of all Living Labs including this one will be performed over 3 iterative cycles, 
each spanning over a period of 6 months to ensure appropriate tes ting and validation is conducted in a 
comprehensive manner per 3GPP release. In this respect, great attention has been provided to align the validation 
of the use cases with the corresponding upgrades of the ICT -17 5G-VINNI Norway and the portable private 5G 
nodes facilities brought by UOP (part of 5G-VINNI consortium). Specifically, field trials will be conducted over 
3GPP Rel. 15, Rel. 16 and also Rel.17 in case the latter release would be made available by Q3 2021. 
 
Task 4.3 - Performance evaluation and lessons learned (IRIS, GLAN, IREN, NTNU, OMES, PBGS, TNOR, 
YARA) The purpose of this task can be briefly described from the following three aspects. First of all, the 
performance of each use case will be evaluated, particularly from the KPI perspective to illustrate how current 5G 
capabilities can be leveraged for different applications in each use case. Secondly, according to the results received 
from each use case in every agile-based iteration, provide requirements and sugge stions to further improve both 
functional and non-functional capabilities of 5G facilities. Following that, each use case will be further evaluated 
to reflect the latest improvement of the 5G infrastructure from the application perspective.  This task will also 
provide and establish systematic feedback loops to WP1-WP3, for continuous refinement. Results will be analysed 
both quantitively and quantifiably. Conclusions and recommendations will be drawn including recommendations 
for further trial validations. When possible, the impact of 5G deployment will be also analysed so to potentially 
allow operators to evaluate their 5G network deployment scope, pattern and duration. Throughout the validation 
testing period, knowledge and findings will be documented in deliverable D4.3 together with evaluation reporting 
and impact assessment for the LL, and extracting lessons learned for internal dissemination among the consortium, 
capacity building and external dissemination as appropriate. 
 
Role of main partners: IRIS will lead WP 4, overseeing the validation of the use cases in the Factories of the 
Future vertical, as well as the evaluation and lessons learned, supported by the industrial FoF partners.   
 
Justification of resources:  IRIS will assign resources equivalent to 2 full-time persons in WP4 over a 2 -year 
period (i.e. 1 2PM/person/year), supported primarily by GLAN, NTNU, OMES, PBGS (0.6 FTE person 
@7PM/year). 
 
Deliverables

The deliverables (initial and final versions)  contain the implementation and testing plan for the operation  of all 
Living Labs, updated at the end of each iterative testing cycle period, providing reporting on progress made.

M34] Actual field trials of all Living Labs, repeated over 3 iterative testing cycles, one per 3GPP release.

containing a critical evaluation and findings from the LLs, lessons learned, the degree the KPIs have been met and 
suggestions for improvements.

Objectives  
• To setup the test environment and perform the relevant planning and LL operational management for the Smart 
Urban Environment cluster. 
• To design and implement the Living Lab specific software and hardware upgrades needed to execute the Smart 
Energy, Smart Cities and Smart Ports use cases enabled by 5G communication technology. 
• To conduct advanced field trials in the vertical sectors of Smart Energy, S mart Cities and Smart Port s to 
validate the technological and business performance of use cases over 5G.  
• To use the test results and data, to deliver impact analysis and impact assessment reports to systematically 
address the LL stakeholder perspectives. 
 
Description of work  
Task 5.1 - LL planning, setup, operational management and evaluation ( A2T, ENEL, IBM, IREN, NURO, 
TNOR, YARA): Similar to task T4.1. 
 
Task 5.2 - LL2 execution: Smart Energy (A2T, ENEL, IREN) 
The activities envisioned in this task are similar to those in task T4.2, but adjusted to reflect the specificities of the 
Smart Energy Living Lab. At first, an in -depth analysis of the use cases and the related functional requirements 
proposed in WP1 will  be performed, with the aim of identifying the needed LL -specific control functionalities, 
establish a reference control architecture and define use case specific sequence diagrams. Following that, two 
parallel activities will be performed: (i) the control  algorithms enabling the execution of the use cases will be 
designed and preliminary tested in a simulation environment; (ii) the technical specifications characteri sing the 
communication interfaces among LL-specific control architecture components will be defined. Based on that, new 
software modules characteri sing the technical solution will be implemented and all hardware installations and 
upgrades needed to execute the demonstration will be performed. Then the demonstration activities will be 
undertaken, according to the test cases and the related planning established in Task 5.1. The use cases will be 
demonstrated in the 5G-EVE Turin ICT-17 facility, relying on ENEL, IREN and TIM equipment . This task also 
covers the fusing of the dedicated Energy equipment to be used with the 5G-EVE Turin facility to ensure proper 
communication operation. A2T will engage a linked 3rd party (CRAT, as explained in Section 4) to partly support 
them in the project. Specifically, CRAT will provide contributions in the design and simulation of extended control 
strategies for active demand and electric vehicles smart charging.  In addition, ENEL will subcontract part of its 
work (~20%) that cannot be fully undertaken by ENEL (e.g. statistical analysis in data analysis/post-processing). 
 
Task 5.3 - LL3 execution: Smart Cities & Ports (IBM, NURO, TNOR, YARA) 
The main objective of this task is to plan, design and conduct a set of six use cases as outlined in Section 1.3.4.1 
by using an agile -based iterative process. The Smart Cities & Ports  vertical will validate KPIs from the six use 
cases of interest, which h ave been identified by the 5G -PPP community and the 5G -SOLUTIONS partners as 
important for the stakeholders of the Smart Cities & Ports industry. In particular, the initial iterations will allow 
the stakeholders to perform an initial validation of the KPIs, and the subsequent ones will perform a more critical 
validation and to draw up recommendations, that will be documented and disseminated. The field trials for all use 
cases apart from UC3.4  will be conducted in 5G -VINNI Norway. UC3.4 will be conducted in  IBM technology 
campus in Dublin through a localised RAN station, encompassing gNB and MEC functionalities, provided , 
installed and configured onsite by partner UOP. This node will be interconnected with the 5G -VINNI Patra core 
facility via the GEANT network. All use cases will be performed in a complementary and mutually supportive 
manner to optimally use all the available capabilities and expertise to ensure technical and operational excellence 
for all partners. The performance of each use case will be measured in detail and benchmarked according to the 
pre-defined target KPIs.  
 
Task 5.4 - Performance evaluation and lessons learned (IBM, A2T, ENEL, IREN, NTNU, NURO, TNOR, 
YARA): Similar to task T4.4. 
 
Role of main partners: IBM will lead WP5, overseeing the validation of the use cases in the Smart Energy, Smart 
Cities and Smart Ports verticals, as well as the evaluation and lessons learned, supported primarily by A2T for the 
planning and operational management of the Living Lab and the vertical partners (ENEL, NURO, IREN, YARA).   
 
Justification of resources: IBM will assign resources equivalent to 1.7 full-time persons in WP5 over a 2-year 
period (i.e. 20PM/year), supported by  A2T (1.5 FTE person @18PM/year), ENEL (1.25  FTE person 
@15PM/year), NURO (1.2 FTE person @14PM/year), IREN (0.9 FTE person @11PM/year) and YARA (0.6 FTE 
person @7.5PM/year).

Objectives  
• To setup the test environment and perform the relevant planning and LL operational management for the multi-
vertical concurrent services usage Multi Living Lab. 
• To conduct advanced field trials in a combined, parallel and concurrent manner of those use cases from LL1-
LL4 whose target KPI requirements fall under eMBB, mMTC and/or URLLC classes of s ervice, to validate 
the technological and business performance of 5G and to prove that no performance degradation occurs.  
• To use the test results and data, to deliver impact analysis and impact assessment reports to systematically 
address the LL stakeholder perspectives. 
 
Description of work 
Task 7.1 - LL planning, setup, operational management and evaluation (TNOR, TIM, IBM, IRIS, IREN, 
LIVEU): Similar to task T4.1. 
 
Task 7.2 – MLL execution: Concurrent validation of eMBB, mMTC & URLLC service classes from LL1-
LL4 (IRIS, all)  
The main objective of this task is to conduct  concurrently field trials from a combination of UCs from LL1 -LL4 
as illustrated in Table 1.6, which  are grouped over the separate classes of ITU requirements, i.e. eMBB, mMTC 
and URLLC. The purpose is  to demonstrate and capture evidence through the relevant performance KPIs that 
slicing and virtualisation are (i) capable of successfully managing multi-domain resources, (ii) are in line with such 
concurrent performance requirements and (iii) that there is no interference between vertical use cases in the 
presence of concurrent usage of resources. The use cases will be executed in the same ICT-17 facilities as in LL1-
LL4. The performance of each use case will be measured in detail and benchmarked according to the pre-defined 
target KPIs.  
 
Task 7.3 - Performance evaluation and lessons learned (TNOR, all): Similar to task T4.4.  
 
Role of main partners: TNOR will lead WP7, overseeing the planning and operational management of the MLL, 
as well as the evaluation and lessons learned, supported primarily by IRIS for the validation of the concurrent use 
cases in all verticals. 
 
Justification of resources: TNOR and IRIS will assign resources equivalent to 0.4 full-time persons in WP7 over 
a 2-year period (i.e. 4.5PM/year), supported by all consortium members with an effort of 1-3PM/year each to have 
a collective understanding of the findings.
