Objectives  
• To assess market opportunities, to monitor the technological landscape and to develop viable business plans 
for targeted cluster groups of applications that can be delivered to the market as a commercial service. 
• To make impactful contributions towards standardisation bodies. 
• To identify and manage innovation from the project , to develop the Data Management Plan and to develop 
and implement the Intellectual Property Rights (IPR) strategy. 
 
Description of work 
Task 8.1 - Market assessment and technology monitoring (NURO, TIM, NOKIA, A2T, CEL, EBOS, ENEL, 
IBM, ILS, IREN, IRIS, LIVEU, LMI) 
All involved members will perform a continuous market and research watch in order to identify and verify that the 
use cases to be trialled are indeed the most relevant having the highest commercialisation interest and potential 
amongst the targeted vertica l industries. This task will undertake a market survey assessment to understand the 
This proposal version was submitted by Frini LAZAROU on 14/11/2018 13:54:55 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
G                Page  81  
sectoral needs and opportunities for 5G -SOLUTIONS, with an initial focus on telecoms and SMEs. The market 
analysis will include a SWOT analysis, trend analysis and, where a ppropriate, develop tactical and strategic 
responses, informing its commercialisation plan in task T8.2. It will also seek to understand well how 5G -
SOLUTIONS compares and contrasts to other solutions being developed within the market, to define a market 
position and unique value propositions for the solution.   
 
Task 8.2 - Business, marketing plan and sustainability (ILS, A2T, CEL, ENEL, IBM, IREN, IRIS, LIVEU, 
NURO, TNOR) 
This task has two strands. The first strand will deliver a comprehensive business focused (as opposed to 
technology) assessment of the most immediate and realistic market opportunities for 5G vertical applications. The 
detailed market assessment conducted in task T8.1 combined with the evaluation and lessons learn ed from the 
Living Labs will identify those use cases that have the highest commercialisation potential. Based on the output 
of the first strand, the 5G-SOLUTIONS use cases will be consolidated into 3 targeted cluster groups of applications 
(i.e. Industry 4.0, Smart urban environment and Enhanced user experience) that can be delivered to the market as 
bundled commercial services. Each commercial service will have a lead commercialisation partner who will own 
the execution of the business development plan that is created within 5G -SOLUTIONS.  The commercialisation 
owners are A2T for the Smart Energy, IBM for the Smart Cities & Smart Ports, IRIS for Factories of the Future 
and LIVEU for Media & Entertainment. ILS will provide the industry and commercial knowle dge to lead the 
commercialisation partners in creating viable business plan s for each of the targeted areas that identifies the 
specific market opportunity, the financial model, operational model and initial go-to-market steps. Business model 
analysis will be performed and enable recommendations on the preferred business structure. 
 
Task 8.3 Standardisation (IRT, TIM, NOKIA, CTTC, NURO, TNOR, WIT)  
5G-SOLUTIONS will use standardi sation as a means to exploit the impacts of the project result and to most 
efficiently invest the public funding of this project. It will go about this in two ways: Firstly, it will ensure that the 
research results produced by the project will be aligned wi th existing and emerging standards from the relevant 
standardisation bodies (e.g. 3GPP, ETSI, ITU, IEEE, IETF, etc ). Secondly, through 5G-PPP pre-standardisation 
Working Group and contributing to the 2nd phase of 5G standardisation efforts, 5G-SOLUTIONS will analyse the 
standardisation gaps with respect to the 5G-PPP vision so that such gaps can be adequately addressed. In particular, 
the consortium will provide feedback to the standardisation process by providing experiences, lessons learned, and 
research results, relevant to the overall 5G architecture, network softwarisation and slicing, network management, 
use cases and key requirements , as indicatively listed in Table 2.9 in Section 2.2.2. The following planning 
activities are foreseen: 
• A dedicated standardisation action plan, identifying relevant standardisation and regulatory bodies.  
• A roadmap of relevant standardisation and regulatory bodies (3GPP, ETSI, ITU, IEEE, IETF, etc.) and topics 
for 5G, including evaluating existing roadmaps at international  level; influencing pre-standardisation on 5G 
and related R&D, recommending which outcomes should be standard ised; joint actions with international 
fora, such as, ONF, GSMA, TMN, Broadband Forum, NGMN, OneM2M, etc. 
• Setting up the standardi sation activity roadmap by M8 and continue the updating of this roadmap based on 
the project’s work progress and in conjunction with the SDOs progress. 
• Coordinating the project and standardi sation groups through constant monitoring of activities and regular 
conference calls with standardisation experts.  
• Seizing opportunities to push technology contributions into ongoing specifications. 
• Coordinating with standardisation experts to draft contributions ahead of standard meetings. 
• Continuously promoting the project at standardisation-related workshops, panels, and summits.  
• Contribution to 5G-PPP pre-standards WG with at least two (2) white papers based on the experiences in the 
validation of the use cases over the 5G technologies and addressing gaps with respect to 5G-PPP vision.  
 
Task 8.4 – Innovation, data management and IPR activities (ILS, APPART, EBOS) 
This task will determine how innovation and research data will be handled during the project and describe what 
data will be collected, processed or generated, what methodologies and standards will be followed, whether and 
how this data will be shared and/or made open, and how it will be curated and preserved, with emphasis on ensuring 
GDPR compliance. 
Innovation management [ILS]: Identify and manage i nnovation from the project, advising the P C and P M and 
partners on the scope and potential of the innovations arising and paying attention to discerning IPR at regular 
checkpoints. The work also includes identifying, assisting and overseeing the filing of three (3) strategic patent 
filings, as explained in the joint commercialisation strategy in Section 2.2 .4.2. The Innovation & IPR Manager 
will be supported by an Innovation & Commercialisation Board ( I&CB), as explained in Section 3.2. Work 
includes the monitoring of the progress of development of innovative tools/services throughout the project. 
This proposal version was submitted by Frini LAZAROU on 14/11/2018 13:54:55 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
G                Page  82  
Data Management Plan (DMP) [ILS]: Development of the DMP, which will contain information related to the 
types of data the project will generate and collect, the standards that will be used to represent the data during the 
project and how partners might exploit the data resulting from the project. The DMP will set robust management 
procedures that will protect personal data collected as a result of pro ject activities, as well as client owned data, 
from unauthorised use or sharing, also supporting GDPR compliance. In addition, the DMP will include a data 
protection impact assessment of 5G-SOLUTIONS’s requirements and LLs that will be used to ensure the project 
takes a data protection-by-design approach. The DMP will be produced at M6 and finalised in M32. The project’s 
Data Protection Officer (DPO) will be available to assist - if needed - in decision-making as 5G-SOLUTIONS is 
developed to identify potential risks, mitigation solutions and support compliance. All partners have appointed 
their own internal DPO who will closely collaborate with the project’s DPO (see Section 4). 
IPR activities [ILS]: This task will cover the management of the main IPR activities taking into consideration the 
specificities of the project and the participants. The task will focus on the identification of the tangible and 
intangible assets that will be required for the project's implementation and for the use of the expected results. All 
IP produced will be monitored and the potential IPR attached to them (e.g. copyright, patent) will be also verified 
and cleared for the project's smooth execution.  Design the IPR protection strategy to promote the sustainability of 
project results, building on existing assets, considering aspects defined in Section 2.2. This strategy will be used 
as a valuable tool for managing and documenting any activity regarding the potential IPRs of the project's outcomes 
during its lifecycle and the integration of possible technical advances in their way of becoming marketable products 
and services. Establish IPR management procedures and associated activities. Conduct a search on the prior -art 
for potential inventions, trademarks and other IPRs when necessary and evaluate the costs for potential Intellectual 
Property protection. Monitor the project from the IPR point of view so that confidentiality agreements and all the 
partners’ defined IPRs (foreground and background) in the Consortium Agreement are fully respected.  
 
Task 8.5 - Clustering plan and activities for international cooperation and exchange of results (TNOR, TIM, 
NOKIA, CTTC, IRT, LMI, UOP, PIIU, WIT) 
This task will define and prepare a clustering plan with associated activities aiming at promoting the exchange of 
results, sharing knowledge and experience as well as best practices for the emerging 5G services to different 
relevant verticals. It aims to foster cooperation not only between other ICT -19 consortia, but also with other EU 
and international initiatives on 5G services with clusters in the USA, Japan, Korea and China. This direct 
cooperation among relevant 5G actors and vertical industries at an international level will create a sustainable 
meta-cluster that will help to improve even further the results from the field trials so as to promote international 
cooperation and contribute further to global 5G standardisation (leveraging the initiatives from task T8.3). For this 
purpose, consortium members wil l participate in major international 5G events as well as arrange workshops to 
meet with their counterparts outside EU. 
 
Role of main partners: ILS will lead WP8, overseeing the commercialisation, business plan and IPR activities , 
supported primarily by  NURO for the market assessment and technology monitoring, by IRT for the 
standardisation activities, by TNOR for the clustering plan and activities for international cooperation and 
exchange of results, as well as by TIM, CEL & IRIS as major supporting contributors. 
 
Justification of resources: ILS will assign resources equivalent to 1 full-time persons in WP8 over a 33-month 
period (i.e. 12PM/year), supported primarily by NURO (0.5 FTE person @6.5PM/year), TIM (0.3 FTE person 
@4PM/year), CEL, IRT and IRIS (0.25 FTE person @3PM/year). 
 
Deliverables 
D8.1A-B Market assessment & technology monitoring (ILS) [M7, M33]: Interim (v1.0) and final (v2.0) report 
detailing the business opportunities and barriers for 5G vertical applications providing a roadmap for all future 5G 
applications development. 
D8.2: Business development plan (ILS) [M33]: A business development plan for vertical sectors consolidated 
from the industry 4.0, smart urban environment and enhanced user experience clusters. 
D8.3A-B: Standardisation activities (IRT) [M8, M32]: Initial (v1.0) and final (v2.0) version of reports covering 
actions with standardisation experts based on a defined standardisation roadmap. 
D8.4A-B: Data Management Plan (ILS) [M6, M32]: The deliverable contains the initial (by M6) and final DMP.  
D8.5: Data Management report (ILS) [M32]: The deliverable contains the data management report. 
D8.6: Innovation and IP protection report (ILS) [M33]: The deliverable consists of the Innovation management 
plan and the IP protection report with the patent activities. 
D8.7A-B: Clustering plan for international cooperation and sharing of results (TNOR) [M10, M33]: Initial 
(v1.0) and final (v2.0) version of reports containing the clustering plan activities.

Description of work 
Task 9.1 - Dissemination and communication activities (CTTC, all partners)  
Implement the dissemination of the project goals, software products, reports, results, achievements, and other 
outputs. The target audiences will be identified, ranging from general public through scientific and academic 
communities up to specific 5G stake holders and market actors. The dissemination and communication channels 
and actions as defined in Section 2.2.1 will serve as a baseline to achieve the goals in this task. 
Dissemination of publications and white papers [CTTC]: Along the project, the 5G-SOLUTIONS partners will be 
involved in the preparation and publication of articles in scientific journals, peer-reviewed conferences, and books. 
The approved publications will be available in the internal document repository of the consortium, and those with 
appropriate copyright permissions will be publicly available through the project’s website.  
Joint dissemination actions and events [CTTC]: The project’s intermediate results will also be presented in form 
of white papers, presentations and online demos in various conferences and industrial/commercial exhibitions (e.g.  
MWC, Global 5G events, ITS Congress, EuCNC) with the purpose of commercially exploiting 5G-SOLUTIONS 
results and identifying new partners for collaboration in the EU market. At the end of the project, the task leader 
will organize the final project workshop gathering both local and international participants. To further amplify the 
potential of the initiative, the following options will be considered: (i) joint or ganisation with other relevant 5G-
PPP projects, (ii) co -hosting in the framework of other well -established events, (iii) organi sation of a dialogue 
session with other 5G stakeholders, (iv) cooperation of 5G -SOLUTIONS stakeholders with 5G -PPP Working 
Groups and mapping of results.   
Communication media [CTTC]: Ensure the creation and constant update of all web-based communication means, 
including the project’s website (from M1  by EBOS), as outlined in Section 2.2.1.2. Participants will also ensure 
visibility of the project activities through a number of traditional and electronic dissemination material edited 
electronically and sent out to a large pool of stakeholders (Table 2.5) on a quarterly basis.  
Implement the communication plan of the project and its associated activities and create a set of documents and 
tools, which can be shared with consortium partners in order to communicate the project’s goals and outcomes. 
Relevant activities include: (i) create and publish visual representations (infographics) of information, data or 
knowledge intended to present complex information quickly and clearly; (ii) provide effective support to 
dissemination and exploitation activities, whils t ensuring effective and appropriate communication towards 
various stakeholders, (iii) foster community building and realize impact on industry and research in Europe and 
worldwide, (iv) gather feedback from relevant stakeholders through networking activit ies, and (v) monitor and 
evaluate communication and dissemination activities. 
Development of the communication plan  [CTTC]: Development of the communication plan, which will 
incorporate innovative methods for sharing information with the public and interested stakeholders, in accordance 
with the dissemination strategy. 
 
Task 9.2 – Involvement of SMEs (A2T, APPART, EBOS, IRIS, PIIU)  
The overall aim of 5G-SOLUTIONS is to accelerate the European ICT ecosystem by creating and supporting new 
businesses by unlocking the commercial potential of high -value solutions. The aim of SME involvement is to 
onboard innovative companies fitting innov ations and knowledge skills developed by 5G -SOLUTIONS 
consortium. In line with the stakeholders’ engagement and community building strategy, this task will identify the 
right stakeholders in order to reach the most relevant SMEs and research institutes (Section 2.1.3.1). This task will 
organize three specific prizes for third parties (non -partners of the consortium: especially SMEs and spin -off of 
This proposal version was submitted by Frini LAZAROU on 14/11/2018 13:54:55 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
G                Page  84  
research institutes) who are willing to contribute to the project with new components in order to address new u se 
cases. After an online application, the best ideas to exploit 5G -SOLUTIONS results (Calls for Ideas) will be 
selected. The winners will receive a prize of €10.000 each, together with technical and business support from the 
main industrial partners of th e project. 5G-SOLUTIONS plans to offer a total of 3 prizes with a total  budget of 
€30.000 (planned in A2T resources, see Section 3.4). Detailed information regarding the SMEs related KPIs can 
be found in Section 2.1.3.1). 
This task aims at preparing the in formation package for the SMEs, managing the online application and the 
selection procedures for prizes, identifying the objectives and defining the guidelines, the terms and references of 
the selection procedure, for the submission of the proposals and fo r their evaluation. Considering the evaluation 
of the jury of external experts, the highest scored proposals will be selected for the prizes. Moreover, the 
participation of additional experts and the online application will be continuously monitored, and the lessons 
learned will provide inputs for the overall analysis and for future similar initiatives. Specific attention will be given 
to IPR issues. These initiatives will be launched and published in M24 and will be open for two months.  
 
Task 9.3 - Community Building (PIIU, TIM, NOKIA, CTTC, LMI, TNOR, WIT) 
Establishment and coordination of EAB [PIIU]: Establish the 5G-SOLUTIONS External Advisory Board (EAB) 
to support and direct the promotion activities of the project.  The members of the EAB will participate in the 
exploitation and innovation activities, providing input towards adoption and take -up actions. EAB members will 
participate in 4 out of the 8 project  meetings in order to collect their feedback and suggestions and to organize 
industrial workshops and panels. The interactions with the EAB are expected to be threefold: (i)  in the form of 
collection of requirements from different vertical industries, (ii) in the form of technical and strategic meetings to 
discuss design matters and use cases and (iii) in the form of presentation of main results validation from the trials.  
Policy recommendations & coordination with existing 5G -PPP Working Groups [PIIU]: Based on the project’s 
results create policy briefs. Given that within the 5G -PPP there are a number of cross -project Working Groups 
(WGs), in which shared issues and outputs of several projects are identified, 5G -SOLUTIONS will have 
representatives from partners, participating in the 5G -PPP Steering Board (TIM) and Technical Boards (TNOR) 
(see Section 3.2, ‘Commitment of 5G-SOLUTIONS to 5G-PPP program level’) as well as in 5G-PPP WGs that are 
relevant to the project in order to contribute through white papers and workshops. This participation would include 
contacts and coordination with at least the following WGs: Pre -Standardisation, 5G Architecture, SDN/NFV, 
Network management & QoS, Trials, SME and Security, including 5G-IA. 
 
Task 9.4 - Transferability and trainings (CTTC, CEL, FNET, LMI, PIIU) 
Leverage the collective 5G-SOLUTIONS consortium’s work and build a transferability framework, which will be 
fed with the experiences and lessons learned from the LLs  (deliverables D4.2 -D7.2), thus enabling the 
identification of best practices for the rollo ut of new 5G applications , guidelines, best practices, methodologies 
and other potential solutions beyond the project completion, thus leveraging EU’s funding. 5G-SOLUTIONS will 
organise trainings aiming to support 5G network stakeholders across Europe, ma ximising the use and impact of 
the project’s outputs. It will be used to provide the opportunity for hands -on experience on how to use its KPI 
visualisation system to conduct innovative use case validation. Training s will be offered through workshops, 
webinars, online documentation and community mailing lists. Training supports and facilitates academic and 
international collaboration and helps the adoption of 5G -SOLUTIONS results in particular in open source 
communities (e.g. OpenAirInterface). Training will aim at keeping participants’ knowledge and capabilities sharp 
during and after the project. Therefore, training activities include:  
• Agreeing on a concrete methodology for the design of the training programmes.  
• Developing “dynamic” online courses in a flexible and modular format so that they can be updated.  
• Developing an official enrolment process, controlled by a secure authorisation system.  
• Developing a competencies matrix and credit system for all courses, linked to on-line assessment activities, to 
allow certification (and periodical re-certification) of participants.  
• Setting up workshops and online hands-on training labs  (as an integral part of the curricula), to allow 
experimentation and piloting with the 5G -SOLUTIONS KPI visualisation system and services on test use 
cases, amplifying the opportunities to learn, develop, and apply the new skills.  
• Creating a trusted community of knowledge exchange to encourage the interactive sharing of knowledge and 
best practices between participants. 
 
Role of main partners: CTTC will lead WP9, overseeing the dissemination, communication and capacity building 
activities, supported primarily by A2T for the involvement of SMEs, as well as by PIIU for the community building 
activities.

Objectives  
• To coordinate all activities in the project and ensure that partners work together effectively. 
• To ensure the project meets its contractual commitments (deliverables, quality, etc.). 
• To f acilitate the scientific and research success of the project through careful monitoring of progress, 
management of resources and coordination of activities. 
 
Description of work 
Task 10.1 - Project Coordination (TIM) 
This task will be the responsibility of the Project Manager (PM) and includes all the general management 
responsibility. By its nature, the management of RIA demands the application of mechanisms to guarantee a 
maximum grade of flexibility, whilst maintaining coherence and focus on the objectives. The PM will be supported 
by the Project Management Board. The PM will manage the cooperation with other 5G -PPP projects, relevant 
projects and participation to the 5G-PPP WGs. An Activity Report will be produced in two periods (M20 & M36) 
containing a management -level overview of the activities carried out (a description of progress toward the 
scientific and technological objectives, a description of progress toward the milestones and deliverables), 
identification of problems encountered during the project and actions taken to resolve them. 
 
Task 10.2 - Administration and resources management (TIM, EBOS, ILS, IRIS)  
This task will provide support for financial matters and project administration activities. An administration office 
created under the coordinator will support the PM to plan all project’s resources and be in charge of the day -to-
day support to partners for administrative, procedural and legal matters. This task consists of the following: 
• Resource planning and monitoring against 5G-SOLUTIONS deliveries and advancements; 
• Preparation and management of the planned project meetings; 
• Day by day administrative support to partners and financial consultancy to partners; 
• Coordination of reporting of the administrative activities. 
 
Task 10.3 - Technical Management (TNOR, NOKIA, APPART, EBOS, LMI) 
Execution of overall technical management of the project including: (a) Monitoring of the technical progress of 
the project according to the contractual schedule, (b) Liaise with EAB on technical matters, (c) Monitor the 
This proposal version was submitted by Frini LAZAROU on 14/11/2018 13:54:55 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
G                Page  86  
preparation of technical deliverables, (d) Provide an internal platform for information exchange between project 
partners, (e) Handle issues like knowledge management, and (f) Prepare technical project reviews. Apart from the 
Technical Manager ( TNOR) W P1-WP3 technical leaders as well as  EBOS as a technological task leader will 
support the technical management and have been assigned effort under this task. 
 
Task 10.4 - Quality Assurance and Risk Management (EBOS) 
Quality assurance [EBOS]: Implementation of quality assurance procedures with particular focus on monitoring 
review activities built into the work programme and submitting quality review reports. A quality plan within the 
Project Quality Handbook (deliverable D10.3) will specify the quality procedures, internal and external peer 
reviews, control, monitoring and reporting activities to be implemented in the project to ensure that satisfactory 
quality standards are met. 
Risks management [EBOS]: Implementation of the plan including the  risk library (>100 risks), processes and 
procedures for risk management and reporting to be performed by all partners in each project work package, 
covering both the project operational risks and the framework level barriers/risks. Monitor the progress to ensure 
that proactive measures are taken to mitigate risks which could jeopardise the planned project outcomes. Monitor 
the risks outlined in Section 3.2 related to the updating of the Risk Management Framework. This task will produce 
the plan (by M3, consolidated in deliverable D10.3) and will conduct quality management through the project. 
 
Task 10.5 - Legal and Ethics (CEL)  
This task will investigate, design and monitor all the procedures and protocols necessary for handling legal and 
ethical issues during the whole project lifetime. The 5G constitutes a formidable challenge from a legal and ethical 
point of view. A hyperconnected society offers to people an extraordinary capacity for augmented access to (and 
related transformation of) the reality. This world-constructive power raises several societal questions on different 
stages of inquiry: from creating a level of awareness in the population applicable to the 5G spread, to the proposal 
of new models of liability, from the review of the idea of trust in the relationships between human beings and 
between human beings and machines, up to the need of rethinking decision-making processes in the light of new 
decentralised governance in which human -discretionary procedures and automated -protocols of technological 
control can coexist. The goal of this task is to try to give a preliminary answer to all these challenges.  This task 
will also manage the ethical issues concerning with the design of the information and consent forms that will be 
used in case of involvement of human beings in the research. It will include the delivery of the ethical and legal 
guidelines early in the project to drive the partners in their research activity.  It will produce the research ethical 
protocol (D10.4) for the project, stipulating the ethical principles that the 5G -SOLUTIONS partners will adhere 
to in their work. CEL will also act as the 5G-SOLUTIONS’s Data Protection Officer (DPO) and will collaborate 
with partners’ assigned Data Privacy Single Point of Contact, supporting them during the research process to 
comply with ethical principles and the legal framework on privacy as well as maintaining track of partners activity 
for what concern local authorities’ notifications and requests for authorisations when needed. Gender balance will 
also be monitored during the course of the grant through this task to ensure that the female/male ratio is maintained 
as close to 1:1 as possible for people employed during its course, highlighting success along the way. 
 
Role of partners: TIM has the overall responsibility for the execution and strategic management of the project , 
implementing the agreed strategy and decisions taken by the project’s committees. TIM is the official contact point 
of the project with the European Commission and, as such, author ised to negotiate on behalf of the consortium.  
TNOR will undertake the project’s Technical Management. EBOS and CEL will undertake the roles of the Quality 
Assurance & Risk Management and Legal & Ethics, respectively. 
 
Justification of resources:  TIM will assign 1 full-time person for 3 7 months (i.e. 12PM/year) for Project 
Management, supported primarily by EBOS in T10.4 and CEL in T10.5 (each 0.4 FTE  person @~5PM/year) as 
well as by TNOR in task T10.3 (0.2 FTE person @2PM/year),

3.2 Management structure, milestones and procedures  
The successful implementation of a collaborative research project, such as 5G-SOLUTIONS, with 26 partners from 
7 EU and 2 associated countries, involved in parallel, requires efficient, well -documented and structured project 
management procedures. Of parti cular importance are the clear distribution of responsibilities and the flow of 
information for building a common technical and commercialisation vision, for reporting progress, controlling the 
deliverables (Table 3.1c), the milestones (Table 3.2a), and managing and mitigating the risks (Table 3.2b). The 5G-
SOLUTIONS project management structure is designed to meet the objectives of all stakeholders, i.e. the European 
Commission and all the consortium partners by creating responsiveness to the evolving needs of the project.  
 
3.2.1 Organisational Structure 
The management structure, as shown in Figure 3.3, consists of: (i) the General Assembly (GeA), (ii) the Project 
Management Board (PMB), and (iii) Work Package (WP) Leaders, all supported by an External Advisory Board 
(EAB), an Ethics panel and an Innovation & Commercialisation Board (I&CB). The management structure has been 
designed to:  
a) Ensure that the project meets its contractual obl igations. This will entail continuous progress monitoring, 
managed by the Project Coordinator, communication and a shared understanding of roles and responsibilities. 
b) Facilitate the delivery of high -quality research and development. Central to achieving th is will be the 
coordination of the activities of the technical partners and the integration of their results. 
c) Maximise, measure and validate the impact of the system on the target audiences, both within and beyond the 
technology enhanced learning research and industry communities. 
 
Figure 3.3: Project Management Structure 
 
The PMB will focus on consortium management issues for the whole project, including technical matters, quality 
assurance, the consortium agreement, roles and responsibilities, audit certificates, ethics, gender issues, societal 
questions and liaison with 5G-PPP and other third parties and the EU. The related management functions, roles and 
procedures are described in detail in the following sections and will form the basis for the Consortium Agreement.  
 
3.2.1.1 Project governance structure 
General Assembly (GeA): Chaired by the Project Coordinator (PC), assembled once a year (i.e. in M1, M12, M24 
and M36). This is the highest decision authority in the consortium, which includes representatives from each and 
every partner, having the authority to make decisions on behalf of their respective organisations in terms of overall 
strategy and contractual aspe cts. The GeA appoints the EAB, Ethics panel and I&CB members and chairs. The 
meeting agenda includes: (a) Report by the Project Manager (PM), (b) Report by the Quality Assurance & Risks 
Manager on quality and risks issues, (c) Reports by the WP Leaders on technical implementation issues, (d) Approval 
of annual and final reports, (e) Approval of yearly implementation plans, and (f) Decisions on specific items. 
 
Project Management Board (PMB): The PMB consists of the managers of the project, as listed in Figure 3.3, brings 
to the project a wealth of experience in coordinating EU projects over many years, and ensures that the project will 
achieve its objectives and satisfy the needs of the consortium, its target stakeholders, and ultimately the end users. To 
achieve this, a clear mandate from the GeA will be provided at the project’s kick-off meeting, assigning non-strategic 
project decisions to the PMB so that day-to-day decisions (e.g. reallocate resources and/or budget to allow for the 
efficient implementation of a task, or when a decision needs to be taken  with short notice) can be taken in a timely 
manner without causing significant delays. The PMB reports to the GeA, is chaired by the Project Coordinator, and 
includes the Project Manager, the Technical Manager, the Innovation & Commercialisation Managers, the  
Dissemination & Communications Manager, the Quality Assurance & Risk Assessment Manager and the Legal & 
Ethics Manager (Figure 3.3). 
 
 
This proposal version was submitted by Frini LAZAROU on 14/11/2018 13:54:55 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
G                Page  89  
Work Package leaders (WP leaders): Produce detailed work plans and progress reports. Guard the timely and 
effective execution of the WP work and that deliverables meet the quality standards.  Control and monitor activities 
of tasks and regularly communicate, as needed, with task leaders.  M anage the information flow with other WPs, 
monitor the WP plan and maintain consistency with the project plan . Review WP results and flag up any 
underperformance. Provide input to management reports. Represent the WP at the PMB. 
 
3.2.1.2 Support bodies to the governance structure 
External Advisory Board (EAB):  The EAB comprises a well -balanced group of external “advisors” drawn from 
across Europe and embracing a range of knowledge of the project’s focus areas The EAB will offer impartial external 
advice from technological, scientific, market, regulation, ethical, societal, economic and business points of view. The 
consortium seeks to validate its technology direction with the EAB. It will be chaired by one of its members, elected 
upon the EAB’s first meeting in M6. The EAB will be consulted on occasion, and will be convened at a project meeting 
(in M6, M12, M24 & M36) to present 5G-SOLUTIONS’ progress, decisions and designs, to hear their opinion. The 
consortium will take such feedback into account to correct if necessary, or to consider relevant aspects indicated by 
the EAB. The EAB will be presented with a Terms of Reference description of the EAB role.  The consortium will 
cover EAB travel expenses to project meetings. The following persons, whose CVs are presented in Annex 1 (Section 
4), have explicitly confirmed their interest in and willingness to participate in 5G-SOLUTIONS EAB: 
1. Ms. Delphine Bernet-Travert (F), Secretary General, Independent Regulators Group, Brussels, Belgium. 
2. Ms. Afrodite Sevasti (F), Chief Technology Officer, GRNET, Athens, Greece. 
3. Prof. Nicola Blefari Melazzi (M), Director CNIT, Parma, Italy. 
4. Mr. Moisès Morató Güell (M), Energy Depart. Coordinator, Agencia d’ecologia urbana de Barcelona, Spain 
 
Letters of Support for the EAB members listed above are provided in Annex 2 (Section 4).  
 
Ethics Panel: Chaired by the Legal & Ethics Manager and includes legal advisors of t he participating members 
(experts on ethics, privacy and legal issues). An external expert will be invited to the panel, to act as independent 
reviewer and consultant to ensure decisions taken can be generalised and adopted by wider audiences. 
 
5G-PPP Community: See following Sections 3.2.1.4 and 3.2.1.5. 
 
Innovation & Commercialisation Board (I&CB) : Chaired by  the IM and includes a member from each partner 
organisation engaged in the development of the technological enablers and in the Living Labs. Their role is to specify 
in detail the commercialisation strategy and implement the process for filing patents.

3.2.1.4 Commitment of 5G-SOLUTIONS to 5G-PPP program level  
As recommended by the 5G -Infrastructure PPP working structure suggestion 92, 5G -SOLUTIONS consortium is 
aware of the contractual commitment of the 5G-PPP, as well as the organisational structure as described in the 5G-
PPP contract and its technical annex. In particular, it acknowledges the roles and commitments of the European 
Commission, the PPP partnership board, the Networld2020 ETP 93, the 5G Infrastructure Association, the Industry 
Advisory Group and commits to constructive interactions with these bodies. The proposal commits to work with its 
peer 5G -PPP projects as required under the complementary Grant Agreement clause 41.4 of the 5G -PPP grant 
agreement. This includes at least the following contributions:  
▪ Appointment of a Steering Board (SB) mandated representative (i.e. Mr. Maurizio CECCHI (TIM) who will 
act as the 5G-SOLUTIONS Project Coordinator) and full participation in the SB activities.  
▪ Appointment of a deputy SB member (Mr. Valerio PALESTINI (TIM) who will act as the 5G-SOLUTIONS 
Project Manager) to ensure the project is always represented.  
                                                 
92 https://5g-ppp.eu/wp-content/uploads/2016/04/5G-PPP-Phase-3-Working-Structure-Proposal-and-Recommendations-Version-1-0.pdf   
93 http://networld2020.eu/   
member, reports to GeA. 
Tasks:  In strong Collaboration with PM, CM, IM, WP2 & WP3 leaders and the EAB, align technical direction with 
innovation strategies and establish and maintain the 5G-SOLUTIONS design specification and solution. Monitor the 
preparation of technical deliverables. Identify trends and technologies relevant to the project.  
Quality assurance & Risk Manager (QRM):  Dr. Loizos CHRISTOFI (EBOS) 
Role:  Dr. Loizos Christofi will guide and monitor the quality plan and assess the project’s risks. Ensures high-quality 
deliverables and fully tested and reliable software systems. Quality reviews chair. PMB member, reports to GeA.

of Reference (ToR) document. The mandate of a WG is approved by the SB based on the ToR. Changes to WGs will 
be based on the SB approval of updated ToR documents.  
 
Meetings of all boards and groups will be a mixture of face to face and audio/online conferences as required. 
 
3.2.1.5 Mandate of the 5G-PPP level boards that the 5G-SOLUTIONS project will support:  
The following responsibilities are indicat ive of the shared responsibility for the programme achievements that 5G -
SOLUTIONS will contribute to. It is fully understood by the 5G -SOLUTIONS consortium that, while the Grant 
Agreements (GA) are contracts at project level, success may be evaluated in th e program context. So, under the 
complementary GA clause 41.4, this programme level responsibility is understood as part of the project undertaking. 
 
The Steering Board has the following responsibilities:  
▪ Perform the executive management of the programme.  
▪ Facilitate the effective and efficient collaboration between the projects (including the resolution of conflicts).  
▪ Ensure the global consistency of the programme.  
▪ Assure sharing of information across the projects of the programme.  
▪ Ensure the programme has an effective communications strategy for promoting the results of 5G-PPP.  
▪ Perform self-assessment of the progress of the program towards achieving the program KPIs.  
▪ Initiate activities at program level when necessary.  
▪ Detect and address any risks endangering the functioning of the programme.  
▪ Delegate appropriate work items to the TB or specific WGs. 
 
The Technology Board has the following responsibilities:  
▪ To monitor the technical progress of the work.  
▪ To ensure alignment of the technical work at programme level.  
▪ To consolidate the technical requirements related to the programme.

3.2.1.6 Progress reporting 
Internal (within Consortium): Every beneficiary commits to write bi-annually a management report to the Project 
Coordinator (PC). It will describe the technical and management project work done, listing effective time spent on 
the project, mention difficulties, milestones and deliverables (or contributions to deliverables in case of joint 
deliverables) that have been reached, patents, publications, travel and visits. The PC will be able to track both overall 
budget burn rates, as well as identify potential problems with individual organisations as a result of this report. 
 
External (to EC): The PC will coordinate, consolidate and submit to the EC the interim (M20) and final Activity 
Reports (M36), deliverables and financial statements as required.  
 
3.2.1.7 Project communications and meetings 
The consortium recognises that a vital contributing factor towards the successful management of a project, is effective 
communication. A kick-off meeting is planned in M1. GeA will be assembled once a year (i.e. in M1, M12, M24 & 
M36). Some of GeA meetings and PMB meetings will coincide in time, in which case the day before the GeA 
meeting, PMB members will gather to prepare discussion about possible critical decisions that may be on the agenda 
for the GeA meeting. Additional cross-team, meetings at WP level, and face to face meetings will be organised when 
necessary, and teleconferences will be arranged at much frequent time intervals, as needed. PMB physical project 
meetings will be convened every 4 months in year 1 to boost momentum and every 6 months afterwards, while virtual 
(teleconference) PMB meetings will take place monthly to ensure adherence to the project plan and prompt reaction 
to identified risks. Thus, in total 8 face-to-face PMB meetings (i.e. in M1, M4, M8, M12, M18, M24, M30 and M36) 
are anticipated. TIM will host 6 and EBOS and TNOR will each host 1 project meeting. EAB meetings will occur in 
M4, M12, M24 and M36 coinciding with the relevant GeA meetings. Day to day communications will primarily use 
email and specialised tools for H2020 projects, such as EuresTools. These tools have been specifically designed to 
meet the needs of Horizon 2020 projects and European R&D projects, making project collaboration more effective, 
offering full compliance with EC requirements as well as maximum security and reliability. TIM and CTTC have 
been assigned budget under ‘ other direct costs’ (see Section 3.4) to purchase the licenses for consortium members 
for using EuresTools.  
 
Project mailing lists will also be established (general, administrative and per WP). Contact (email, phone and mail) 
details for all personnel involved in the project will be available on the project’s intranet (i.e. private, secure section 
in project’s website available only to consortium members), where information, ideas and documents will be shared.

3.2.1.8 Consortium Agreement 
A Consortium Agreement (CA) will be concluded between all members of the consortium in advance of the signature 
of the Grant Agreement (GA), thus establishing a clear legal framework for the project. The CA will be based on the 
template published by the “Development of a Simplified Consortium Agreement” (DESCA 2020) group, which is a 
comprehensive, modular CA model specifically designed for ICT projects within the EU Horizon 2020 Programme94. 
The CA will complement the Description of Action (DoA), covering topics that are important for the delivery of the 
project and the management of knowledge between the partners, but are not specific to the consortium’s contract 
with the EC. 
 
3.2.1.9 Decision-making mechanisms and conflict resolution 
In the course of the project, the consortium will have to agree on and develop technical, scientific and commercial 
ideas and specifications. Most decisions about the work to be carried out in the project have been made at proposal 
stage and will be subject to the GA signed with the EC. Decision making will strive for consensus: agreement will 
usually be reached, followed by official confirmation via electronic ma il, letter or agreed written minutes. For 
important issues, the agreement may take the form of a short report that needs to be signed by those responsible for 
decision-making. The most important mechanisms for reaching decisions in a consortium with multip le partners, 
each with their own goals, is shown below. The general principle  will be to try to achieve decisions by informal 
means and consensus, using formal procedures, such as voting, only when essential. 
 
Level Decision mechanism Escalate in case: 
1. Project 
Manager 
Verbal consensus only. 
Meetings and/or audioconferences: as needed No consensus is reached 
2. Project 
Management 
Board 
Verbal consensus. Vote if necessary, decisions taken 
with simple majority. 
Meetings: every 4 months in year 1, twice a year 
afterwards (see Section 3.2.1.7). 
At least one partner insists 
3. General 
Assembly 
Voting is mandatory, decisions taken with simple 
majority. 
Meetings: once a year (see Section 3.2.1.7). 
Intervention by the EC, or legal 
action, is the only escalation 
possible.  
 
Where consensus cannot be reached, conflict resolution procedures will be used. The specific personnel roles and 
committees described above, will resolve and/or implement the necessary actions to respond to c onflict resolution. 
In particular, conflict prevention techniques will be used to avoid problems in decision-making. Should any conflict 
issues arise between parties then they will be resolved according to the following simple process:  
1) They will first be addressed within the relevant WP through discussion chaired by the WP leader.  
2) If this fails, the issue will be presented by the WP leader either to the PM, TM, PBM or the GeA depending 
on the nature of the problem (i.e. administrative, technical or business/strategic).  
3) The relevant board will resolve the issue through a majority vote, with the PC / board chair holding a casting 
vote. The EAB will be consulted in case of a high-level scientific dispute.  
4) Conflicts that cannot be resolved through those principles will be handled according to the dispute resolution 
provision set forth in the CA. 
 
3.2.1.10 Innovation Management  
The EAB will be consulted for continuous review of the innovation progress, being provided with reports at 6-month 
intervals from the GeA, in order to identify new opportunities for innovation, grow the engagement with our industrial 
partners, and seek opportunities for new collaborations. The Innovation & IPR Manager ( Dr. Pat O’Sullivan, ILS) 
will lead this activity. Specific measures to engender an innovation culture within the project will be:  
a) Project meetings will include sessions on emerging technologies/approaches to generate novel ideas for 
innovation and to ensure applied knowledge transfer to our industrial partners, and inform future innovation 
decisions. 
b) In close collaboration with the Commercialisation Manager to foster a commercialisation culture among 
group members to maximise the identification, assessment and execution of opportunities to deliver impact 
from innovation outputs.

3.2.3 Critical Implementation Risks and Mitigation actions (Table 3.2b) 
The scientific and technical risks 
management concerns the implementation of 
the project under the responsibility of the 
QRM in collaboration with the PM, TM, IM 
and WP leaders. The management of risks 
will be part of the regular meetings of the 
PMB. Risks in this project may arise in 
different areas, such as in the technology 
maturity, the availability  of data and 
information, risks related to integration, 
stakeholder and end user engagement buy-in 
and commitment. Based on the experience 
from previous projects, and while in proposal 
phase, we have created a risk management 
plan that covers the following to ensure that 
adverse situations are properly managed 
along the evolution of the project: 
▪ Iterative identification of risks with 
adverse effects or impacts - Contingency 
plan and actions. 
▪ Evaluation, quantification and 
prioritisation (ranking) of the risks, rating 
the probabilities of occurrence (low, 
medium and high), and impact/ significance (low, medium and high). 
▪ Constant vigilance, risk monitoring and control, manage outcomes minimising negative impact.  
▪ Identifying and managing opportunities, due to potential unexpected opportunities that may arise.

Strong dependency analysis. Quality procedures, templates 
and guidelines are key elements for mitigating this risk.  WP 
leaders will carry out d etailed monitoring of tasks, with 
specific attention to the dependencies. EuresTools will be used 
by each partner. If there is a delay with one task, the knock-on 
effects can be quickly checked and contingencies put in place 
to manage time slippage and cost increases.  
This proposal version was submitted by Frini LAZAROU on 14/11/2018 13:54:55 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
G                Page  97
3.3 Consortium as a whole  
3.3.1 Consortium overview  
 
The 5G-SOLUTIONS consortium was formed to 
put together a group of 26 organisations from 9 EU 
and associated countries , as shown in Figure 3.5, 
that complement each other in terms of background 
knowledge, technical competence, capability of 
new knowledge creation, business and market 
experience and expertise in the 5G domain. Section 
4 provides full details of partner profiles. 
 
The consortium consists of 3 main groups of 
partners (some partners may be included in several 
groups) as illustrated in the value chain Figure 3.6, 
highlighting the complementarity and 
interdisciplinarity of the consortium: 
• Group 1 (technology suppliers  & telecom 
operators) leading the work in the technical 
work packages (WP1, WP2, WP3). 
• Group 2 (vertical end-users) leading the work 
in the LLs (WP4-WP7) with support from the 
technology suppliers and telecom operators. 
• Group 3 (ecosystem development partners) 
leading the work in  the commercialisation, IP R and international networking  (WP8), dissemination, 
communication and capacity building (WP9) with contributions by all partners, as well as project and technical 
management, quality assurance, legal and ethics (WP10).  
 
 
 
 
 
   
 
 
 
 
 
 
There is a strong presence of SMEs  (38% of consortium members ) leading a number of tasks especially in the  
technical development, absorbing 37% of the total budget. In addition, 4 out of the 7 managerial roles in the PMB 
are undertaken by SMEs. There is a very high amount of 5G-PPP experience across the consortium, since 50% of 
the consortium members have participated or are still participating  in 24 out of the 43 5G -PPP projects and in 
several 5G-PPP Working Groups. Strong commitment to the 5G-PPP program, exploitation, IPR, communication 
and dissemination of the project’s results is demonstrated by a llocating 23% of the personnel effort to the relevant 
WPs (WP8 & WP9).  
 
The consortium members are complementary in terms of roles and interests, technical, scientific and administrative 
expertise, with little overlap, necessary to perform the development, innovation and validation tasks described in this 
proposal. The size of the consortium is justified by the core competences and expertise of each partner, to achieve 
the goals of the project.
3.4 Resources to be committed 
The allocation of person -month effort amongst the partners is summarised in Table 3.4a, according to their 
responsibilities and the resources estimated for achieving their assigned tasks. The staff effort in each WP is estimated 
based on the complexity of the tasks, complementarity of partner skills, inter -WP relationships and integration 
schedule between WPs. The overall effort of the project is 1291 person-months over the 3-year project period. Please 
refer to Part A (3 – Budget) for the detailed budget per partner.

4.1.1 TELECOM ITALIA SPA 
Short name TIM  
Country Italy 
Type Industrial 
Number of employees 55.000 
Website www.telecomitalia.it  
Short Profile 
The Telecom Italia Group  is a major Italian enterprise and a key European strategic ICT player with an active 
presence all around the world: Europe, United States of America, Africa and Asia.  Driven by technological 
innovation and a commitment to service excellence, the companies of the Group operate in fixed-line and mobile 
telecommunications, Internet & Media, Information Technologies.  
 
Most of the R&D activities of the Group are performed inside the Innovation and R&D Departments of Telecom 
Italia Spa (TIM) involving around 4,500 researchers and technicians with an average investment of 650 M€ per 
year. The Innovation department ensures the supervision of technological innovation for the Group, scouting for 
new technologies and engineering operations for services and network platforms.  The work carried out by the 
Innovation Department is the outcome of a strategic partnership with the main manufacturers of 
telecommunications equipment and systems, and with centres of excellence in research at the most highly qualified 
national and international academic institutions.  
 
On the international level, TIM has pledged a substantial commitment to the task of standardisation and has been 
involved from the beginning in the European Union Framework Programmes starting with the first pilot projects 
of the ESPRIT programme in 1983 and continuing as one of the primary European collaborators in terms of both 
finance and the number of projects. In Horizon 2020 and FP7, TIM is at present involved in more than 40 Projects 
and has so far participated in more than 90 projects.  
 
TIM is currently involved in the experimental evaluation of 5G technologies in Italy, as well as in the definition 
of the standards in 3GPP and ITU -R. TIM is a member of both 3GPP and ITU. TIM is also a member of ETSI, 
one of the only three bodies officially recognised by the EU as a European Standards Organisation (ESO). In 
addition, TIM participates in NGMN Alliance aiming to expand the communications experience by providing a 
truly integrated and cohesively managed delivery platform that brings affordable mobile broadband services to the 
end user with a particular focus on 5G while accelerating the development of LTE-Advanced and its ecosystem. 
 
The coordination of the project 5G-SOLUTIONS represents for TIM a clear opportunity for the investigation in 
a real and multi-national environment of the feasibility of the 5G use cases with a particular focus on the integration 
of verticals needs and interests. The results and learnings gained through the participation and coordination of the 
project will be of absolute relevance once transferred to the internal TIM business departments, and moreover the 
interaction of the project activities with the “Torino 5G” environment will represent a highly relevant synergy. 
 
TIM is leading the initiative “Torino 5G” to test and validate sel ected 5G use cases in the city of Turin, where 
TIM has its “Innovation” department, previously known as CSELT (TIMLab). The Innovation department has 
produced hundreds of patents and publications on the telecommunications related topics in recent years, standing 
at the forefront of research and actively contributing to standardisation in 3GPP and ITU-R. 
 
TIM is also involved in the 5G trials supported by the Italian Ministry of Economic Development with a specific 
consortium of partners. Moreover, TIM is leading an experimental trial in San Marino, the first covering an entire 
nation. 
Role in the project 
TIM will coordinate the 5G-SOLUTIONS project given their wide expertise and experience in developing mobile 
networks including 5G facilities and its proven project management track record in the Horizon 2020 programme.  
TIM is the coordinator of 5G -EVE project (5G-PPP Phase 3) , and in 5G -SOLUTIONS TIM is committed to 
provide, upgrade and support their 5G-EVE Turin facility to the latest 3GPP releases, fully aligned to the 5G-PPP 
and 5G-SOLUTIONS roadmap, during and after the completion of their ICT-17 project and until the completion 
of 5G-SOLUTIONS. This will enable the validation of the Smart Energy vertical use cases to the latest available 
5G 3GPP releases in order to ensure that the latest features will be supported before actual widespread 5G

deployments in Europe. During 5G-SOLUTIONS, TIM will investigate (in a real and multi-national environment) 
the feasibility of the 5G trials with a particular focus on the integration of verticals needs and interests. TIM will 
use the results from 5G SOLUTIONS to consolidate the achievements in the 5G experimental acti vities at

TIM considers the cooperation in 5G-SOLUTIONS with the most significant players in the sector gathered in the 
consortium, a viable opportunity to trigger broad European-wide 5G adoption. The inclusio n of 5 key verticals 
and the evaluation of their needs is of paramount importance for the business development direction of TIM in the 
future evolution of the telecommunications market. The network slicing and the orchestration of the slices among 
different network segments is relevant from a technical point of view, as well as the consolidation of the KPIs and 
the related performance ensured by 5G future deployments. These changes need to be thoroughly validated and 
5G-SOLUTIONS fully answers these needs. 
 
TIM will also have an active participation in standardisation fora to disseminate 5G-SOLUTIONS’ results.

Relevant Projects 
1. 5G-EVE [5G-PPP Phase 3]: ‘5G European Validation platform for Extensive trials’. 5G-EVE aims to create 
the foundations for a pervasive roll -out of end -to-end 5G networks in Europe. The project supports this 
fundamental transition by offering to vertical industries and to all 5G-PPP Phase3 projects facilities to validate 
their network KPIs and their services. A2T is designing and developing a testing environment to perform 5G 
experimentations in a real 5G facility to ease the development of e-mobility and smart mobility applications. 
https://www.5g-eve.eu/.    
2. 5G-MoNArch [5G-PPP Phase 2 ]: ‘5G Mobile Network Architecture for diverse services, use cases, and 
applications in 5G and beyond’ which is about the experimental evaluation of the 5G end to end architecture 
in two selected testbed, one of them in Turin coordinated by TIM. (01/07/2017 – 30/06/2019).  
3. Flex5Gware [5G-PPP Phase 1]: ‘Flexible and efficient hardware/software platforms for 5G network elements 
and devices’ aims to deliver a software platform' - considering increased capacity, reduced energy footprint, 
as well as scalability and modularity - to enable a smooth transition from 4G mobile wireless systems to 5G. 
(01/04/2015 – 30/06/2017). https://flex5gware.eu/.  
4. 5G-Crosshaul [5G-PPP Phase 1]: ‘The 5G Integrated fronthaul/backhaul’ aims at developing a 5G integrated 
backhaul and fronthaul transport network enabling a flexible and software -defined reconfiguration of all 
networking elements. (01/07/2015 – 31/12/2017). http://5g-crosshaul.eu/.  
5. 5G-ENSURE [5G-PPP Phase 1]:  ‘5G Enablers for Network and System Security and Resilience ’. 5G-
ENSURE aim was to deliver a 5G Security Architecture, shared and agreed by the various 5G stakeholde rs. 
(01/11/2015 – 31/10/2017) http://www.5gensure.eu/.

4.1.2 ALCATEL-LUCENT ISRAEL LTD 
Short name NOKIA 
 
Country Israel 
Type Industrial 
Number of employees ~80 (Cloudband group, Israel), 102.761 worldwide

Short Profile 
NOKIA is a global leader in technologies connecting people and things. Powered by the innovation of Nokia Bell 
Labs and Nokia Technologies, the company is at the forefront of creating and licensing the technologies that are 
increasingly at the heart of our  connected lives. With a state -of-the-art software, hardware and services for any 
type of network, NOKIA is uniquely positioned to help communication service providers, governments, and large 
enterprises deliver on the promise of 5G, the Cloud and the Internet of Things.  
 
Alcatel-Lucent Israel Ltd (NOKIA), is composed of two separate research and development groups, namely, 
CloudBand Business Unit and Bell-Labs Israel.  
 
CloudBand, a pioneer in the Network Functions Virtualisation (NFV) industry, coined the term “Virtual Telco” 
over 5 years ago and developed a ground -breaking, market-ready, Telco-grade end-to-end NFV solution that is 
inherently built for carrier applications. With CloudBand, operators can quickly deploy a proven NFV solution 
that enables them to leverage the cloud to work faster and more cost effectively. The CloudBand portfolio makes 
it simple to host, orchestrate, automate, and manage virtualised network functions (VNFs) and services. Its scalable 
and flexible line of products optimises and automates network operations to create a lean environment that helps 
reduce time to revenue for new services. The recently optimised CloudBand portfolio includes CloudBand 
Infrastructure Software (NFVI & VIM), CloudBand Application Manager (VNFM ), and CloudBand Network 
Director (NFVO) – for an ultimate fit to the ETSI NFV Management and Orchestration (MANO) framework. This 
reduces complexity and ensures applicability to single and multi-vendor infrastructures. 
 
The Bell Labs team is largely dedicated to NOKIA’s CloudBand solution. The local Bell Labs team contribute to 
CloudBand’s efforts by leading the research in the field of cloud software foundations and NFV cognitive cloud 
management, devising a new dev -ops paradigm optimised for the Telecom industry, also exploring its security 
aspects. Powered by the innovation of Bell Labs and CloudBand technology, NOKIA is leading the research and 
development in the NFV domain in Europe. Indeed, it is participating in three 5G -PPP Phase 1 projects and 1 
phase 2 project, namely, Superfluidity, SONATA, and CogNet in phase 1 and NGPaaS in phase 2. The Israeli 
team is fully dedicated in innovation paving the path to 5G. 
Role in the project 
NOKIA will provide and extend the functionality of their Cloudband Director to develop the cross domain service 
orchestrator in 5G -SOLUTIONS, so as  to be able to  bind all use cases across different 5G facilities, and in 
particular, the 5G-EVE Turin and 5G -VINNI Norway and Patra facilities. Also, NOKIA will contribute in 5G-
SOLUTIONS through network slicing and Zero Touch Configuration capabilities. 
 
NOKIA will lead WP2 ‘5G Infrastructure setup and operational readiness ’, contributing in the design and 
development of  the necessary plugins in an existing Cross -Domain Service Orchestrator (CDSO - NOKIA’s 
CloudBand Network Director), so as to act as an umbrella orchestrator to enable automatic, unified, concurrent 
service provisioning, management and cross -domain orchestration across the ICT -17 facilities.  In addition, 
NOKIA will lead the following tasks: 
• T2.2 CDSO plugins design & development for cross-domain orchestration 
• T2.3 Integration of CDSO plugins with the 5G ICT-17 facilities

Relevant Projects 
1. NGPaaS [5G-PPP Phase 2]: ‘Next Generation Platform as a Service’ . The purpose of the project is to b uild 
Telco-grade PaaS: to support different configurations and a large set of deployment options. NOKIA is a Work 
Package leader in NGPaaS. (01/06/2017 – 31/05/2019). 
2. CogNet [5G-PPP Phase 1 ]: ‘Building an Intelligent System of Insights and Action for 5G Network 
Management’. NOKIA has implemented a Machine Learning based solution for the placement of resources in 
the datacentre. NOKIA also initiates and leads the Noisy Neighbor scenar io and demo. It set s up a demo 
platform based on Cloudband and generated data for detection of the Noisy Neighbor phenomena using 
Machine Learning algorithms (01/07/2015 – 31/12/2017) http://www.cognet.5g-ppp.eu/. 
3. SONATA [5G-PPP Phase 1]: ‘Service Programming and Orchestration for Virtualized Software Networks ’ 
is developing a NFV framework that provides a programming model and development toolchain for virtualised 
services, fully integrated with a DevOps -enabled service platform and orchestration s ystem. CloudBand is 
highly involved in the project, taking part in all work packages and leads several Tasks.  (01/07/2015 – 
31/12/2017) http://sonata-nfv.eu/. 
4. SUPERFLUIDITY [5G-PPP Phase 1]: ‘Superfluidity: a super-fluid, cloud-native, converged edge system’. 
In physics, Superfluidity is a state in which a matter behaves like a fluid with zero viscosity. This project aims 
at achieving Superfluidity in the Internet: the ability to instantiate services on -the-fly, run them anywhere in 
the network (core, aggregation, edge) and shift them transparently to different locations. NOKIA’s CloudBand 
served as the technical manager for the first year of Superfluidity, and led the architectural work package. In 
addition to that, CloudBand collaborated on all other work packages, particularly with respect to orchestration. 
Finally, CloudBand VNFM solution was leveraged to demonstrate dynamic scaling and migration of a video 
distribution solution provided by Unified Streaming based on a modeling developed by Intel in collaboration 
with Citrix, ONAPP and NOKIA.(01/07/2015 – 31/03/2018) http://superfluidity.eu/.

CloudBand Network Director – to fit the key NFV management and orchestration (MANO).

patients suffering from Heart Failure (HF), towards developing a multi-stakeholder patient centered mHealth 
ecosystem. HEARTEN approaches the problem of medication non-adherence and treatment non-compliance 
of HF patients by challenging specific scientific and technological objectives. HEARTEN will design, develop 
and validate an ICT co-operative environment that will enable the HF patients to achieve sustainable behavior 
change regarding their drug adherence and compliance. At the same time, HEARTEN will motivate and 
empower the ecosystem actors (doctors, caregivers, nutritionists, physical activity expert, psychologist) to be 
further engaged to HF patients’ routine improving HF management. The target is to create an ecosystem that 
will empower collaboration among its actors gathering valuable information and analysing it in favour of the 
patient, enhancing patients’ health status. The idea is to utilise biosensors and sensors that will reflect the 
health status of the patient and will identify whether the patient adheres to the administered drugs. Concerning 
biosensors, the breath biosensor will be integ rated into the smartphone while the saliva biosensor will be 
integrated into the patient’s cup. Additional, commercially available sensors will be used for monitoring the 
ECG, the blood pressure, physical activity and temperature constituting the sensor kit of the patient. The input 
data are complemented with nutrition information from the patient’s smartphone, weight monitoring through 
wireless weight scales as well as the patient’s profile and information directly added by the patient himself, 
the caregivers, and the healthcare professionals. The multi-parametric data are transmitted to the HEARTEN 
cloud architecture, where a knowledge management system analyses them and delivers critical information at 
hand. 
Significant Infrastructure 
APPART has designed, developed and implemented its own Analytics and Reporting Application Platform, named 
Cortex, which handles a significant number of data volumes and size, covering a wide range of commercial and 
technical business needs: 
• AppArt Cortex Analytics Platform for Network Performance Monitoring: APPART has implemented a 
large number of KPIs for various Operator’ s systems such as VAS (MSP), Core (Transit, SGSN, NGIN, 
CSCF, SBC, NGME etc.), Transmission and Radio (4G) network. The friendly and easy-to-use Graphical 
User Interface designed by APPART allows its users to have full visibility to KPIs measurements and reports 
and thus have quickly the necessary information on their hands in order to take important business decisions.  
• AppArt Cortex Platform for Customer Experience Analytics: APPART has implemented its own Cortex 
Analytics Platform for the presentation and the overall satisfaction of business customers, based on specific – 
configurable – KPIs. The platform provides to Operator’s Corporate Marketing, the ability to have access to 
aggregated and valuable KPIs measuring the customer satisfaction e.g. detailed call analysis etc. Cortex 
solution manages various data in such a way so that useful results are produced quickly and in one place. By 
accessing the application, the user gains at a glance visibility and understanding of the customer’s experience 
allowing him/her to take any relevant actions. In case the user wishes to receive further analysis, he / she may 
have access to further information by choosing the relevant parameters.

resource systems. To achieve this, the application is built using a highly modular design, which allows

o Customer Segmentation – that is used to build subscribers’ profile based on usage patterns and other

customer information from Operator’s network (i.e. tariff plan, active subscriptions, passport etc.) and

level.

easily react to customer events in near real time (i.e. a top-up, low credit, change in spending patterns, 
change in usage patterns etc.). Cortex Campaigns Management platform allows effective creation of 
Event-driven marketing (EDM) - a new discipline w ithin marketing, where commercial and 
communication activities are based upon the measurement of relevant and identifiable changes in a 
customer's individual needs. It is a new and highly successful approach to direct marketing and 
traditional Database and  Segmentation only marketing, which typically use statistical methods and 
analysis. 
o Communication Channels - The campaign is channel agnostic allowing effective communication. 
However, the campaign also allows for configuration of separating channels (i.e. make an offer only 
available through SMS or mobile app, IVR etc.). 
o Analytics Reporting Tool  – An essentia l tool used to track responsiveness towards every single 
campaign. Reporting tool works in real -time and post processing mode, creating all the necessary 
charts for the marketer to decide how to handle every single customer.  
o Innovative campaigns concepts – A plethora of campaign types such as Regional Target Campaigns, 
Campaigns through Shops, Welcome, Data, Social Media, Digital Campaigns. 
o Powerful algorithms effectively minimising churn rates and customer turnover and allowing for 
creation of proactive campaigns.  
o Highly modular solution in terms of functionality and integration with Operator’s network

Short Profile 
The Centre Tecnològic de Telecomunicacions de Catalunya (CTTC), located in Castelldefels (Barcelona), is a 
private non-profit R&D center with substantial funding support from the autonomous government of Catalonia 
(Generalitat de Catalunya) along with research and development part nership with industry. So far, four distinct 
research divisions have been identified in the Research Unit: Communication Networks, Communication 
Subsystems, Communication Technologies and Geomatics. CTTC has contributed to more than 300 international 
journals and more than 600 international conferences. In addition, CTTC has currently submitted 17 patent 
applications and, among them, 9 have already been internationally patented and 1 has been awarded. 
The SMARTECH Department, part of the Communications Technologies Division (CTD), is led by Dr.Christos 
Verikoukis and involves research activities, both fundamental and experimental, focusing on technologies related 
to WSNs, WLANs and dense cellular networks. In particular, SMARTECH aims to provide advanced PHY layer 
solutions, cooperative network coding-assisted protocols, cognitive aware radio resource management schemes, 
network management protocols and power demand algorithms in order to improve the energy efficiency of the 
wireless technologies. Experimenta l activities include the development of a flexible platform for smart 
environments and a flexible tool for implementing advanced resource allocation schemes.

actuation and semi-autonomic behaviour in IoT/IIoT applications. The SEMIoTICS framework will support 
cross-layer intelligent dynamic adaptation, including heterogeneous smart objects, networks and c louds. To

establishing fully connected pilot lines in More than Moore (MtM) technologies. The new pilot lines will form 
a network with existing specialised R&D and manufacturing lines to work as a European modular solution 
system. In particular the segment of sensor technologies and MEMS, which pl ays a key role in solving the 
grand societal challenges, related to Smart Mobility, Society, Energy, Health and Production will be addressed.

secure smart grid ’. CONNECT will develop solutions for high interoperable, high data rate local and wide 
area communication in the power grid with enhanced security in order to protect this critical infrastructure 
against attacks. Particular e ffort is spen t to minimize the power consumption of the developed solutions.  
(1/4/2017-31/3/2020). 
4. 5GSTEP FWD [EU]: ‘5G System Technological Enhancements Provided by Fiber Wireless Deployments ’. 
5G STEP FWD will define the overall 5G network architecture, in both optical and wireless domains, by 
taking into account cross -layer and cross -system design requirements, while the UDWDM PON as the 
backhaul of mmWave cellular networks will be proposed as candidate solution for 5G networks.  (1/6/2017-
31/5/2021). 
Significant IT Infrastructure 
IoTWORLD® is the IoT part of the 5G platform that will be used in Barcelona. It is an End-to-End testbed for the 
Internet of Things (IoT). The main focus is on Wireless Communications systems and data analytics. IoTWORLD® 
is a unique testbed for the IoT. It features: 
• Scalable design 
• End-user involvement 
• Integration with 5G technologies 
• Heterogeneity of wireless technologies 
• Traffic shaping using SDN 
This proposal version was submitted by Frini LAZAROU on 14/11/2018 13:54:55 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
 
G                                                                                                                                                   Page 117 
 
 
The most relevant capabilities of the testbed: 
• Applied research . IoTWORLD ® testbed facilitates experimental research  in the area of wireless 
communications and data analytics. IoTWORLD ® has been used to demonstrate the potential of the 
Distributed Queuing (DQ) technology. 
• Heterogeneous implementations. It allows several technologies to coexist and cooperate to achieve a 
common goal. 
• Commercial solutions integration . Thanks to its flexibility, IoTWORLD ® also allows the easy 
integration of off-the-shelf technologies. 
The architecture of the IoTWORLD ® testbed is the following. It relies on a 5 -tier architecture. Se nsors and 
actuators (IoT Device tier) are connected to a set of gateways (Gateway tier), either with a direct connection or via 
multiple hops. These gateways collect the data from the sensors and send it to the Edge Cluster tier where another 
set of more p owerful nodes process it. The Edge tier provides the testbed with Fog computing capabilities. For 
instance, reduce the congestion of the Core tier and the underlying nets, provide services with ultra -low latency, 
manage the different use cases that run over IoTWORLD® and incorporate flexibility and intelligence in the edge 
of the network. The Edge Cluster tier nodes are then connected to the Internet providing the capability to retrieve 
and store data in the Cloud (Core tier). Flexibility in the management of the edge net resources is provided through 
a Software Defined Network (SDN). This is complemented with Network Function Virtualization (NFV) to 
virtualize network services and hardware, thereby providing a more efficient use of net resources. Finally, the data 
gathered by the sensors is stored in the Cloud which can be accessed from a web interface or a smartphone 
application (User tier). 
This proposal version was submitted by Frini LAZAROU on 14/11/2018 13:54:55 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
 
G                                                                                                                                                   Page 118 
 
IoTWORLD® permits to obtain valuable information from the data measurements by means of data analytics on 
the edge. For this purpose, Software -Defined Networking (SDN) is a key enabler to realize a flexible 
communication between the different computing entities. By leveraging the ability to gather network -wide 
information at a centralized SDN controller, IoTWORLD ®’s Gateway tier adapts the forwarding path according 
to each flow’s predefined requirements. This opens the door to context -aware forwarding strategies, revealing 
different network resources according to the type of 
flow and current network conditions. 
IoTWORLD® constitutes a fundamental part of the 
unique End -to-End 5G experimental platform 
available at CTTC. IoTWORLD® can be connected to 
other demonstrators devoted to the physical layer, 
optical networks, and wireless backhauling. Together, 
end-to-end research can be conducted towards a 
holistic definition and exploration of 5G technologies. 
IoTWORLD® can be used to demonstrate any use 
case. For instance: 
• Indoor air quality and gas monitoring 
• Smart energy grids: Distribution Automation 
(DA) and smart HVAC control 
• eHealth: Heart rate and oxygen saturation 
monitoring 
• Smart parking: presence detection 
• Water and waste management 
• Smart lighting 
• Intrusion detection systems 
• Remote robot control

Cyberethics Lab Srls (CEL) is a start -up Italian SME leveraging on the experience and knowledge of its

principles and the current legal framework.  CEL has formul ated its own methodology on ethical, political and

Short Profile 
ENEL X SRL (ENEL) is a global business company in Rome, Italy leading the transformation of the energy sector. 
Shifting the paradigm, ENEL helps customers use technology to transform energy into new opportunities, so they
